The question is whether, in addition to the contents, the Men of the Great Assembly only determined the “seals” (following the Babli) or also the introductory sentences (following this Yerushalmi, but incompatible with the poetic versions of the daily prayers known from Yerushalmi sources from the Cairo Genizah).</i>. Rebbi Aḥa said, all benedictions in the kind of their seals<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">The language is difficult. R. Eleazar Askari in his Commentary to <i>Berakhot</i> explains that Rebbi Aḥa insists that only the “seal” counts and, therefore, the text preceding the “seal” is unimportant; the text of the seal cannot be a verse. R. Shelomo Cirillo and R. Moshe ben Ḥabib in their Commentaries to <i>Berakhot</i> explain, on the contrary, that the seal must fit the text of the benediction just preceding and that this text cannot be a verse. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 104a" href="/Pesachim.104a">Babli (<i>Pesaḥim</i> 104a</a>) this principle is spelled out only for Havdalah.</i>. But those who say: <i>Jubilate and sing, inhabitant of Zion, for great is in your midst the Holy One of Israel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 12:6" href="/Isaiah.12.6"><i>Is</i>. 12:6</a>.</i> do not violate the rule that no benediction is a verse<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">Ezra Fleischer (Tarbiz 41, p. 450) has published a Yerushalmi prayer text from the Cairo Genizah which uses this verse in the third benediction of the `Amidah. From what is left of the original Galilean practice it seems clear that the standard text of longer benedictions always ended with a Biblical verse just preceding the “seal”. The text here states that the only acceptable place for a Biblical verse is before the “seal“. Since the Mishnah prescribes benedictions on fast days whose text is a Biblical verse, what is prohibited is using a verse in the final doxology.</i>.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the first he says<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">The first additional benediction (either the text of <i>Shofarot</i> without its doxology or the text from <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 8" href="/I_Kings.8"><i>1K</i>. 8</a>) is followed by the text of the Mishnah, to be answered with “Amen” by the congregation.</i>: “He Who answered our forefather Abraham on Mount Moriah, He may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Redeemer of Israel.”
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <i>Gen. rabba</i>56(15), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Vayikra Rabbah 29:8" href="/Vayikra_Rabbah.29.8"><i>Lev</i>. <i>rabba</i>29(8</a>), <i>Midrash Ps</i>. 29[1].</i> But was not Isaac redeemed<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">Since Mt. Moriah is invoked, it was Isaac who was in danger, not Abraham.</i>? Since Isaac was redeemed it is as if all of Israel was redeemed. Rebbi Bevai Abba<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">In G: The Elder R. Bevai.</i> in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Abraham said before the Holy One, praise to Him: Master of the worlds, it is open and known before You that when You said to me to sacrifice my son Isaac I could have answered and said before You, yesterday You said to me, <i>for in Isaac will your descendants be named</i><sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 21:12" href="/Genesis.21.12"><i>Gen</i>. 21:12</a>.</i>, and now You are saying, <i>sacrifice him as elevation offering</i><sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 22:2" href="/Genesis.22.2"><i>Gen</i>. 22:2</a>.</i>. Heaven forbid that I should have done this, to the contrary I suppressed my inclination and did Your will. So may it be Your pleasure, Eternal, my God, that when my son Isaac’s descendants will be in trouble and nobody will speak in their defense<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">Greek συνηγορία.</i>, that You will speak in their defense. <i>The Eternal will see</i><sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 22:14" href="/Genesis.22.14"><i>Gen</i>. 22:14</a>.</i>. You will remember for them the binding of Isaac and be filled with mercy for them. What is written afterwards? <i>Abraham lifted his eyes and saw a ram, after</i><sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 22:13" href="/Genesis.22.13"><i>Gen</i>. 22:13</a>.</i>, etc. What means “after”? Rebbi Judah ben Rebbi Simon<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">In G: R. Yudan bar Shalom said, the Holy One, praise to Him, said to Abraham: Abraham, after …</i> said, after all generations in the future your sons will be gripped by sins and involved in troubles but at the end they will be redeemed by the horns of this ram, [as it is said]<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">In G: This what is written.</i>, <i>and the Eternal, God, will blow the horn and go in Southern storms</i><sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 9:14" href="/Zechariah.9.14"><i>Zach</i>. 9:14</a>.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <i>Lev. rabba</i>56(14).</i> Rebbi Ḥuna in the name of Rebbi Ḥinena bar Isaac. This entire day Abraham saw the ram being caught at one tree but freed and leaving, caught in that thicket but freed and leaving, caught in this underbrush but freed and leaving. The Holy One, praise to Him, said to him, Abraham. So in the future will your descendants be caught in sins and become entangled with governments: From Babylon to Media<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">The Persian Empire.</i>, from Media to Greece<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">Alexander’s Empire and its successors.</i>, from Greece to Edom<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">The Roman Empire.</i>. He said before Him: Master of the worlds, [will this be] so forever? He said to him, at the end they will be redeemed by the horns of this ram: <i>and the Eternal, God, will blow the horn and go in Southern storms</i><sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 9:14" href="/Zechariah.9.14"><i>Zach</i>. 9:14</a>.</i>.<br>Text of G (Genizah):<sup class="footnote-marker">145a</sup><i class="footnote">אָמַר ר' חֲנַנְיָה בְרְבִּי יִצְחָק. כָּל־אוֹתוֹ הַיוֹם הָיָה אָבִינוּ אַבְרָהָם רוֹאֶה אֶת הָאַיִל נֶאֱחַז בַּסְבַךְ הַזֶּה וְנִיתוֹר וְיוֹצֵא מִסְתַּבֵּךְ בַּחוֹרֶשׁ הַזֶּה וְנִיתוֹר וְיוֹצֵא. אָמַר לוֹ הַקָּדוֹשׁ בָּרוּךְ הוּא. אַבְרָהָם. כָּךְ עֲתִידִין בָנִיךְ נֶאֱחָזִים וּמִסְתָּבְּכִים בַּמַּלְכִיוֹת. אָמַר לְפָנָיו אני"ו. רִבּוֹן הָעוֹלָמִים. וְכֵן לְעוֹלָם. אָמַר לֵיהּ לֹא. וְסוֹפָן לִיגָאֵל בְּקַרְנָיו שֶׁלְאַיִל הַזֶּה, הָדָה הִיא דִכְתִיב וַיי עֲלֵיהֶם יֵרָאֶה.</i><br>Rebbi Hanania ben Rebbi Isaac said: This entire day our father Abraham saw the ram being caught in this underbrush but freed and leaving, caught in this thicket but freed and leaving. The Holy One, praise to Him, said to Abraham: Abraham, so in the future your descendants will be caught and entangled with governments. Abraham our forefather said to him, Master of the worlds, will this go on forever? He said to him, no. At the end they will be redeemed by the horns of this ram. This is what is written, The Eternal will appear over them<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 9:14" href="/Zechariah.9.14"><i>Zach</i>. 9:14</a>.</i>

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the second he says<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The second additional benediction, with doxology appropriate for a recitation of <i>Zikhronot</i>.</i>: “He Who answered our forefathers on the Reed Sea, He may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Who remembers the forgotten.<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">Since Israel was like forgotten during the time of servitude in Egypt.</i>”
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael Bešallaḥ</i>(ed. Horovitz-Rabin p. 96); <i>dR. Simeon ben Ioḥai</i>14:13 (ed. Epstein-Melamed p. 56). <i>Targum Pseudo-Jonathan</i> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:13" href="/Exodus.14.13"><i>Fragmentary Targum Ex</i>. 14:13</a>.</i> Our forefathers formed four factions on the Sea. One said, let us fall into the Sea. And another said, let us return to Egypt. And another said, let us fight with them. And another said, let us shout against them. To the one who said, let us fall into the Sea, Moses said, <i>stay firm and see the help of the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:13" href="/Exodus.14.13"><i>Ex</i>. 14:13</a>.</i>, etc. And to the one who said, let us return to Egypt, Moses said, <i>for as you are seeing Egypt today</i><sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:13" href="/Exodus.14.13"><i>Ex</i>. 14:13</a>.</i>, etc. And to the one who said, l let us fight with them, Moses said, <i>the Eternal will fight for you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:14" href="/Exodus.14.14"><i>Ex</i>. 14:14</a>.</i>. And to the one who said, let us shout against them, Moses said, <i>and you be silent</i><sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:14" href="/Exodus.14.14"><i>Ex</i>. 14:14</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the third he says<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The second additional benediction, with doxology appropriate for a recitation of <i>Zikhronot</i>.</i>: “He Who answered Joshua at Gilgal He may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Who hears the sound of the horn.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish in the name of Rebbi Yannai: The Holy One, praise to Him, associated His great Name with Israel. {A parable} of a king who had the small key of a jewelry box<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">Explained as Greek διπλωματάριον.</i>. The king said, if I leave it as it is, it is apt to be lost. Therefore I shall put in on a chain. Then if it were lost the key would prove where it is. So the Holy One, praise to Him, said, if I leave Israel as they are, they would be absorbed by the nations. Therefore I shall associate My great Name with them and they will survive. What is the reason? <i>The Canaanites and all inhabitants of the Land will hear, and encircle us, and eradicate our Name from the Land; then what would You do for Your great Name</i><sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 7:9" href="/Joshua.7.9"><i>Jos</i>. 7:9</a>.</i><i>?</i>[Immediately]<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition, to be deleted.</i>, <i>the Eternal said to Joshua, get up</i><sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 7:10" href="/Joshua.7.10"><i>Jos</i>. 7:10</a>.</i>. Rise for what You mentioned.
The younger Rebbi Yannai in the name of his ancestors: Anybody who is not qualified like Joshua that in case he falls on his face the Eternal, praise to Him, will tell him, “get up”, should not fall down. This applies to a single person {praying for} the community<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph belongs to the rules of prayer. On all days (except those of festive character) after the main <i>Amidah</i> said standing there follows a private penitentiary prayer said first falling down and then sitting up. Since prostration was part of the Temple service, one has to be careful not to imitate the details of Temple prostration. In addition, it is stated here that in contrast to the public Temple service, this prayer has to be private. It is authorized as public ceremony only for a genuine holy man praying for a community in distress. Since it is presumptuous for anybody to declare himself a holy man, the statement has to be read as a general prohibition to make the prostration into a public act. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 22b" href="/Megillah.22b">Babli <i>Megillah</i>22b</a> (in the name of R. Eleazar).</i>.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the fourth he says<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The second additional benediction, with doxology appropriate for a recitation of <i>Zikhronot</i>.</i>: “He Who answered Samuel at Miṣpah may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Who hears vociferation.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 7:6" href="/I_Samuel.7.6"><i>1S</i>. 7:6</a>.</i>: <i>They assembled at Miṣpah, drew water, and poured it out before the Eternal</i>. Did they pour out water? But it teaches that they poured out their heart like water<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">Since water libations are authorized only in the central Sanctuary on Tabernacles, this pouring out cannot refer to a sacral act. The explanation given here is found in <i>Targum Jonathan ad loc</i>., <i>Midrash Sam</i>. 13[1], <i>Midrash Psalms add</i>. 119:77; quoted by Rashi <i>ad loc</i>. This has to be the original meaning of the verse, as noted by S. R. Driver (<i>Notes on the Hebrew Text and the Topography of the Books of Samuel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup>, Oxford 1913) following A. B. Ehrlich, (<i>Randglossen zur Hebräischen Bibel</i>, vol. 3): “LXX add ארצה, perhaps rightly: the water was poured out not as a libation (for which יִסְּכוּ would have been said), but probably as a symbolic act implying a complete separation from sin: sin was to be cast away as water poured out upon the earth (<a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 14:4" href="/II_Samuel.14.4"><i>2S</i>. 14:4</a>).”</i>. <i>(They said there)</i>[Samuel said] <i>we sinned before the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">The (scribe’s text) is the MT; [the corrector’s] is unsupported.</i>. Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac said, Samuel wore the robe of all of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">The verse does not mention any prayer of Samuel at this occasion; one has to explain why the Mishnah refers to Samuel and not the entire people. Wearing the robe of all of Israel means arguing for all of Israel.</i>. He said before Him: Master of the worlds, do You not judge a person only if he says before You, “I did not sin”? <i>I shall sit in judgment over you because you said, I did not sin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 2:35" href="/Jeremiah.2.35"><i>Jer</i>. 2:35</a>.</i>. But those said before You “we sinned”.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the fifth he says<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The second additional benediction, with doxology appropriate for a recitation of <i>Zikhronot</i>.</i>: “He Who answered Elijah on Mount Carmel may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Who hears prayer.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 18:36" href="/I_Kings.18.36"><i>1K</i>. 18:36</a>.</i>: <i>At the approach of the afternoon sacrifice, Elijah the prophet stepped up and said, Eternal, God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel, today may it be known</i>&lt;<i>that You are God in Israel and I am Your servant</i>.&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">Added from G.</i> And Elijah sacrifices when local altars are forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Temple was already built, all other altars became illegitimate. This doctrine was certainly held by the author of the books of Kings who nevertheless reports favorably on Elijah’s action in repairing an abandoned High Place dedicated to the Eternal.</i>? Rebbi Simlai said, the Word He said to him<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">One must assume that he acted on direct Divine command.</i>: <i>I acted on Your saying</i>. I acted following Your Word. <i>Answer me, Eternal, Answer me</i><sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 18:37" href="/I_Kings.18.37"><i>1K</i>. 18:37</a>. Why a double invocation?</i>. Answer me for my merit, answer me for the merit of my student &lt;the students.&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">The reading of G, “students”, is preferable since the singular would have to refer to Elisha who at that moment was not Elijah’s student.</i>

Halakhah 9

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the sixth he says<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The second additional benediction, with doxology appropriate for a recitation of <i>Zikhronot</i>.</i>: “He Who answered Jonah in the belly of the fish may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Who answers in time of trouble.<br>On the seventh he says<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The second additional benediction, with doxology appropriate for a recitation of <i>Zikhronot</i>.</i>: “He Who answered David and Solomon in Jerusalem may answer you and hear your vociferation today. Praise to You, Eternal, Who shows mercy on the Land.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jonah 2:3" href="/Jonah.2.3"><i>Jon</i>. 2:3</a>. The verse referred to in the Mishnah.</i>: <i>He said, I called on the Eternal in my trouble and he answered me</i>. Would not David and Solomon have to precede Elijah and Jonah<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">Since the next Mishnah refers to David and Solomon, the sequence Abraham, Exodus, Joshua, Samuel, Elijah, Jonah, David and Solomon, is not chronological.</i>? Only to conclude with “Who shows mercy for the Land.”
On the seventh? In the name of Symmachos they said, “praise to Him who humiliates the haughty.<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">Since there are only six additional benedictions, what is the seventh? The answer is given in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 1:10" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).1.10">Tosephta 1:10</a> which here is quoted only in part: “The seventh, Symmachos they said, “praise to Him who humiliates the haughty,” <u>this is the benediction about sectarians</u>; i. e., a modified conclusion of one of the permanent benedictions; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 2:2:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.2.2.5">Note 95</a>. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 16b" href="/Taanit.16b">Babli 16b</a> the modified daily benediction is the seventh, the prayer for redemption.</i>” One understands Solomon as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 8:3" href="/I_Kings.8.3"><i>1K</i>. 8:3</a>.</i>: <i>I was able to build a dwelling house for You</i>; why David? Rebbi Abbahu said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 4:2" href="/Psalms.4.2"><i>Ps</i>. 4:2</a>.</i>: <i>When I am calling, answer me, my true God; in straights You widened for me</i>. David said before the Holy One, praise to Him: Master of the worlds, in any straights which I was entering into<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">Any trouble which he caused for himself, as the affair of Batseba and the census against which he was warned. The census resulted in David’s buying of the Temple Mount, Arawna’s threshing floor, as building plot for the Temple.</i> You widened for me. I entered the straights of Bat-Sheva and You gave me Solomon. I entered the troubles of Israel and You gave me the Temple. <sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">Added from G.</i>&lt;this is what is written <sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 22:1" href="/I_Chronicles.22.1">1Chr. 22:1</a>.</i>: <i>David said, this is the Temple and this is the altar for Israel’s elevation offerings</i>.&gt;

Halakhah 10

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> It happened in the days of Rebbi Ḥalafta and Rebbi Ḥanania ben Teradion that somebody stood before the Ark<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">The reader in the synagogue service</i> and finished the entire benediction and they answered after him Amen<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">This also is the text of Maimonides’s autograph Mishnah. In the Babli one reads: They did not answer Amen.</i>. “Blow, Cohanim”, they blew. “He Who answered our forefather Abraham on Mount Moriah, He may answer you and hear your vociferation today.” “Treble, Cohanim”, they trebled. “He Who answered our forefathers on the Reed Sea, He may answer you and hear your vociferation today.” When the case came before the Sages they said, this we only used to do at the Eastern gate<sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli one reads: At the Eastern gate on the Temple Mount. Maimonides reads: At the Eastern gates, and he explains that there were synagogue services both at the Eastern entrance to the Temple and the Eastern entrance to the Temple Mount.<br>The way it is described in the Yerushalmi Mishnah, the procedure was a hybrid between regular synagogue service, where every benediction by the reader is answered by “Amen”, and Temple service where “Amen” never was used, and the Temple service where Cohanim blew trumpets and horns in straight or modulated sounds to accompany every public action. (According to the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 16b" href="/Taanit.16b">Babli 16b</a> the order to the Cohanim was given not by the reader but by the beadle.) The objecting Sages decided that proceedings used only on the Temple Mount never should be imitated at other places.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated: “One does not answer ‘Amen’ in the Temple. What did they say? ‘Praised be the glory of His Kingdom forever and ever.’ And from where that one does not answer ‘Amen’ in the Temple? The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 9:5" href="/Nehemiah.9.5"><i>Neh</i>. 9:5</a>.</i>, <i>Arise, praise the Eternal, your God, forever and ever</i>. From where for every single benediction? The verse says, <i>and exalted over all praise and glory</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 1:11" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).1.11">Tosephta 1:11</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 16b" href="/Taanit.16b">Babli 16b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 63a" href="/Berakhot.63a"><i>Berakhot</i> 63a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 40b" href="/Sotah.40b"><i>Soṭa</i>40b</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 9:5:15" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.9.5.15">Yerushalmi <i>Berakhot</i>9:7 (Notes 278–280</a>).</i>”

Halakhah 11

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the first three fast days, the people of the watch<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">The priests were divided into 24 “watches”, <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 24" href="/I_Chronicles.24"><i>1Chr</i>. 24</a>. Each “watch” was serving in the Temple for one week, from the <i>musaf</i> sacrifice of the Sabbath to the morning sacrifice of the following Sabbath.</i> fast but do not finish, but the people of the clan<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">The watch was divided into seven clans; each of the clans was serving for one day of the week. However, if the members of the clan were too few to complete all required service, they could ask other members of the watch to come and help. Therefore the members of the clan whose day of work is the fast day cannot be ask to finish a fast since rabbinic fast days may not impinge on the biblically ordained Temple service. The remaining members of the watch who are on stand-by may be asked to fast as long as they are not called up for actual duty.</i> do not fast. On the second three the people of the watch fast and finish, but the people of the clan fast and did not finish. On the last seven both fast and finish, the words of Rebbi Joshua. But the Sages say, on the first three fast days neither of them did fast. On the second three the people of the watch fast but do not finish, but the people of the clan do not fast. On the last seven the people of the watch fast and finish, but the people of the clan fast and do not finish.<br>The people of the watch are permitted to drink wine during nights but not during days<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">Priests on duty are forbidden wine and any intoxicating drink, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:8-11" href="/Leviticus.10.8-11"><i>Lev</i>. 10:8–11</a>. The priests on stand-by may drink in the evening since by morning the effects of the wine will have disappeared. The members of the clan who during the night also are occupied in Temple service, either on watch or to dispose of the remainders of the sacrifices of the previous day, may not drink alcohol during the entire period of their actual duty. Obviously this Mishnah spells out rules for the entire year, independent of fast days.</i>. The people of the clan neither by day nor by night. The people of the watch and those of the bystanders<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">The Non-priests standing by at the time of offering of the public sacrifices as representatives of this public (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.2.1">Mishnah 4:2</a>). In practice these are delegates of the district from which the watch serving during the week was drawn. They are forced to appear for duty in clean garments and well groomed by being forbidden these activities during their week of duty.</i> are forbidden to shave and to wash their garments, but on Thursday they are permitted because of the honor of the Sabbath.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Why are the bystanders &lt;men of the watch&gt; permitted to drink water &lt;wine&gt; during the night but not during the day? For if the service would be too much for the men of the watch &lt;bystanders&gt; the bystanders &lt;men of the watch&gt; would join them<sup class="footnote-marker">184a</sup><i class="footnote">The scribe’s text clearly is completely off; the text of G has one major defect. The correct text obviously has to read: “Why are the men of the watch permitted to drink wine during the night but not during the day? For if the service would be too much for the men of the clan the men of the watch would join them.”</i>. “The people of the clan neither by day nor by night,” since they are permanently in service<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">Priests on duty are forbidden wine and any intoxicating drink, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:8-11" href="/Leviticus.10.8-11"><i>Lev</i>. 10:8–11</a>. The priests on stand-by may drink in the evening since by morning the effects of the wine will have disappeared. The members of the clan who during the night also are occupied in Temple service, either on watch or to dispose of the remainders of the sacrifices of the previous day, may not drink alcohol during the entire period of their actual duty. Obviously this Mishnah spells out rules for the entire year, independent of fast days.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is repeated at the start of Mo`ed qatan 3:1, with the places of Ta`aniot and Mo`ed qatan duly switched.</i>“The people of the watch and those of the bystanders<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">The Non-priests standing by at the time of offering of the public sacrifices as representatives of this public (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.2.1">Mishnah 4:2</a>). In practice these are delegates of the district from which the watch serving during the week was drawn. They are forced to appear for duty in clean garments and well groomed by being forbidden these activities during their week of duty.</i> are forbidden to shave<sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">Groom their beards.</i> and to wash their garments, but on Thursday they are permitted because of the honor of the Sabbath.” Therefore on all other days they are forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">There seems to be no biblical or rabbinical reason for the prohibition.</i>? Rebbi Yose, Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan; Rebbi Abun, Rebbi Yasa in the name of Ḥizqiah: They decreed about them so they should not enter their week badly groomed. There<sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Mo`ed qaṭan</i>3:1.</i>, we have stated: “The following do (wash their garments) [shave]<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">The corrector’s [text] is that of the Mishnah; also confirmed by G. The scribe’s text is a lapse of the pen.</i> on the holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">The corrector’s [text] is that of the Mishnah; also confirmed by G. The scribe’s text is a lapse of the pen.</i>: He who comes from overseas, or from captivity, or who leaves the jail, or the excommunicated one from whom the Sages lifted {the excommunication.}” Therefore all other people are forbidden? Rebbi Simon said, they decreed about them so they should not enter the holiday badly groomed.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:2" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.2">Tosephta 2:2</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 17a" href="/Taanit.17a">Babli 17a</a>.</i>: “Any one who knows the people of his watch and the people of his clan which is not<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">Even though this is the text of both Yerushalmi sources, it seems clear that with all Tosephta and most Babli texts one has to delete this word.</i> of the fixed clans, is forbidden this entire day. Any one who knows the people of his watch but not the people of his clan which is not<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">Even though this is the text of both Yerushalmi sources, it seems clear that with all Tosephta and most Babli texts one has to delete this word.</i> of the fixed clans, is forbidden this entire week. Any one who knows neither the people of his watch nor the people of his clan which is not<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">Even though this is the text of both Yerushalmi sources, it seems clear that with all Tosephta and most Babli texts one has to delete this word.</i> of the fixed clans: Rebbi says, I am saying that he is permanently forbidden, but his improvement is his detriment, in that he may deliver eulogies.<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">This Tosephta presupposes that even after the destruction of the Temple it was known (and, as Genizah poems prove, up to the time of the first crusade it was publicly announced every Sabbath, ידיעות המכון לחקר השירה העברית vol. 5, pp. 111–112) which watch would serve were the Temple in existence. If a person has a tradition that his ancestors actually had been serving in the Temple as members of the clan whose day is fixed any time their watch is serving are subject to the restriction in the use of wine spelled out in the Mishnah and in addition have to treat the day as a holiday when they are forbidden work and mourning. Since the rebuilding of the Temple is expected to be sudden in a miraculous way, the Cohen has to be ready to serve anytime at a moment’s notice. If these data are unknown to the Cohen, logically he should be forbidden wine and work all his adult life. Since this is obviously a rabbinic restriction which is impossible to follow, the restriction must be waved and his detriment, that he does not know his place in the genealogy of priests, is his improvement in that he may work and drink wine any day where this is permitted to non-Cohanim.</i>” As you are saying, his detriment is his improvement that he may not deliver eulogies, similarly is (his detriment his improvement) [his improvement his detriment] that he would be forbidden to work<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">The text of this sentence is thoroughly garbled in the scribe’s, the corrector’s, and G’s versions but the meaning is clear as explained in the preceding Note.</i>?

Halakhah 12

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Anywhere it is written in the Scroll “not to deliver eulogies”, before it is forbidden, afterwards is permitted. Rebbi Yose says, before and after are forbidden. “Not to fast”, before and after it is permitted; Rebbi Yose says, before is forbidden, afterwards permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">The “Scroll” is the “Scroll of fasts”, a late pre-Mishnah document mostly commemorating victories either of Maccabeans against Seleucids or revolutionaries against Romans, or Pharisees abolishing Sadducee usages. The entire discussion of Megillat Ta`anit is repeated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 1:4:2-14" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.1.4.2-14">Megillah 1:6</a> (מ). “Before” and “after” refers to the days preceding and following these rabbinic (or traditional) festive days, which are treated as if biblical.</i>
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">194*</sup><i class="footnote">This Halakhah and the next are repeated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 1:3:4-5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.1.3.4-5">Megillah 1:5</a> (מ).</i> The Mishnah is Rebbi Meïr’s, since Rebbi Meïr said, “not to eulogize” one is forbidden to fast, “not to fast” one is permitted to eulogize<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">“To eulogize”, to eulogize a deceased person either on his funeral or on a formal occasion in his remembrance. Both are incompatible with a holiday spirit. In the Babli, the attribution to R. Meïr is affirmed in <i>Roš Haššanah</i> and denied in <i>Ta`anit</i> 18a.</i>. “Not to” unspecified<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">A day mentioned in the Scroll without indication of any restriction.</i> is as “not to fast.” Rebbi Jonah said, “these are the days not to eulogize &lt;fast&gt; on them, and partially not to fast &lt;eulogize&gt; on them.<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">The introductory statement to <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>. All sources of <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> support the version in <i>Megillah</i>, here given in &lt;braces&gt;, that days of fast are fewer than days of no eulogies.</i>” Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel said, why does it say “on them” twice? To teach that the night is permitted but the day forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">No restrictions apply to the night of the day mentioned in the Scroll.</i>. As it was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, end of Month of Adar.</i>, “therefore a person who takes it on himself has to forbid himself in prayer.” Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, that he must mention it on the preceding evening<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">If a person intends to fast on a day where this is prohibited by <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, he has to start in the evening and mention his fast in the prayer. Then he has to fast as a vow which is a biblical obligation which cannot be annulled by rabbinical festive days.</i>. This comes following what Rebbi Ze`ira said in the name of Rav Huna: Similar to Friday night and Sabbath day.
The Mishnah either follows Rebbi Yose on the eleventh or Rebbi Meïr on the twelfth<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">This and the following paragraph refer to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 1:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.1.3.1">Mishnah <i>Megillah</i>1:5</a> where it is stated that even though if the Purim scroll cannot be read on the 14th, one reads it on one of the preceding days, this does not mean that the Purim celebration and the concurrent prohibition of fasting and public mourning are extended. Now <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> for the month of Adar notes rabbinic festive days on the 12th and the 13th, Purim on 14th and 15th, and other holidays on 16th and 17th. Therefore the statement that one may fast and publicly mourn before the official Purim date certainly cannot apply to Adar 13th, and on first look also not to Adar 12th. Since the holiday on the 12th is rejected in the Halakhah, the Mishnah in <i>Megillah</i> may apply to Adar 12th for R. Meïr who does not extend the influence of rabbinic holidays to the preceding day, but only to Adar 11th for R. Yose following his opinion recorded here in Mishnah 14.</i>. But it is difficult for Rebbi Meïr. Was it not stated<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, <i>Adar</i>.</i>, “on the twelfth of it is Tirion<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">The name is טיריון in both occurrences in the Yerushalmi (the single טוריון in G may be disregarded); in <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> it is טריינוס, in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 18b" href="/Taanit.18b">Babli 18b</a> טוריינוס. Only the last reading can be interpreted as “Trajanus”, and it is difficult to imagine that any happy occasion for Jews should be connected to this name. Also the <i>baraita</i> in <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> makes it clear that one does not refer to an emperor since it states that after this Tirion had killed Julianus and Pappos in Laodicea for their being Jews there came an order from Rome and he was slain.</i> Day?” But Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa said, Tirion Day was disestablished; the day when Julianus and Pappos were killed. “On the thirteenth of it is Nikanor Day<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, <i>Adar</i>.</i>.” What is Nikanor Day? <sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1Maccabees</i>7:19, <i>2Maccabees</i>15:36.</i>“A commander of the Greek government was passing by on his way to Alexandria when he saw Jerusalem, and insulted, vituperated, and blasphemed and said, <i>when I shall return in peace I shall destroy this tower</i><sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">An ironical quote of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Judges 8:9" href="/Judges.8.9"><i>Jud</i>. 8:9</a>.</i>. One of the dynasty of the Hasmoneans went out against him, killed his soldiers until he came to his car<sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>carruca</i>, Greek καρούχα. A travel wagon, not a fighting vehicle.</i>. When he came to his car he hacked off his hand and cut off his head, stuck them on a piece of wood and wrote under it, the mouth which spoke in guilt and the hand stretched out in haughtiness, and hung it on a pole<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">Greek κοντός.</i> outside Jerusalem.” In Rebbi Meïr’s opinion it is understandable, it comes to forbid the previous day<sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">The day preceding Purim.</i>. What does it come to forbid for Rebbi Yose? To forbid the day before he does not need since itself it forbidden because of the fourteenth. It comes to inform you that eulogies are forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Yose only forbids fasting on the day preceding a holiday.</i>. And also for Rebbi Meïr it is not difficult; was it not stated, “on the twelfth of it is Tirion Day?” But Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa said, Tirion Day was disestablished; the day when Julianus and Pappos were killed<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1Maccabees</i>7:19, <i>2Maccabees</i>15:36.</i>. “On the fourteenth and the fifteenth is Purim, not to eulogize. On the sixteenth they started to build the wall of Jerusalem<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">According to the <i>baraita</i> in <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, the repair of the walls damaged by a Gentile army. There is no necessity to refer to the first war against the Romans.</i>, not to eulogize<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, <i>Adar</i>.</i>.” In Rebbi Meïr’s opinion it is understandable, it comes to forbid the previous day. What does it come to forbid for Rebbi Yose? To forbid the day before he does not need since itself is forbidden because of the fifteenth. It comes to inform you that eulogies are forbidden. <sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition, probably to be deleted since missing in <i>Megillah</i>, even though it seems to be supported by G which ends here after two words.</i>[And also for Rebbi Meïr it is not difficult; was it not stated, “on the twelfth of it is Tirion Day?” But Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa said, Tirion Day was disestablished; the day when Julianus and Pappos were killed.]
“On the seventeenth of it Gentiles attacked the remainder of the Sopherim at the city of Khalkis and Bet-Zabdin<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">Khalkis was a city near Tripolis (Lebanon) and Bet-Zavda probably was in Syria. The <i>baraita</i> in <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> connects this with the persecution of the Pharisees by Alexander Yannai.</i> and there was relief.<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, <i>Adar</i>.</i>” In Rebbi Meïr’s opinion it is understandable, it comes to forbid the {day} itself. What does it come to forbid for Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is the day after the second day of Purim which for him automatically is forbidden.</i>? [The day before? Is not the day itself forbidden for him?]<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">Unsupported corrector’s addition, to be deleted.</i> Rebbi Yose said, all these matters neither support nor contradict either Rebbi Meïr or Rebbi Yose; they only come to report the days on which miracles were done for Israel. You have to understand that this is so since we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, <i>Nisan</i>. This does not refer to the start of regular sacrifices as described by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 9" href="/Leviticus.9"><i>Lev</i>. 9</a>, but to the acceptance as Temple practice that public offerings must be paid for by public taxes, against the Sadducee opinion that private donations may be solicited for these.</i>: “On the New Moon of Nisan the Daily Offering was settled, one may not eulogize.” Without this is he not already forbidden because of the New Moon<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">Which is a semi-holiday, only without work-related restrictions.</i>? <sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:6" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.6">Tosephta 2:6</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 17b" href="/Taanit.17b">Babli 17b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 19a" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.19a">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i>19a</a>.</i>“But on Sabbath and holidays one fasts before and after them. What is your reason to be lenient with these and restrictive with those? For these are words of the Torah, and words of the Torah do not need reinforcement. But those are words of the Sopherim<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">The mention of <i>Sopherim</i> indicates that the principles of <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> are part of Ezra’s organization of post-exilic Judaism, even though the redaction of the Scroll belongs to the last generation before the destruction of the 2nd Temple.</i>, and words of the Sopherim need reinforcement.” That is what you were saying, as long as <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was not abolished. But since <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished, all these were abolished. Rebbi Ḥanina and Rebbi Jonathan both said, <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished<sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">First generation Amoraim. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 18b" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.18b">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i>18b</a>. From here on a similar text also is in <i>Nedarim</i>8:1 (Notes 33–35,<b>נ</b>).</i>. Rebbi Abba and Rebbi Simon both said, <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished. Rebbi Joḥanan said, yesterday I was repeating, <sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:5" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.5">Tosephta 2:5</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 18b" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.18b">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i>18b</a>.</i>“it happened that in Lydda they decided on a fast-day on Ḥanukkah. They said about Rebbi Eliezer that he got a haircut, and about Rebbi Joshua that he took a {thermal} bath<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">Forbidden on a later fast-day for rain, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 1:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.1.6.1">Mishnah 1:7</a>.</i>. Rebbi Joshua said to them, go and fast because you fasted.” And you are saying, <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished? Rebbi Abba said, even if you are saying that <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished, Ḥanukkah and Purim were not abolished<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">Confirmed in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 19b" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.19b">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 19b</a>.</i>.
The actions of the rabbis imply that <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> was abolished. Rebbi Jonathan fasted every New Year’s Day’s eve. Rebbi Abun fasted every Sabbath eve<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">Even though <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:6" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.6">Tosephta 2:6</a> states that one may fast on Fridays, it notes, as quote from <i>Megillat Ta`anit,</i> the dissenting opinion of R. Yose the Galilean who forbids. The problems of fasting on Friday are taken up in the last paragraph of this Chapter.</i>. Rebbi Ze`ira fasted 300 fasts, and some say 900, and disregarded <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i><sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">The Babli (<i>Bava Meṣia`</i>85a) reports that he fasted in order to forget the teachings of his native Babylonia.</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa commanded the schoolteachers, if a woman comes to ask you, tell her that one may fast any time except Sabbaths, holidays, New Moons, intermediate days of holidays, Ḥanukkah and Purim<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">Only Purim and Ḥanukkah are rabbinic holidays in this list.</i>.

Halakhah 13

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One does not decide about a public fast on Thursdays in order not to inflate prices<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">If people suddenly have to buy provisions not only for the Sabbath but also for breaking the fast on Thursday, food stores might use the increased need to raise prices. The next week people also know of the need to buy extra food and they will do this earlier in the week when competition will keep the prices down.</i>, but the first three fast days on Monday, Thursday, and Monday, and the second three on Thursday, Monday, Thursday. Rebbi Yose says, just as the first one not on Thursdays so not the second ones. Nor the last ones<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">As the Halakhah shows, this sentence is copied from the Babli version; it is not originally Yerushalmi.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">This text is not only copied in <i>Megillah</i>, it exists in a slightly different text in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 4:11:6-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.4.11.6-7"><i>Yebamot</i>4:11 (Notes 172–175</a>).</i> Simeon bar Abba said, there came a case before Rebbi Joḥanan<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">Since the two texts are not identical, one cannot say that the instructions of R. Joḥanan reported here refer to the opinion of R. Yose in <i>Yebamot</i>. It was reported in the previous paragraph that R. Joḥanan was reluctant to declare <i>Megillat Ta`anit</i> as obsolete; here it is noted that he even endorsed the most restrictive version of the interpretations of the scroll. Since the following discussion is one about the principles of edition of Rebbi’s Mishnah, the implication is that R. Joḥanan’s objection is disregarded.</i> and he instructed following Rebbi Yose. Rebbi Eleazar was sorry about this; he said, does one disregard the anonymous {Mishnah} and follow an isolated opinion<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Joḥanan holds in general that the anonymous Mishnah is practice (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 52b" href="/Menachot.52b"><i>Menaḥot</i>52b</a>).</i>? He found that Rebbi Ḥiyya stated this in the name of Rebbi Meïr. When he understood that Rebbi Ḥiyya stated this in the name of Rebbi Meïr., he said, the old man<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">R. Joḥanan.</i> understands his chapters well. Rebbi Mana asked before Rebbi Yudan: Did not Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Abbahu say in the name of Rebbi Eleazar, every place where Rebbi taught a disagreement and afterwards taught it anonymously, practice follows the anonymous statement. He said to him, and if not Rebbi, maybe somebody else. How is this? If it is found that Rebbi taught a disagreement and afterwards taught it anonymously, then practice follows the anonymous statement. In a case where Rebbi did not teach a disagreement but others taught it in disagreement and Rebbi taught it anonymously, certainly practice has to follow the anonymous text. There come Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Simeon bar Abba, in the name of Rebbi Eleazar, every place where Rebbi taught a disagreement and afterwards taught it anonymously, practice follows the anonymous statement. Why does he instruct here following the isolated opinion? Rebbi Samuel bar Ina in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: That is, if no disagreement is stated together with the anonymous opinion. But if a disagreement is stated together with the anonymous opinion, practice does not follow the anonymous opinion. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: that is if an individual disagrees with an individual. But in the case of an individual following the {anonymous} Sages, practice does not follow the anonymous text<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 42b" href="/Yevamot.42b">Babli (<i>Yebamot</i>42b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Kamma 102a" href="/Bava_Kamma.102a"><i>Bava qamma</i>102a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Avodah Zarah 7a" href="/Avodah_Zarah.7a"><i>Avodah zarah</i>7a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Niddah 11b" href="/Niddah.11b"><i>Niddah</i>11b</a>) formulates the rule in the name of R. Joḥanan: Disagreement followed by anonymous statement, practice follows the anonymous statement. Anonymous statement followed by disagreement, practice does not follow the anonymous statement.</i>.
(Rebbi Yose agrees for the seven last ones.<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">The sentence was deleted by the editor of the Venice edition and therefore is missing in the printed versions of the Yerushalmi. R. Yose agrees that by the time of the last fast days people already are used to preparing for the fast day well in advance. J.N.Epstein in <i>Tarbiz</i> 5, 1934, pp. 261-262.</i>)

Halakhah 14

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One does not decide on a fast day<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">To start a series of 3 or 7 fast days for rain, or an isolated fast day because of a public calamity.</i> on a New Moon, on Ḥanukka, or Purim. If they started, they do not interrupt<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Once the fast day on a New Moon or Ḥanukkah, etc., is not the first in the series, one does not interrupt the regular sequence of Mondays and Thursdays.</i>, the words of Rabban Gamliel. Rebbi Meïr said, even though Rabban Gamliel said that one does not interrupt, he agreed that one does not complete<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">One stops fasting before nightfall.</i>. The same on a Ninth of Av which falls on a Friday<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">So one does not start the Sabbath when hungry. In our computed calendar the Ninth of Av, which always falls on the same weekday as the first day of Passover, never falls on an Friday.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> How much is “started”<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">How many times does one have to fast to continue fasting on a day of the New Moon?</i>? Rebbi Abba said, once. Rebbi Yose said, twice. It was acted on following Rebbi Abba<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">This is binding precedent. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 18b" href="/Taanit.18b">Babli 18b</a> concurs. [However the Babli switches the attributions between RR. Aḥa and Yose (not Assi, impossible for chronological reasons, cf. Rabbinovicz, <i>Variae Lectiones, ad loc</i>. Note מ.)]</i>. And what does one read? Rebbi Yose said, one reads “blessings and curses.<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 26:3-46" href="/Leviticus.26.3-46"><i>Lev</i>. 26:3–46</a>, the public Torah reading for all fast days for rain, even if such a fast is on a New Moon or Ḥanukkah which have their own fixed readings.</i>” Rebbi Mana said to him, since they know it is a fast day they are falling on their bellies, do they not know that it is a fast day<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">Usually called “falling on one’s face”, the penitentiary prayer following the Amidah, which is omitted on all festive days. But if the day of the New Moon, where usually the penitentiary prayer is omitted, is a fast day for rain, the penitentiary prayer is recited. Since therefore everybody knows that it is a fast day, why does one have to change the customary Torah reading?</i>? He said to him, to tell you that one reads “blessings and curses.<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">Since the penitentiary prayer is incompatible with the reading for the New Moon, everybody expects to read the portion customary for the fast day.</i>” Rebbi Yudan from Kappadokia said before Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Jehudah bar Pazi, one reads about the New Moon<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:11-15" href="/Numbers.28.11-15"><i>Num</i>. 28:11–15</a>.</i>. Rebbi Yose met Rebbi Jehudah bar Pazi; he said to him, did you hear this from your father? He said to him, my father said this only about Eintab<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">The permanent seat of the Calendar Court, which has to proclaim every New Moon in the absence of a computed calendar.</i>. Since they know that it is the New Moon, they are reading about the New Moon. At all other places they are reading “blessings and curses.”
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:7" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.7">Tosephta 2:7</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 41a" href="/Eruvin.41a">Babli <i>Eruvin</i>41a</a>.</i>: “On a Ninth of Av which falls on a Friday he eats even an egg and drinks even a cup full<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">He breaks the fasts shortly before sundown.</i>, in order not to enter the Sabbath being deprived, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Yose says, he fasts and finishes.<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">He fasts until it certainly is the Sabbath since the obligation is to eat a festive meal on the Sabbath and this is not infringed on if he stays fasting into the Sabbath.</i>” Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rav Jehudah, Rebbi Immi bar Ezechiel<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">The brother of Rav Jehudah, ordained in Palestine. In the Babli he is called Rammi bar Ezechiel.</i> in the name of Rav: Practice follows him who says, he fasts and finishes. Why does he not say, practice follows Rebbi Yose? There are Tannaim who switch the names of the sages. Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rav Ḥuna: Even an individual who decided for himself to fast on a Friday fasts and finishes. As the following: Rebbi Bevai was sitting before Rebbi Yasa; he wanted to learn from him this matter<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">He fasted on a Friday in order to receive instructions from his teacher on how ro proceed.</i>. He said, let me go home a little bit. He said to him, it is afternoon. He answered, I am fasting. He said to him, I have lupines with me. He answered, and one finishes following Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">First R. Bevai asked whether he could go home and break the fast before sundown. This was denied, but R. Yasa said, he had some lupines, (Greek θέρμος) animal feed which is turned into human food by extended cooking. Since the lupines would not be edible before nightfall, R. Bevai concluded that he was told that practice is to keep fasting into the Sabbath.</i>.


Chapter 3



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The order of these fast-days was said for the first period of rains. But about abnormal growth one sounds the alarm immediately<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">While the extended prayers and shofar blowing are instituted if there are no rains in the entire month of Marḥeshwan, even though the need becomes apparent in the second half of the month, a fast-day instituted because of danger to growing crops (such as widespread fungus) is proclaimed on the first Monday after the phenomenon was observed and accompanied by blowing the <i>shofar</i>.</i>. Also if rains stopped for 40 days between rainy periods one raises the alarm about it since it is a sign of drought<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Since the crop which started to grow after the first rains will wither and be lost before the second rains.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “The order of these fast-days was said,” etc. What is their “immediately”? Rav said, Monday<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">The first Monday after the need became evident. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 19b" href="/Taanit.19b">Babli 19b</a>.</i>, Thursday, and Monday. If it became abnormal on Monday, what about sounding the alarm on Thursday<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">But <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 2:13:3-14:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.2.13.3-14.1">Mishnah 2:15</a> forbids to start a series of fast-days on Thursdays.</i>? Rebbi Ze`ira understood it from the following<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Daniel 10:12" href="/Daniel.10.12"><i>Dan</i>. 10:12</a>.</i>: <i>He said to me, do not fear, Daniel, since from the first day when you intended to fast before the Eternal, your God, your words were heard.</i> Already your words were heard. And here, since the Court were determined to do it is as if they did<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">The fast-day is proclaimed immediately but executed only the next Monday.</i>.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:8" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.8">Tosephta 2:8</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 19b" href="/Taanit.19b">Babli 19b</a>.</i>: “Just as one sounds the alarm during the other years of a Sabbatical period, so one sounds the alarm during the Sabbatical because of the livelihood of others.” What means “because of the livelihood of others”? The colleagues said, because of the livelihood of Gentiles. Rebbi Ze`ira said, because of the livelihood of the suspect ones<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">People suspected of dealing in Sabbatical produce. While the poor and everybody else are permitted to collect spontaneously growing produce on any field in the Holy Land, nobody is permitted to use any of these as an object of trade.</i>. That of Rebbi Ze`ira follows Rebbi, that of the colleagues follows Rebbi Phineas ben Yair. That of Rebbi Ze`ira follows Rebbi: A teacher<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Possibly one may read סַפָּר “barber”. But it is difficult to see why a barber should be disciplined by Rebbi.</i> was suspected in matters of Sabbatical produce. They brought him before Rebbi who said to them, what should this wretch do, he does it for his livelihood. But that of the colleagues follows Rebbi Phineas ben Yair. <sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">From here on the text also is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:3:12" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.3.12"><i>Demay</i> 1:3 (Notes 145–149</a>,<b>ד</b>).</i> Rebbi wanted to permit the Sabbatical year<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Since in the absence of a Temple and the distribution of land as ordered in the Torah the Sabbatical year is observed as a rabbinic ordinance, Rebbi wanted to permit cultivation of the land to help pay real estate taxes which were imposed irrespective of yield. A generation later R, Yannay did just this.</i>. Rebbi Phineas ben Yair went to him. He said to him: how is the grain doing? He answered him: endives<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">They are irrelevant for taxes or a payment in kind (<i>annona</i>) to the Roman army.</i> are doing fine. He said to him: how is the grain doing? He answered him: endives are doing fine. From this, Rebbi understood that he did not agree with him. He said to him: Would the Rabbi care to eat a bite with me today? He said to him, yes. When he came, he saw the she-mules<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>mulus</i>. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 8:5:3-8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.8.5.3-8">Yoma 8:5</a> it is stated that the kick of a white mule is life threatening; white mules should not be kept by Jews.</i> of Rebbi standing. He said, are all these fed by Jews? He will not see me again! They went and told this to Rebbi. Rebbi sent and wanted to pacify him. They found him in his city. He said, the people of my city should come close to me. The people of his city came and surrounded him. They said to them, Rebbi wants to make peace with him. They left him and went away. He said, my sons should come close to me. Fire descended from Heaven and surrounded him. They returned and told Rebbi. He said, since we did not have merit to eat our fill from him in this world, may we be worthy to eat our fill from him in the World to Come.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If they descended on produce but not on trees<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Rain beneficial to fields but not to orchards</i>, on trees but not on produce, on both but not on cisterns, ditches, or caves<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The water reservoirs for the dry seasons.</i>, one sounds the alarm immediately.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “If they descended on produce but not on trees,” little by little, “on trees but not on produce,” only heavy downpours, “on both but not on cisterns, ditches, or caves, one sounds the alarm immediately.” It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:8" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.8">Tosephta 2:8</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 19b" href="/Taanit.19b">Babli 19b</a>.</i>: “One sounds the alarm about trees half a month before Passover<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Since Passover is the time of the barley harvest, it is too late for saving produce but still in time to save vines and olive trees.</i>, about cisterns, ditches and caves half a month before Pentecost.” Then even later<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Since if water reservoirs are empty at the end of the rainy season, everybody’s life is in danger.</i>? Later it would be a miracle, and one does not sound the alarm expecting miracles.
Rebbi Berekhiah, Rebbi Ḥelbo Pappos in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: Sometimes rains fall because of the merit of one person, the merit of one grass blade, the merit of one field. All three are from one verse<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 10:1" href="/Zechariah.10.1"><i>Sach</i>. 10:1</a>.</i>, <i>and rain showers He will give to you, to a man, grass, in the field. To a man</i>, but not to men. To <i>a grass</i>, but not to grasses. <i>In the field</i>, but not in fields.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> And also a town on which no rain fell<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">While the rest of the country got rain.</i>, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Amos 4:7" href="/Amos.4.7"><i>Amos</i>4:7</a>. Description of a curse.</i>: <i>I shall give rain on one town and on another town I shall not give rain; one parcel will receive rain but the leaves of a parcel which does not receive rain will wilt</i>. This town fasts and blows the <i>shofar</i> and all its surroundings<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">While they have crops, they are at risk since the increased demand from the town without crops will drive prices higher.</i> fast but do not blow the <i>shofar;</i> Rebbi Aqiba says they blow the <i>shofar</i> but do not fast.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Simon said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Amos 4:7" href="/Amos.4.7"><i>Amos</i>4:7</a>. Description of a curse.</i>: <i>I shall give rain on one town and on another town I shall not give rain; one parcel will receive rain but the leaves of a parcel which does not receive rain will wilt.</i> The merit of the field does it.
<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Bereishit Rabbah 13:5" href="/Bereishit_Rabbah.13.5"><i>Gen. rabba</i>13(5</a>). The problem is that in the Creation it is asserted that fog from below created the conditions for agriculture but its continued existence depends on rain from the clouds. In <i>Gen. rabba:</i> For 4 causes the Holy One, praise to Him, changed nature so that the earth should be irrigated from above.</i> For four causes the rains fall down; because of violent men<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Who are prevented from monopolizing water resources.</i>, because of noxious dew, and that the high country drink like the low country, and that everybody direct his eyes to Heaven. <sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 8b" href="/Taanit.8b">Babli 8b</a>.</i> By the merit of three causes does rain fall. By the merit of the Land, by the merit of charity, and by the merit of sufferings; and all are in one verse<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Job</i>. 37:13.</i>: <i>If for (charity) [the stick], if for the Land, if for (the stick) [for charity] you will find it</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Part of a larger story in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.7"><i>Qiddušin</i>4:1 (Notes 54–58</a>), copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 78b" href="/Yevamot.78b">Babli <i>Yebamot</i>78b</a>; <i>Midrash Samuel</i>28[5]; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bamidbar Rabbah 8:4" href="/Bamidbar_Rabbah.8.4"><i>Num. rabba</i>8(4</a>).</i> Four sins cause the rains to be halted. The sins of idolatry, incestuous and adulterous behavior, spilling blood, and of those who pledge publicly for charity but do not pay up. By the sin of idolatry from where? <sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 11:16-17" href="/Deuteronomy.11.16-17"><i>Deut</i>. 11:16–17</a>.</i><i>Guard</i><i>yourselves, that your heart not be led astray so you deviate and worship other powers</i>, etc. What is written next? <i>The Eternal’s rage will be inflamed against you; He will arrest the sky and there will be no rain.</i> By the sin of incestuous and adulterous behavior, from where? <sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 3:2-3" href="/Jeremiah.3.2-3"><i>Jer</i>. 3:2–3</a>.</i><i>You pollute the Land by your whoring and your criminality</i>. What is the punishment for this? <i>It prevents rain showers, and there will be no late rain</i>. By the sin of the spillers of blood, from where? <sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 35:33" href="/Numbers.35.33"><i>Num</i>. 35:33</a>.</i><i>For the blood pollutes the Land</i>. The blood will make anger rest on the Land. By the sin of those who pledge publicly for charity but do not pay up, from where? <sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 25:14" href="/Proverbs.25.14"><i>Prov</i>. 25:14</a>.</i><i>Clouds and wind but no rain, a man who takes credit for a lying gift</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Bereishit Rabbah 13:11" href="/Bereishit_Rabbah.13.11"><i>Gen. rabba</i>13(11</a>).</i> It is called by five names: fog, canopy, cloud, prince, and storm-cloud. From where “fog”? <i>And fog rose from the earth</i><sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 2:6" href="/Genesis.2.6"><i>Gen</i>. 2:6</a>.</i>. “Thick cloud,” [which thickens the sky]<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from <i>Gen. rabba</i>.</i>, <i>behold, I shall come to you in a canopy of cloud</i><sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 19:9" href="/Exodus.19.9"><i>Ex</i>. 19:9</a>.</i>. “Cloud”, because it makes people meek with one another. “Prince” because it turns owners of houses into princes: <i>He raises rain-clouds from the ends of the earth</i><sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 135:7" href="/Psalms.135.7"><i>Ps</i>. 135:7</a>.</i>. “Storm-clouds” because it turns the sky into multiple visions<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Deriving the unexplained word as <i>pilpel</i> form of חזה “to have a vision”.</i>: <i>The Eternal makes storm clouds</i><sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 10:1" href="/Zechariah.10.1"><i>Sach</i>. 10:1</a>.</i>.
“All its surroundings<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">While they have crops, they are at risk since the increased demand from the town without crops will drive prices higher.</i> fast but do not blow the <i>shofar</i>;” since we find that on the Day of Atonement one fasts but does not blow the <i>shofar</i>. “Rebbi Aqiba says they blow the <i>shofar</i> but do not fast,” since we find that on New Year’s Day one blows the <i>shofar</i> but does not fast.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Similarly, a town in which there is an epidemic or a building collapse, this town fasts and blows the <i>shofar</i>, and all its surroundings<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">While they have crops, they are at risk since the increased demand from the town without crops will drive prices higher.</i> fast but do not blow the <i>shofar;</i> Rebbi Aqiba says they blow the <i>shofar</i> but do not fast.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> There was an epidemic in Sepphoris but it did not touch the avenue where Rebbi Ḥanina was dwelling. The Sepphoreans were saying, why is this old man amongst us sitting in peace while the neighborhood and the town is ruined? He came to preach and said before them: There was one Zimry in his generation but 24’000 fell of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 25:9" href="/Numbers.25.9"><i>Num</i>. 25:9</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 25:14" href="/Numbers.25.14">14</a>. Zimri’s sin was to sleep with a non-Jewish woman who offered herself to him.</i>. But we, how many Zimry are in our generation<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">Visiting the bordellos in Roman Sepphoris.</i> and you are complaining?
One time they needed to proclaim a fast but no rain fell. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi made (one) [a fast]<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Unnecessary corrector’s addition.</i> in the South<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Lydda.</i> and rain fell. The Sepphoreans were saying, Rebbi Joshua ben Levi brought rain to the Southerners, but Rebbi Ḥanina<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">The local Chief Rabbi.</i> stopped water for the Sepphoreans. They needed to make a fast a second time. He sent and brought Rebbi Joshua ben Levi. He said to him, would my Master be willing to go with us to fast. They both went to the fast but no rain fell. He came to preach and said before them, not Rebbi Joshua ben Levi brought rain to the Southerners, nor Rebbi Ḥanina stopped water for the Sepphoreans. Only the Southerners’ hearts are soft and they hear words of instruction and submit. But the Sepphoreans’ hearts are hard; they hear words of instruction and do not submit. When he came home he raised his eyes and saw the air clear. He said, is it still like this<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">That his sermon had no influence on the people and therefore, while the drought was not his fault as explained in the next paragraph, it was his failure as a preacher which was the indirect cause. For this he felt very badly; Heaven sent rain to make feel him better. All these Aramaic texts are sermon concepts.</i>? Immediately rain fell. He vowed by himself not to do this again. He said, who am I to tell to the creditor not to collect his due?
Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: What should the great men of a generation do since the public is judged only according to its majority? So we find that during the 38 years during which Israel were as in a ban, He did not speak with Moses, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 2:16-17" href="/Deuteronomy.2.16-17"><i>Deut</i>. 2:16–17</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>.</i>: <i>It was when all the warriors finished dying from inside the camp</i>. What is written next? <i>The Eternal spoke to me to give orders</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: What should the great men of a generation do since the public is judged only according to its majority? So we find that if Israel had not said<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 18:39" href="/I_Kings.18.39"><i>1K</i>. 18:39</a>.</i>, <i>The Eternal is the supreme power, the Eternal is the supreme power</i>, no fire would have come down from heaven and burned the sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">However the verse makes it clear that the people answered after the fire had descended.</i>.
Rebbi Joshua ben Yair in the name of Rebbi Phineas ben Yair. Three created the Holy One, praise to Him, and was wondering why He created them. These are the Chaldeans, the Arabs, and evil inclinations. Chaldeans: <i>this is the land of the Chaldeans, of the non-existing people</i><sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 23:13" href="/Isaiah.23.13"><i>Is</i>. 23:13</a>.</i>. If only they did not exist. Arabs: <i>unkept tents of robbers, trusted by those who irritate God, those who God brought in His hand</i><sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 12:6" href="/Job.12.6"><i>Job</i>12:6</a> (to be combined with the statement there v. 9 that the Eternal had created all this.)</i>. Evil inclinations: <i>On this day, this is the Eternal’s oracle, I shall gather the lame, and collect the disowned, and to whom I did wrong</i><sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Micah 4:6" href="/Micah.4.6"><i>Micah</i>4:6</a>.</i>. Rebbi Berekhiah, Rebbi Abba bar Cahana, Rebbi Joshua ben Yair in the name of Rebbi Phineas ben Yair: it is as if I did wrong to them<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Extended <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 52b" href="/Sukkah.52b">Babli <i>Sukkah</i>52b</a>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 31b-32a" href="/Berakhot.31b-32a">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 31b/32a</a> and Rashi’s commentary, first line of 32a; <i>Ta`anit</i>25b in the name of Samuel Minor.</i>.
Rebbi Eliezer organized a fast but no rain fell. Rebbi Aqiba organized a fast and rain fell. He preached and said before them: I shall tell you a parable, to what the situation is comparable. To a king who had two daughters, one insolent and one well-behaved. When the insolent one wanted to come before him, he said, give her what she wants and let her go away. But when the well-behaved came before him, he was patient and liked to hear her request. Is it permitted to say this<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Extended <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 52b" href="/Sukkah.52b">Babli <i>Sukkah</i>52b</a>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 31b-32a" href="/Berakhot.31b-32a">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 31b/32a</a> and Rashi’s commentary, first line of 32a; <i>Ta`anit</i>25b in the name of Samuel Minor.</i>? Only not to desecrate the Name of Heaven through Rebbi Eliezer.
Rav Aḥa organized thirteen fast days<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">As described in Chapter 2.</i> but no rain fell. When he went home he encountered a Samaritan who said to him: Rabbi, Rabbi, squeeze your garment because of the rain.
