He answered him, by the life of this man, Heaven will perform wonders and the year will be successful but this man will not then live. Heaven performed wonders, the year was successful, but this Samaritan died, and people were saying, come and see the fruits of the sun<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">That there were abundant fruits without rains.</i>.
“All its surroundings<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">While they have crops, they are at risk since the increased demand from the town without crops will drive prices higher.</i> fast but do not blow the <i>shofar</i>;” since we find that on the Day of Atonement one fasts but does not blow the <i>shofar</i>. “Rebbi Aqiba says they blow the <i>shofar</i> but do not fast,” since we find that on New Year’s Day one blows the <i>shofar</i> but does not fast.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> What is an epidemic<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">That one fasts and/or blows the <i>shofar</i> to bring people to repentance.</i>? A town which could mobilize 500 soldiers<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Able bodied males between the ages of 20 and 50.</i> and there were taken out three dead persons on three consecutive days<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Who die because of the same disease.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Levi said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 28:21" href="/Deuteronomy.28.21"><i>Deut</i>. 28:21</a>.</i>: <i>The Eternal will stick to you the epidemic</i>. {A parable} of a woman who sticks three loaves together<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">A plague for which one fasts is a infectious disease.</i>. How is this acted on? Is it not that larger it needs another rate<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">Goes a town larger than that mentioned in the Mishnah by different rules both in the number of victims and in the number of days?</i>? Let us hear it from the following: Even a city large as Antiochia, and there were brought out three dead persons during three consecutive days. This implies that larger it needs another rate<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">The interpretation of this sentence depends on the interpretation of the expression “rate”. If this means “percentage” then instead of “needs” one has to read “does not need”. If it means “absolute numbers” then the text as it stands is correct. Since there is no corrector’s addition, the second interpretation is to be accepted.</i>. The houses about which they spoke<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 3:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.3.4.1">Mishnah 4</a>; one fasts only for unforeseeable building collapses.</i>, healthy but not shaky. And similarly, young people but not old ones. It was stated: Diphtheria any; two by plague and one by diphtheria. Come and see, “diphtheria any” and you are saying so<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">If one fasts for one deadly case of diphtheria (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 2:9" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).2.9">Tosephta 2:9</a>), why the mention of two deaths by another communicable disease?</i>? It is needed for the case that they blew the <i>shofar</i> about diphtheria and it went away and after that two died of a plague and one of diphtheria<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">In the case of diphtheria, the requirement is waived that to declare an epidemic the causes of death must be the same infection.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> About the following one blows the <i>shofar</i> everywhere: About blight and canker<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">These destroy the harvest.</i>, about locusts and <i>ḥasil</i><sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Kinds of locust as explained in the Halakhah.</i>, about dangerous beasts, and on war<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">Mainly civil war.</i> one blows the <i>shofar</i> since it is a moving plague.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Ḥama bar Uqba in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina: One blows the <i>shofar</i> for the failure of the flax crop. What is the reason? <i>Horrible and execrable things happened in the land</i><sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 5:30" href="/Jeremiah.5.30"><i>Jer</i>. 5:30</a>.</i>. Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: One blows the <i>shofar</i> about hot East wind<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">Which coming from the Arabian desert is very dry and threatens to dry out growing crops.</i>. What is the reason? <i>I went black without sun</i><sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">The sand blown by the East wind makes the sun disappear in a haze.</i>, <i>I rose in the assembly to pray</i><sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 30:28" href="/Job.30.28"><i>Job</i> 30:28</a>.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar said, honor your healer before you need him<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">A quote from <i>Sirachides</i> 38:1.</i>. What is the reason? <i>If your prayer had preceded your need, and all efforts of power</i><sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 36:19" href="/Job.36.19"><i>Job</i> 36:19</a>. Just as one should have good relations with one’s doctor before sickness strikes, so one should pray to prevent bad things to happen. The <i>ḥamsin</i> itself is not dangerous but it points to dangerous consequences.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish. Rebbi Joḥanan said, [if you prayed, no one up high will begrudge you, but all will reinforce your power, <i>and all efforts of power</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, if you prayed,]<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from the quote in <i>Yalqut Job</i> #920. A different, more explicit, version in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 44b" href="/Sanhedrin.44b">Babli, <i>Sanhedrin</i> 44b</a>.</i> do not keep your mouth narrow, but <i>open your mouth and I shall fill it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 81:11" href="/Psalms.81.11"><i>Ps</i>. 81:11</a>.</i>.
Not only a locust but even a wing<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">Since a wing recognizable as from a dangerous locust proves their presence. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 22a" href="/Taanit.22a">Babli 22a</a></i>. And why is it called <i>ḥasil</i> because it eliminates everything<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">The words used in the Mishnah for “locusts” are biblical. In Talmudic times the name was <i>govai</i>, possibly Arabic גוואב “traveller through the desert.”</i>. And why is called <i>govai</i>? Because it forecloses the claims of its Master<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">Is an instrument of Divine retribution.</i>. Not only a dangerous beast but even a dangerous domestic animal. Already there were years in the Land of Israel when a donkey’s bite was deadly, a steer’s bite was deadly. Not only declared war, but also war in peacetime<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">Or the Roman army in Roman territory since its pay was mostly plunder. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 22a" href="/Taanit.22a">Babli 22a</a>.</i>, which already happened in the time of Josiah.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> It happened that Elders left Jerusalem for their cities to decree a fast since blight to fill an oven<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">Enough grain which if healthy would have been enough to form a cake filling a small portable clay oven.</i> was seen in Ascalon<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">A Philistine city just outside the borders of Hasmonean Judua.</i>. Also they decreed a fast the following day because wolves ate two children in Transjordan. Rebbi Yose says, not that they ate but that they were seen.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> That is, if collected. But dispersed even less than that<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">Since every incidence of blight is a focus of infection, dispersed incidences of blight are much more dangerous. “Less” is Latin <i>parum</i>.</i>. Rebbi Mana said, if the are seen one pursues them<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">If one has time to organize a pursuit, one chases the wild predators away until they do no longer present a danger. R. Yose’s remark seems unjustified.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, they were seen at a place inappropriate for them<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">While in general wild predators are only a danger if they form a pack, if they are seen in town even a single one is an indication that he is part of a pack and therefore dangerous. R. Yose’s remark is justified. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 22a" href="/Taanit.22a">Babli 22a</a> has a different criterion.</i>.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> About the following one blows the <i>shofar</i> on a Sabbath: About a town surrounded by Gentiles<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Who come as enemies.</i> or a river<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">In a flood.</i>, and a ship in danger in the ocean. Rebbi Yose said, to help<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">Blowing the <i>shofar</i> on a Sabbath is rabbinically forbidden; it only is permitted as a military signal to mobilize all available personnel in a situation where lives are at stake.</i> but not to vociferation. Simeon from Timna says, also about an epidemic but the Sages did not agree with him<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Since the only people who can help are the doctors who certainly are already on duty.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rav said, <i>answer me, Eternal, answer me</i><sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 18:37" href="/I_Kings.18.37"><i>1K</i>. 18:37</a>. According to the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 14a" href="/Taanit.14a">Babli 14a</a> the reference is not to this verse but to the standard prayer on fast day, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.3.2">Halakhah 2:2, Notes 107–108</a>. He holds that one never sounds the <i>shofar</i> on the Sabbath for any reason whatsoever, but he permits penitentiary prayers on a Sabbath (which other authorities permit only on a Day of Atonement which is a Sabbath.)</i>. The Mishnah disagrees with Rav: “Rebbi Yose said, to help<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">Blowing the <i>shofar</i> on a Sabbath is rabbinically forbidden; it only is permitted as a military signal to mobilize all available personnel in a situation where lives are at stake.</i> but not to vociferation.” Therefore the first Tanna holds even for vociferation<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Yose must refer to <i>shofar</i> blowing, and the Mishnah brings his opinion as a modification of, not a contradiction to, the anonymous Tanna’s statement, it follows that the anonymous Mishnah refers to actual <i>shofar</i> blowing.</i>.
Armies came against Levi ben Sisi’s town. He took a Torah scroll and climbed onto the roof. He said: Master of the worlds. If I neglected one word of this Torah scroll they may come; if not, they shall leave. Immediately they were looked for but not found. His student did the same; his hand was paralyzed and they left<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Not every holy man can claim the status of Levi ben Sisi.</i>. His student’s student did the same; his hand was not paralyzed and they did not leave. To say that the idiot is not hurt and dead flesh does not feel the knife<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">A popular adage.</i>.

Halakhah 9

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One blows the <i>shofar</i> because of any danger which menaces the public except an overabundance of rain.<br>It happened that they said to Onias the circle-drawer, pray for rain. He said to them, go and shelter the Passover ovens so they should not get softened. He prayed but no rain fell. What did he do? He drew a circle, stood inside it, and said: Master of the World! Your children trusted me since I am like a familiar before You. I am swearing by Your great Name that I shall not move from here until You show mercy for Your children.<br>Rain started to drip. He said, that is not what I was asking for, but rain {to fill} cistern, ditches, and caves. It rained in a raging storm. He said, that is not what I was asking for, but rain of goodwill, blessing, and donation. It rained normally until Israel moved from Jerusalem to the Temple Mount because of the rain. They came and said to him, just as you prayed for them to come, so pray to remove them. He told them, go and check whether the losers’ stone was wiped away.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Jonah, Simeon bar Abba in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: The thing about which it is impossible to say “enough”, that is blessing. Rebbi Berekhiah, Rebbi Ḥelbo, Rav Abba bar Ilay in the name of Rav: Until your lips will wear out saying, we have enough blessings, we have enough blessings<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">An incomplete copy of a section in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 9:5:17" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.9.5.17"><i>Berakhot</i> 9:7 (Note 290</a>). The beginning is missing which states that this is an explanation of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Malachi 3:10" href="/Malachi.3.10"><i>Mal</i>. 3:10</a>: <i>I shall pour out blessing over you until ‘without enough’</i>.</i>.
“It happened that they said to Onias the circle-drawer, pray for rain. He said to them, go and shelter the Passover ovens so they should not get softened.” This implies that it was close to Passover<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">Verbally “Passover eve.”</i>. It also was stated thus<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Megillat Ta`anit</i>, Month of Adar, 25 days before Passover. The <i>baraita</i> to this statement, copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 23a" href="/Taanit.23a">Babli 23a</a>, defines it as Onias’s fast.</i>: “On the twentieth all the people fasted for rain and it fell on them.”
“He prayed but no rain fell..” Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, because he did not come in meekness. <sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">A different version of this story which knows only of one Onias the circle-drawer is in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 23a" href="/Taanit.23a">Babli 23a</a>. Both versions are reported in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 126" href="/Psalms.126"><i>Midrash Psalms</i> 126</a>.</i> Rebbi Yudan son of proselytes said, this Onias the circle drawer was the grandson of Onias the circle-drawer {who lived} close to the destruction of the Temple. He went to a mountain to his workers. While he was there, rain fell. He went to a cave; when he was sitting down he slumbered and fell asleep. He stayed in his sleep for 70 years, while the Temple was destroyed and rebuilt. At the end of 70 years he awoke from his sleep. He left the cave and found the world changed. At a place where there had been vineyards were olive trees. At a place were there had been olive trees was a field. He asked about the province, and said to them, what is news in the world? They answered him, do you not know what is news in the world? He said, no. They asked him, who are you? He answered them, Onias the circle-drawer. They told him, we heard that when he entered the Temple courtyard it lit up. He went there and it lit up. He recited about himself, <i>when the Eternal leads back the return of Zion we were like sleepers</i><sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 126:1" href="/Psalms.126.1"><i>Ps</i>. 126:1</a>.</i>.
“Rain started to drip..” They said, this happened only to eliminate this one’s vow<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 23a" href="/Taanit.23a">Babli 23a</a>.</i>.
“He said, that is not what I was asking for, but rain {to fill} cistern, ditches, and caves. It rained in a raging storm.” Samuel stated, as pouring from a water-skin.
“He said, that is not what I was asking for, but rain of goodwill, blessing, and donation. It rained normally until Israel moved from Jerusalem to the Temple Mount because of the rain.” This implies that the Temple Mount was covered by a roof. And it was stated so: There was a stoa inside a stoa<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 33b" href="/Berakhot.33b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 33b</a> (referring to Herod’s Temple.)</i>.
“They said to him, just as you prayed for them to come, so pray to remove them. He told them, go and check whether the losers’ stone was wiped away.” What was the purpose of the losers’ stone. Only that anybody who lost something was taking it from there and anybody who found something was bringing it there<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Bava meṣia`</i>28b.</i>. He told them that just as it is impossible for this stone to be wiped off from the world, so it is impossible to pray that the rains should stop. But go and bring me a bull as thanksgiving offering. They went and brought him a bull as thanksgiving offering. He leaned on it with both of his hands and said, my Master! You brought evil on Your children and they could not stand it; You brought benefit on Your children and they could not stand it, but may it be Your pleasure to bring relief. Immediately the wind blew, the clouds dissolved, the sun shone, and the earth dried. They went out and found the desert full of truffles<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 23a" href="/Taanit.23a">Babli 23a</a>.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 22b" href="/Taanit.22b">Babli 22b</a>.</i> They asked Rebbi Eliezer, when may one pray for the rains to stop? He told them, if a person stands on top of the Ophel and with his hands<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli: his feet.</i> makes noise in the Kidron brook. But we trust the merciful Father that He will not bring a deluge over the world. What is the reason? <i>This is to Me like the waters of Noe; as I swore not to bring Noe’s waters another time over the</i> earth<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 54:9" href="/Isaiah.54.9"><i>Is</i>. 54:9</a>.</i>

Halakhah 10

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Simeon ben Shataḥ sent to him and told him, you should be excommunicated<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">According to Maimonides, the excommunication would have been because at the end Onias found a way to pray for the end of the rains. The text of the Mishnah here is that of Maimonides’s autograph; different from the Babli version.</i>, but what can I do since you are misbehaving before the Omnipresent like a son who misbehaves towards his father who does his will. About you the verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 23:28" href="/Proverbs.23.28"><i>Prov</i>. 23:28</a>.</i>, <i>your father and mother will enjoy and the one who bore you jubilate</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Simeon ben Shataḥ sent to him and told him, you should be excommunicated.” For if there had been a decision made as it was decided in the days of Elijah<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">When the decision about rainfall was delegated by God to Elijah (<a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 17:1" href="/I_Kings.17.1"><i>1K</i>. 17:1</a>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 10:2:5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.10.2.5"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 10:2, Notes 147ff</a>.).</i>, would you not have caused a desecration of the Name in public<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">If the decision had been given into the hands of another holy man, his prayer would have been ineffective and people would conclude that prayer is ineffective and stop praying.</i>? And everybody who causes a public desecration of the Name must be excommunicated. [There, we have stated: Rabban Gamliel sent to him, if you hinder the public you will cause a deluge. Would you not hinder the public from performing a meritorious act? And any who would hinder the public from performing a meritorious act must be excommunicated.]<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition; totally garbled copy from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 1:5:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.1.5.4"><i>Roš Haššanah</i> 1:5, Note 279</a>.</i> He answered him, but does not the Holy One, praise to Him, cancel His decision because of the decision of a just person<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">This is the standard interpretation of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 145:19" href="/Psalms.145.19"><i>Ps</i>. 145:19</a>, <i>the pleasure of those who fear Him He will do</i> and similar verses as explained in the next paragraph. Babli <i>Mo`ed qaṭan</i> 16b.</i>? He said to him, [yes]<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition, unnecessary.</i>. The Holy One, praise to Him, may cancel His decision because of the decision of a just person, but He will not cancel the decision of one just person because of the decision of his just colleague<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">This is the essence of the reference to Elijah.</i>.
“But what can I do since you are misbehaving before the Omnipresent like a son who misbehaves towards his father who does his will.” Rebbi Berekhia, Rebbi Abba bar Cahana, Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rav Jehudah. But some say it in the name of Rav Ḥisda, and some say it in the name of Rav Mattanah. <i>You decide the command and He confirms it for you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 22:28" href="/Job.22.28"><i>Job</i> 22:28</a>. All these verses are interpreted to show that God executes the judgment of the just.</i>. Why does the verse say, “for you”? But even if I am saying so and you are saying otherwise, yours is enduring, Mine is not enduring. <i>On your paths shines light</i>; Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, this is rainfall. <i>As heavy as He has loaded the rain-cloud, His light will disperse the cloud</i><sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 37:11" href="/Job.37.11"><i>Job</i> 37:11</a>; justifying Onias against Simeon ben Shataḥ.</i>. <i>For those humbled you order elevation</i><sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 22:29" href="/Job.22.29"><i>Job</i> 22:29</a>.</i>; if I said to humble them and you say to elevate them, yours is enduring, Mine is not enduring. <i>And the one of low eyes will be saved;</i> I said to bring their eyes down by misfortune but you are saying to save them, yours is enduring, Mine is not enduring. I said, <i>may the not-innocent escape</i><sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 22:30" href="/Job.22.30"><i>Job</i> 22:30</a>.</i>? But you [said]<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition.</i>, he shall escape even though he is not innocent, yours is enduring, Mine is not enduring. What means, <i>and he will escape by the purity of your hands</i>, by the choice of your hands, by the merit of meritorious deeds and good works which were in your hands from before.
“About you the verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 23:28" href="/Proverbs.23.28"><i>Prov</i>. 23:28</a>.</i>, <i>your father and mother will enjoy and the one who bore you jubilate.</i>” Why does the verse say, “the one who bore you”<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">What is the difference between the mother and the one who bore him?</i>? Rebbi Mana said, your nation. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, your time<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">The date of his birth will be counted as lucky time.</i>. But the rabbis are saying, just as he brings double curse, so he brings double joy. [As it is said:] <i>a silly son is anger to his father and bitterness to the one who bore him. A wise son brings joy to his father but a silly son is sadness to his mother</i><sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 17:25" href="/Proverbs.17.25"><i>Prov</i>. 17:25</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 10:1" href="/Proverbs.10.1">10:1</a>. The silly son brings pain once to his mother and once to the one who bore him. The wise son brings joy to both in one verse.</i>. What means <i>tugah</i> of his mother? Rebbi Ludah said, it is encrypted language, ashes in his mother’s eyes<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">If letters are represented by numbers from 1 to 22, תוגת  is represented by 22 6 3 22. If nis replaced by 23-<i>n</i> (the <i>atbash</i> rule) one obtains 1 17 20 1 which is אפרא. The prime example is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 51:1" href="/Jeremiah.51.1"><i>Jer</i>. 51:1</a>, the curses against לב קמי which by the same rule are כשדים.</i>. And from where that he brings double joy to her? <i>Your father and mother will enjoy and the one who bore you jubilate</i>.

Halakhah 11

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If they were fasting and it rained before sunrise, they do not finish<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">They do not continue fasting until evening.</i>; after sunrise they finish. Rebbi Eliezer says, before noon they do not finish, after noontime they finish.<br>It happened that they decided on a fast at Lydda when it rained before noon. Rebbi Tarphon said to them, go, eat, drink, and make a holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">Deciding practice following R. Eliezer.</i>. They went, ate, drank, made a holiday, and returned in the evening and recited the Great Hallel. What is the Great Hallel? <i>Give thanks to the supreme Power; truly, His kindness is forever. Give thanks to the Master of masters,</i> <sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 136" href="/Psalms.136"><i>Ps</i>. 136</a>, the only Hallel recited at night in the synagogue.</i><i>etc</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “If they were fasting and it rained before sunrise, they do not finish,” as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 65:24" href="/Isaiah.65.24"><i>Is</i>. 65:24</a>.</i>, <i>before they will call I shall answer</i>. “After sunrise they finish,” <i>still they are talking and I shall hear</i>. Or may be the other way around<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">Maybe the verse could be read differently: “Still they are talking” about convening the prayer service on the next day; “before they will call” during regular service in the morning before the prayers for rain.</i>? Rebbi Tanḥuma said, it was stated so: there is no answer but close to calling, and no calling but close to answering<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Identifying “calling” with “public prayer” as in the second interpretation of the verse.</i>. In the days of Rebbi Yudan they decided on a fast; then rain fell in the night. Rebbi Mana went up to him; he said to him: since I am thirsty, may I drink? He said to him, wait. Maybe they will take counsel to finish<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">If the fast was no longer needed because of the drought, maybe they decided that a penitentiary service was needed for other reasons. The individual is not permitted to break the fast until the fast is suspended by official notice.</i>.
Rebbi Aḥa, Rebbi Abbahu, in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina: One is forbidden to fast until the sixth hour on the Sabbath. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, the Mishnah states this: “before noon they should not finish,” because it is morning; “after noontime they should finish,” since most of the day already was spent in holiness<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">If the fast was no longer needed because of the drought, maybe they decided that a penitentiary service was needed for other reasons. The individual is not permitted to break the fast until the fast is suspended by official notice.</i>.
When Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai desired that it rained, he said to his barber: stand in front of the Temple: because my rabbi needs to be groomed and is not strong enough to suffer; then immediately it started to rain. When Rav Ada bar Aḥawa desired that it rained, he took off his shoe. If he took both off the world was swamped. There were building collapses; Rav let one of his students sit there until they had emptied the house. After that one left the house, the house collapsed. But some are saying, this was Rav Ada bar Aḥawah<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 20b" href="/Taanit.20b">Babli 20b</a> told of Rav Huna. But the follow-up is there also in the name of Rav Ada bar Ahawa.</i>. The Sages sent and asked him, what good deeds did you do? He told them, never came a person earlier than me to the synagogue, and I never left a person in the synagogue before I left. I did not walk four cubits without Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">But mentally repeating subjects of Torah study; a necessity as long as oral law never was written down.</i>, but never mentioned words of the Torah at a smelly place<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">A formal prohibition (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 2:3:2-19" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.2.3.2-19"><i>Berakhot</i> 2:3</a>).</i>. I never prepared my bed and slept deep sleep<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">In order to study Torah “day and night”.</i>, and never walked among the colleagues<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">When the students were sitting on the ground, the teacher may not pass through them since it would look as if he stepped on their heads; he has to go along the wall.</i>. I never called a colleague by a nickname<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">A grave sin; Babli <i>Bava meṣia`</i> 58b.</i>, and never enjoyed the calamity of a colleague. The curse of a colleague never came on my bed<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">But I forgave him immediately.</i>, and I never went in public to a person who was in debt to me<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">Not to embarrass him if he could not pay.</i>. I never was angry with my family, to fulfill what was said<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 101:2" href="/Psalms.101.2"><i>Ps</i>. 101:2</a>.</i>, <i>I shall walk in the simplicity of my heart in the midst of my house</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">The text is repeated from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:7:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.7.2"><i>Pesaḥim</i>5:7, Notes 208–216</a>.</i> What is the Great <i>Hallel</i>? Rebbi Parnakh in the name of Rebbi Ḥaninah; <i>Give thanks to the supreme Power; truly, His kindness is forever. Give thanks to the Master of masters; truly, His kindness is forever</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, on condition of <i>who stand in the Eternal’s house</i><sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 135" href="/Psalms.135"><i>Ps</i>. 135</a> as introduction to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 136" href="/Psalms.136"><i>Ps</i>. 136</a>.</i>. Why these two chapters? Because rainfall is included in them. In the opinion of Rebbi Joḥanan it is understandable, for it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 135:7" href="/Psalms.135.7"><i>Ps</i>. 135:7</a>.</i>, <i>He brings up vapors from the ends of the earth</i>. How is it for Rebbi Ḥaninah? Because it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 136" href="/Psalms.136"><i>Ps</i>. 136</a>, the only Hallel recited at night in the synagogue.</i>, <i>He gives nourishment to all flesh; truly, His kindness is forever</i>. Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Simon, both are saying, ours<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 113-118" href="/Psalms.113-118"><i>Ps</i>. 113–118</a>, the “Egyptian Hallel”.</i>. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, ours. Bar Qappara said, ours. Bar Qappara follows his opinion, as it was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 5:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.5.7.1">Mishnah <i>Pesaḥim</i>5:7</a>.</i>: “during the existence of a third group they never reached <i>I am loving; truly the Eternal listened to my voice, my supplication</i>, since its people were few.” Bar Qappara stated, this is the Great Hallel. A patrician stood before the Ark<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 65:24" href="/Isaiah.65.24"><i>Is</i>. 65:24</a>.</i>; he said to them, repeat after me what I am saying. This implies that it is not ours<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">If it were the regular <i>Hallel</i>, the congregation would not repeat the verses but answer every half-verse with “Hallelujah” (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shabbat 16:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shabbat.16.1.7"><i>Šabbat</i> 16, Note 59</a>).</i>. [Rebbi Mana said, it is ours.]<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from <i>Pesaḥim</i>.</i> The miracle was great; therefore he said to them, repeat after me what I am saying<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">Because of the extraordinary nature of the event, he changed the usual response to repetition of the entire <i>Hallel</i>.</i>

Chapter 4



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On three occasions the Cohanim lift their hands<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">To pronounce the priestly blessing in the synagogue.</i> four times a day, during morning prayers, <i>musaf</i>, afternoon prayers, and at the closing of the doors<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ne`ilah</i>, a synagogue service close to sundown.</i>: On fast-days<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Fast days for rain.</i>, for the bystanders<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>.</i>, and on the Day of Atonement.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “On three occasions,” etc. One understands from three things. One understands that the bystanders (pray) [fast]<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Here it seems that the corrector’s text [in brackets] is correct. The argument is that the recitation of the priestly blessing is a sacral act and as such forbidden to Cohanim under the influence of alcohol (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:8-11" href="/Leviticus.10.8-11"><i>Lev</i>. 10:8–11</a>). Since they have to recite the blessing late in the afternoon, they could not have drunk any alcohol during the day and therefore would not have eaten either.</i>, and that they pray<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">In a technical sense, “to pray” means “to recite the <i>Amidah</i> prayer”. In a synagogue setting the priests recite the blessing only during the reader’s recitation of the <i>Amidah.</i></i> four times, and lifting of the hands is not during nighttime, only during daytime<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Since there is no priestly blessing during evening prayers (whose status in Mishnaic times was not well defined.)</i>. Could one not lift his hands without praying? We find prayer without lifting of hands; we do not find lifting of hands without prayer<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Outside the Temple. The priestly blessing during synagogue service is a strictly pharisaic institution; it seems from the Manual of Discipline that at least at Qumran the priests only recited poetic allusions to the biblical priestly blessing.</i>. It was stated, these are the words of Rebbi Meïr<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 3:1" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).3.1">Tosephta 3:1</a>. In this text, the opponents of R. Meïr only admit priestly blessing during the two morning services. This is compatible with the scribe’s text in this paragraph.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 26b" href="/Taanit.26b">Babli 26b</a>. Copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 6:8:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.6.8.3"><i>Eruvin</i> 6, Note 102</a>.</i> Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: In matters of <i>eruvin</i> and public fast-days everybody follows Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name Rebbi Joḥanan: Even about the reading of the Esther scroll everybody follows Rebbi Meïr<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Eruvin</i> one follows R. Meïr that <i>eruv</i> for courtyards and participation for alleys must be separate acts, Chapter 6, Note 99; in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 2:4:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.2.4.3"><i>Megillah</i> 2:1, Note 62</a>, he requires that the Esther scroll has to be read from beginning to end; Babli 72a. These rules are popular usage, not rabbinic decrees.</i>.
Rebbi Ze`ira, Rebbi Ḥiyya, Rebbi Joshua ben Levi in the name of Bar Pedaya: Why did the verse join the chapter of the <i>nazir</i> to the chapter of lifting the hands<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">The rules of the <i>nazir</i> are <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:1-21" href="/Numbers.6.1-21"><i>Num</i>. 6:1–21</a> and those of the priestly blessing 6:22–27.</i>? To teach you that just as the <i>nazir</i> is forbidden wine so lifting the hands is forbidden wine. Then since the <i>nazir</i> is forbidden skins and kernels, also lifting the hands has to be forbidden skins and kernels<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">But there is no prohibition for priests serving in the Temple to eat grapes and non-alcoholic grape products.</i>. Rebbi Jonah said, Joshua the son of the Circumciser and Rebbi Ze`ira disagreed. One infers it from the <i>nazir</i>, the other infers it from Temple service. But we do not know who inferred it from the <i>nazir</i> and who inferred it from Temple service. For him who inferred it from the <i>nazir</i>, since the <i>nazir</i> is forbidden skins and kernels, also lifting the hands has to be forbidden skins and kernels. For him who inferred it from Temple service, since the service is forbidden to bodily defective persons, so lifting the hands has to be forbidden to bodily defective persons<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Which is shown also to be not applicable to the priestly blessing.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The following is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 4:8:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.4.8.2"><i>Megillah</i>, Halakhah 4:8</a>(<b>מ</b>).</i> But was it not stated, if he was known in his town he is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 24b" href="/Megillah.24b">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 24b</a>.</i>? As the following: The finger of Rebbi Naftali was bent<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">In the quote of this passage by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Megillah 24b:12:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Megillah.24b.12.1">Tosaphot <i>Megillah</i> 24b <i>s.v</i>. אם</a>: A Cohen with deformed hands came before Rebbi Naftali.</i>. He came and asked Rebbi Mana, who said to him, since you are known in your town it is permitted. Rav Ḥuna disqualified one with sparse facial hair. But was it not stated, if he was known in his town he is permitted? Rebbi Mana said, it was a holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Megillah:</i> he had short legs.</i>; so they should not say, we saw a minor lifting his hands<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Since as explained later, reciting the priestly blessing is a biblical command, it cannot be performed by an underaged Cohen.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, this<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">The statement on the Mishnah in <i>Megillah</i> that a Cohen with stained hands may not lift them for the priestly blessing.</i> implies that one is forbidden to look at the Cohanim at the moment when they are blessing. Rebbi Ḥaggai, when they said, one does not look, was it not because of inattention<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">The person blessed can benefit from the blessing only if his mind is concentrated on the Heavenly blessing.</i>? By Moses, I shall look and my attention will not be diverted.
From where the lifting of hands? <i>So you shall bless the Children of Israel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:22" href="/Numbers.6.22"><i>Num</i>. 6:22</a>.</i>. So far during the morning prayers<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Since in the Temple the priestly blessing was recited at the time of the morning sacrifice, the inspiration for the morning prayer service.</i>. At <i>musaf</i>? <i>Aaron lifted his hands for the people</i><sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 9:22" href="/Leviticus.9.22"><i>Lev</i>. 9:22</a>, description of the special inauguration service of the Tabernacle.</i>. Is not this verse distorted? Should it not read: <i>he descended from making the purification sacrifice, and the elevation sacrifice, and the well-being sacrifice</i>, and after this, <i>Aaron lifted his hands for the people</i>? But it teaches<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">The verse mentioning blessing before descent.</i> that while descending from the altar he lifted his hands and blessed the people. <sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 38a" href="/Sotah.38a">Babli <i>Sotah</i>38a</a>.</i><i>And he blessed them</i>, standing. I could think, not while standing. The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 21:5" href="/Deuteronomy.21.5"><i>Deut</i>. 21:5</a>.</i>, <i>the Eternal, your God, selected them to serve Him and to bless in His Name</i>. It combines blessing with service. Since service is done standing, also blessing is done standing. And so it says<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 30:27" href="/II_Chronicles.30.27"><i>2Chr</i>. 30:27</a>.</i>, <i>the Levitic Cohanim rose and blessed the people</i>. The verse speaks of the generation of Ezechias, when they toiled in the Torah. But in other generations, when they were serving foreign worship, what does it say? <i>When you spread your hands my eyes shall disregard you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 1:15" href="/Isaiah.1.15"><i>Is</i>. 1:15</a>.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:22" href="/Numbers.6.22"><i>Num</i>. 6:22</a>.</i><i>And he blessed them</i>, any blessing. But we did not hear which it was until the verse came and explained it<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:24-26" href="/Numbers.6.24-26"><i>Num</i>. 6:24–26</a>.</i>: <i>The Eternal shall bless you and guard you. The Eternal shall enlighten His presence to you and show you favor. The Eternal shall turn His presence to you and give you peace</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">From here to the end of the Halakhah the text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 4:1:22-33" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.4.1.22-33"><i>Berakhot</i> 4:1, Notes 64–124</a> (<b>ב</b>).</i> From where Ne`ilah<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ne`ilah</i>, a synagogue service close to sundown.</i>? Rebbi [Levi]<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from <i>Berakhot</i>.</i> said: <i>Even if you prolong your prayers I shall not hear</i><sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 1:15" href="/Isaiah.1.15"><i>Is</i>. 1:15</a>.</i>. From here that everyone who increases his prayers will be answered<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Since Isaiah presents this as a particular curse, it follows that as a rule people will be heard if they increase their prayers.</i>. The argument of Rebbi Levi is inverted. There says Rebbi Abba the son of Rebbi Pappai, Rebbi Joshua of Sikhnin in the name of Rebbi Levi: <i>In all excitement there is something superfluous; and the word of the lips is but for deficit</i><sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 14:23" href="/Proverbs.14.23"><i>Prov</i>. 14:23</a>.</i>. Hannah, because she prayed too long, reduced the years of Samuel because she said, <i>he shall dwell there forever</i><sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 1:22" href="/I_Samuel.1.22"><i>1Sam</i>. 1:22</a>; not part of Hannah’s prayer but a statement to her husband.</i> but “forever” for a Levite is only 50 years, as it is written: <i>at age fifty he should return from the worshipping hosts</i><sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 8:25" href="/Numbers.8.25"><i>Num</i>. 8:25</a>.</i>. But in fact it was 52<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Not a biblical statement but an inference of <i>Seder Olam</i> Chapter 13 (in the author’s edition pp. 134–135.)</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said two years until she weaned him. And here you say so? One for private, the other for public prayers. Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, Rebbi Simeon bar Ḥalaphta in the name of Rebbi Meïr: <i>when she prayed very long</i><sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1 Sam</i>. 1:12.</i>; it follows that everyone who extends his prayers will be answered<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">Denied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 32b" href="/Berakhot.32b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 32b</a>.</i>.
Until when is <i>Ne`ilah</i>? The rabbis of Caesarea say: Rav and Rebbi Joḥanan disagree. Rav said, when the gates of Heaven are locked<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">It is not clear when the Gates of Heaven are locked. Maybe it is at sundown when the sun disappears, but it is more likely sometime after that when on a very clear day one may notice a sudden darkening of the sky in the middle of the gradual dusk. The gates of the Temple were locked for the public at the time of the lighting of the candelabra in the Sanctuary, which must be before sundown.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan: when the gates of the Temple are locked. Rebbi Yudan Antordaya said, the Mishnah supports Rebbi Joḥanan: “On three occasions do the Cohanim lift their hands four times in one day, mornings, <i>Musaph, Minḥah</i>, and at the locking of the gates.” May you say that the gates of heaven are locked while it is still daytime<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Since the priestly blessing may be recited only during daytime, the “locking of the gates” mentioned in the Mishnah must have been during daytime and cannot have been in the night.</i>?
The maternal uncle of Rebbi Ada had rolled up the kaftan of Rav on the great fast. He said to him: When you see the sun on the top of the date palms, give me my kaftan so that we may pray the Locking of the Gates. The argument of Rav is inverted. There he says “the locking of the Gates of Heaven” and here he says “the locking of the gates of the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">Since the sun is on the top of the date palms quite some time before sunset, Rav cannot possibly pray at the Locking of the Gates of Heaven. Hence, his actions contradict his teachings.</i>.” Rebbi Mattanah said: Since Rav needed a lot of time to pray, he reached the Locking of the Gates of Heaven.
May Ne`ilah free one from evening prayers? Rebbi Abba, Rav Ḥuna in the name of Rav: Ne`ilah frees one from evening prayers<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">According to Rav’s original opinion that one prays at the Locking of the Gates of Heaven, Ne`ilah may be started only when evening prayers may already be said. It does not make sense to recite two different prayers at the same time.</i>. Rebbi Abba said to Rav Ḥuna: How may he mention <i>havdalah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">At the end of Sabbath or holiday work is permitted only if <i>havdalah</i> (“distinction”) was recited, preferably in the evening Amidah. Hence, Rav’s decision seems to be impossible.</i>? Rebbi Jonah said to Rebbi Abba: How may seven free one from eighteen<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">The seven benedictions of the holiday Amidah cannot accommodate the 18 of the weekday prayers.</i>? He said to him, did I not already contradict it? He said to him: Because you contradicted it, should it be abandoned? Rebbi Yose said, what Rebbi Abba asked is truly difficult. What Rebbi Jonah asked is not at all difficult; they made it easy on people because of the fast, that seven should free one from eighteen. Rebbi Abba bar Mamal said to his colleagues: From all of them I understand that Ne`ilah does not free one from evening prayers. Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi &lt;joshua ben&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Added from the text in <i>Berakhot</i>. R. Levi was a popular preacher, neither a legal authority nor a teacher of R. Simon.</i> Levi: Ne`ilah does not free one from evening prayers. Rebbi Yose bar Abun said: Did not Rebbi Ḥiyya state this? “Every day one prays eighteen benedictions, including the end of Sabbath, end of Yom Kippur, and end of public fast days.<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">Fast days in a drought.</i>”
<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">While this paragraph also is in <i>Berakhot</i>, the text there is in very bad shape and not directly comparable to the text here.</i> Rebbi Isaac bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: If the Day of Atonement happens to be on the Sabbath, one mentions Sabbath in <i>Ne`ilah</i> even though there is no <i>Ne`ilah</i> for Sabbath<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 24b" href="/Shabbat.24b">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 24b</a> in the name of R. Joshua ben Levi.</i>. Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: On a Sabbath that falls on Ḥanukkah, one mentions Ḥanukkah for <i>Musaf</i> even though there is no <i>Musaf</i> for Ḥanukkah<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 24a" href="/Shabbat.24a">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 24a</a>.</i>. They added to it: If the New Moon happens to be on a public fast-day, one mentions the New Moon in <i>Ne`ilah</i> even though there is no <i>Ne`ilah</i> for the New Moon. When the New Moon falls on a fast-day, how does one mention the New Moon? Rebbi Ze`ira said, in “thanksgiving”. Rebbi Abba bar Mamal said, in “Temple service”. Rebbi Abuna said, one says it as the fourth benediction<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">These sentences are difficult to understand and the greatest authorities of the Middle Ages, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 32b" href="/Berakhot.32b">Rashba on Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 32b</a> and Rosh to <i>Berakhot</i> Chap. 5, #10 felt compelled to emend the text. Since three of the four prayers of the New Moon are weekday prayers with an addition added in “Temple service” (the 16th benediction in the Yerushalmi version) as prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 5:2:2-16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.5.2.2-16"><i>Berakhot</i> 5:2</a>, the only question can be about <i>Musaf</i>. However, we never hear that the particular inserts in the morning prayers of a fast day were recited also for <i>Musaf</i>. On the other hand, as Rosh points out, the previous paragraph certainly implies that the עֲנֵנוּ prayer recited on all fast-days except Yom Kippur, not only on those for rain, must be recited also for <i>Musaf</i> since the day requires that the text be inserted in all prayers. One may at least understand the position of Rebbi Abba that on a fast day for rain which coincides with a day of the New Moon, one recites the usual <i>Musaf</i> with an additional fifth benediction which deals with the fast day, after the fourth for the New Moon. The dissenting opinions of Rebbis Ze`ira and Abba bar Mamal seem to imply that <i>Musaf</i> on a fast day consisted of the introductory and final benedictions that are common to all prayers and the additional benedictions for the fast day, whereas the section on the New Moon, for which <i>Musaf</i> is recited in the first place, is moved from its regular place to an insert in either the 16th or the 17th (“thanksgiving”) benediction.</i>. Rebbi Abba said, since we find everywhere that one says it as the fourth benediction, here also as the fourth benediction. And so it was acted upon according to Rebbi Abba<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">A reported action on an opinion is the best proof that this is accepted practice.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">In addition to the text in <i>Berakhot</i>, this paragraph is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 2:14:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.2.14.2"><i>Ta`aniot</i> Halakhah 2:15, Notes 241–245</a>.</i> And what does one read? Rebbi Yose said, one reads “blessings and curses.” Rebbi Mana said to him, since they know it is a fast day they are falling on their bellies, do they not know that it is a fast day? He said to him, to tell you that one reads “blessings and curses.” Rebbi Yudan from Kappadokia said before Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Jehudah bar Pazi, one reads about the New Moon. Rebbi Yose met Rebbi Jehudah bar Pappai; he said to him, did you hear this from your father? He said to him, my father said this only about Eintab. Since they know that it is the New Moon, they are reading about the New Moon. At all other places they are reading “blessings and curses.”
Jeremiah the Scribe asked before (Rav) &lt;rebbi&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The reading “Rebbi” from <i>Berakhot</i> is the only one possible. The question could have been asked only in Palestine with its 3½ year cycle, when no more than one Torah scroll was removed from the Ark at any time. In Babylonia, place of Rav Jeremiah, with its tight one-year cycle, all exceptional readings always were done with a second scroll read by the <i>maftir</i>.</i> Jeremiah: What does one read if the day of the New Moon is a Sabbath? He said to him: One reads about the New Moon. Rebbi Ḥelbo said before Rebbi Immi: The Mishnah says so: “One interrupts for everything, for New Moons, for Ḥanukkah, and for Purim.”
Isaac the trader asked Rebbi Isaac: What does one read on a New Moon that falls on Ḥanukkah? He said to him: Three for the New Moon and one for Ḥanukkah. Rebbi Phineas, Rebbi Simon, Rebbi Abba bar Zamina brought it in the name of Rebbi Eudaimon of Haifa: Three read of Ḥanukka and one of the New Moon, to tell you that the fourth one comes only because of the New Moon<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 3:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.3.5.1">Mishna <i>Megillah</i> 3:6</a>.</i>. Bar Shelemiah the scribe asked Rebbi Mana: Think of it, if the New Moon of Ḥanukkah falls on a Sabbath, do not seven read? How can you say, to tell you that the fourth one comes only because of the New Moon? He said to him: That is a true question of a scribe<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Usually on Ḥanukkah only three people read from the Torah since it is a regular workday. On the day of the New Moon, four persons read since it is a day with a <i>Musaf</i> sacrifice in the Temple. On the Sabbath, seven read (and the <i>maftir</i> reads one additional portion). Hence, it seems impossible that the fourth person should read about Ḥanukkah.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">The text appears in modified form also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bereishit Rabbah 8:10" href="/Bereishit_Rabbah.8.10"><i>Gen. rabba</i> 8:10</a>, <i>Pesiqta rabbati</i> 23; the parallel in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 27b" href="/Berakhot.27b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 27b</a> disagrees fundamentally with the practice explained here.</i> Rebbi commanded (Abba who was) his speaker &lt;abdan&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that his name was Abba Yudan; therefore both the version here and that in <i>Berakhot</i> are acceptable.</i>: Proclaim before them that he who wants to pray, should pray evening prayers as long as it is still daylight<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">According to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 4:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.4.1.1">Mishnah <i>Berakhot</i> 4:1</a>, the time of afternoon prayers is until 5/4 hours before sundown for Rebbi Jehudah and until sundown for the other Sages. As a corollary, the time of evening prayers starts at 5/4 hours before sundown for Rebbi Jehudah and at sundown for the others. Since Rebbi was a student of Rebbi Jehudah, it seems that he followed his teacher and himself was followed by his own student R. Ḥiyya. It is assumed here that we already know the result of the next paragraph, that evening prayer is not obligatory (this is also accepted in the Babli), and that because of this one permits evening prayer before sundown because it is a minor obligation and in Galilee apparently was not recited in the synagogue. [The Babli states that evening prayers should be said in the night, that this is also Rebbi’s position as reported in the Babli, but that in case of error, under very dark clouds, one does not have to repeat the prayer which in Babylonia was recited in the synagogue.]</i>. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">This R. Ḥiyya bar Abba is not the student of R. Joḥanan who usually is called by this name but Rebbi’s student R. Ḥiyya (the Elder) bar Abba bar Aḥa Karsala.</i> commanded his speaker: Proclaim before them that he who wants to pray should pray evening prayers as long as it is still daylight. Rebbi Ḥanina said: Rebbi Ismael ben Rebbi Yose drew me to an inn and said to me: Here my father prayed Sabbath {Friday night} prayers on Friday. Rebbi Immi said: Rebbi Joḥanan disagrees<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">As Levi Ginzberg explains, it seems from Mishnah <i>Berakhot</i> that originally there were 5 prayer times every day, 3 times for the Amidah prayer and twice for the recitation of the <i>Shema`</i>. R. Joḥanan is the first Amora who requires that the recitation of the <i>Shema`</i>, whose times are determined differently from those of the <i>Amidah</i>, nevertheless be combined with the <i>Amidah</i> in that the benediction following the recitation be the introduction to the <i>Amidah</i>. Since the time of the evening <i>Shema`</i> is in the night proper, he has to oppose an early recitation.</i> but he should not have disagreed since one adds from the profane to the holy time; in addition, donkey drivers come from Arab<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">The village of Arrabeh, North of Kafr Kanah in lower Galilee.</i> to Sepphoris and say, Rebbi Ḥanina ben Dosa already did consecrate the Sabbath in his town. But so it has been said, that Rebbi Ḥanina said: Rebbi Ismael ben Rebbi Yose drew me to an inn and said to me, here my father prayed Saturday night prayers on the Sabbath<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">To say weekday prayers on the Sabbath certainly is possible only if the time allotted to the prayer is dissociated from actual time.</i>. But even with that he should not have disagreed, since Rebbi commanded his speaker Abdan: Proclaim before them that he who wants to pray should pray evening prayers as long as it is still daylight. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">This R. Ḥiyya bar Abba is not the student of R. Joḥanan who usually is called by this name but Rebbi’s student R. Ḥiyya (the Elder) bar Abba bar Aḥa Karsala.</i> commanded his speaker: Proclaim before them that he who wants to pray should pray evening prayers as long as it is still daylight. In the house of Rebbi Yannai they said: If a man went to bed, one does not bother him to get up. Rebbi Ze`ira said, all the time that I followed this rule, I was afraid in the night. You have only what Rebbi commanded his speaker Abdan: Proclaim before them that he who wants to pray should pray evening prayers as long as it is still daylight. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba commanded his speaker: Proclaim before them that he who wants to pray should pray evening prayers as long as it is still daylight.
Rebbi Jacob bar Abba said: There, they did state, what is the status of evening prayer? Rabban Gamliel said, it is obligatory. Rebbi Joshua said, it is voluntary<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">In a dispute between R. Joshua and Rabban Gamliel, practice should follow R. Joshua. But there is never a doubt that the recitation of <i>Shema`</i> in the night is obligatory, and as stated before, evening prayers are still needed for mental health. In addition, following R. Joḥanan’s later combination of <i>shema`</i> and prayer, the recitation of the <i>shema`</i> induces the obligation of the <i>Amidah</i>, which makes the dispute almost moot. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 27b" href="/Berakhot.27b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 27b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanina said, this difference parallels the other difference: He who holds that evening prayer is obligatory, holds that <i>Ne`ilah</i> does not free one from evening prayers. He who holds that it is voluntary, holds that <i>Ne`ilah</i> frees one from evening prayers.
<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">The story of this dispute should be compared with the Babli version, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 27b" href="/Berakhot.27b"><i>Berakhot</i> 27b</a>, where R. Joshua’s profession is given as a charcoal burner. Since Rabban Gamliel in the aftermath of the destruction of the Temple insisted not only on uniformity of practice but also of doctrine (and in this was successful in eliminating Sadduceeism) and R. Joshua was known for his dislike of public quarrels, Rabban Gamliel thought that he was taking little risk in provoking a quarrel.</i> It happened that one student came and asked Rebbi Joshua: What is about evening prayer? He said to him: It is voluntary. He asked Rabban Gamliel: What is about evening prayer? He said to him: It is obligatory. He said to him: But Rebbi Joshua told me that it was voluntary. He said to him: Tomorrow, when I enter the assembly hall, stand up and ask me about this practice. The next day, this student stood up and asked Rabban Gamliel: What is about evening prayer? He said to him: It is obligatory. He said to him: But Rebbi Joshua told me that it was voluntary. Rabban Gamliel said to Rebbi Joshua: Are you the one who says it is voluntary? He answered him: No. He said to him: Stand up on your feet so that they may testify against you. Then Rabban Gamliel was sitting down and lecturing while Rebbi Joshua was standing up until the people started talking and said to Rebbi Ḥuṣpit the interpreter: Send the people home. They said to Rebbi Zenon the <i>ḥazan</i>: Start<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">The ḥazan was not only the reader in congregational prayers, but also the general organizer of religious affairs. In outlying communities he was the ritual slaughterer and the conduit through whom questions of religious practice were addressed to the Academies. Here it seems that he had to recite the prayer at the end of a study which it was customary to start with a Bible verse and that the people spontaneously chose one which was a curse on the speaker.</i>! He said: Start! All the people stood up and said to him: <i>Certainly, on whom did your evil not pass always</i><sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nahum 3:19" href="/Nahum.3.19"><i>Nah</i>. 3:19</a>.</i>? They immediately appointed Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah to the Yeshivah when he was 16 years old; his head became all white. Rebbi Aqiba sat and was sad; he said, not that he is a greater Torah scholar than I am, but he comes from a greater family than I do; hail to the man whose forefathers created merit for him, hail to the man who has a peg to hang on to. What was Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah’s peg? He was the tenth generation after Ezra<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">Also he was very rich and could afford the expenses of representing the Jewish population before the Roman government.</i>. How many seats were there? Rebbi Jacob ben Sisi said: Eighty seats were there of accomplished scholars, not to count those standing behind the railing. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said 300 were there, not to count those standing behind the railing. As we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Zevachim 1:3" href="/Mishnah_Zevachim.1.3">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 1:3</a>.</i>: “On the day Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah was appointed to the Academy.” There we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 4:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.4.6.1">Mishnah <i>Ketubot</i> 4:6</a>.</i>: “This inference did Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah present before the Sages at the vineyard of Jabneh.” Was there a vineyard? It means that the scholars sat there in rows like vines in a vineyard. Rabban Gamliel went immediately to pacify each one in his house. He came to Rebbi Joshua and found him occupied with the making of needles. He asked him: This is how you earn your living? He answered him: Until now you did not know? Woe to the generation whose caretaker you are! He said to him: I humble myself before you. They sent a washerman to Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah, but some say that it was Rebbi Aqiba. He told him: The sprinkler, son of a sprinkler, should sprinkle. Should anyone who is neither a sprinkler nor the son of a sprinkler say to the sprinkler: your water is water from a cave and your ashes are ashes from a fireplace? He said to him: You made your peace with him! I and you shall go in the morning to Rabban Gamliel’s door. Nevertheless they did not remove him from his dignity but made him head of the court.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> These are the bystanders. <i>Command the Children of Israel: My sacrifice, My offering as My gift</i><sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:2" href="/Numbers.28.2"><i>Num</i>. 28:2</a>.</i>. How could a person’s sacrifice be offered not in his presence<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The daily sacrifices commanded in the verse are paid by the yearly <i>sheqel</i>, which was not paid by Cohanim (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 1:4:6-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.1.4.6-7"><i>Šeqalim</i> 1:6</a>). Therefore the officiating Cohanim are not the owners of the sacrifice; a representation of the taxpayers is needed.</i>? But the earlier prophets<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">David and Samuel.</i> instituted 24 watches. For each watch there was a presence<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">A scheduled presence.</i> in Jerusalem of priests, and of Levites, and of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">The Land was divided into 24 districts, centered around the cities of priests.</i>. At the time of service of each watch, its priests and Levites come to Jerusalem, and Israel belonging to this watch congregate in their towns and read about Creation<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">In contrast to all other times when there is a Torah reading only on Mondays and Thursdays, during the week of service there is a daily reading, also some fasting, and other changes in the regular service as described in the Halakhot.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It would only have been necessary: “These are the bystanders; they congregate in their towns and read about Creation<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">The reason the bystanders are mentioned in the Mishnah is the special fasts which they organize. Since it was stated earlier that the priests on duty in the Temple do not fast on minor fastdays, the mention of Cohanim and Levites in this context seems superfluous. They are only mentioned because without sacrifices to be offered by the non-owning Cohanim there would be no need for bystanders.</i>.” He comes to start from the beginning of the subject.
<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">This text and the following paragraphs are copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 4:1:2-14" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.4.1.2-14"><i>Pesaḥim</i> 4:1</a>.</i> Rebbi Jonah said, these daily sacrifices are the offerings of all of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is shown in <i>Pesaḥim</i> that during the offering of a sacrifice the owner is forbidden work, no man in Israel would be permitted to work both in the morning and in the evening.</i>. Could all of Israel ascend to Jerusalem? Is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 16:16" href="/Deuteronomy.16.16"><i>Deut</i>. 16:16</a>.</i>, <i>three times a year all your males shall be seen</i>? If all of Israel would sit there and do nothing, is there not written<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 11:14" href="/Deuteronomy.11.14"><i>Deut</i>. 11:14</a>. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 35b" href="/Berakhot.35b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 35b</a> infers from the verse that it is a religious obligation on a Torah scholar to earn a livelihood.</i>, <i>you shall harvest your grain</i>? Who would harvest their grain? But the early prophets instituted 24 watches; from each watch there were [Cohanim, Levites, and Israel] present in Jerusalem. It was stated, <i>twenty-four thousand</i><sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 27:1" href="/I_Chronicles.27.1"><i>1Chr</i>. 27:1</a>. The verse is read as meaning that every month there were 24’000 representatives of the people at the Temple.</i>. A stand-by group<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Cohanim were changed every week, the people’s representatives also were changed every week; only one quarter of the 24’000 on stand-by were actually needed for one week. The Babylonian term for עָמוּד is מַעֲמָד (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 27a" href="/Taanit.27a">Babli 27a</a>). The actual numbers in Second Temple times were small.</i> from Jerusalem, and half a stand-by group from Jericho. Jericho also could have produced a full stand-by group, but to give precedence to Jerusalem it only produced half a stand-by group. The Cohanim for service, the Levites for the podium<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">For the musical accompaniment of the Temple service.</i>, and the Israel as proof that they are the agents for all of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">These are forbidden any work while the Daily Sacrifice is offered but everybody else may work.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">The first sentence is also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 10:12:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.10.12.3"><i>Eruvin</i> 10 (Note 141</a>). The text there reads “musical instruments”, which is required by the context there and must be understood here also since the choir is subsumed under “Levites”.</i> It was stated: “Rebbi Simeon<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">In the other sources: R. Simeon ben Eleazar.</i> said, Cohanim, Levites, Israel, and song invalidate the sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">A sacrifice requiring a wine offering is invalid if not accompanied by the Levite’s song.</i>.” Rebbi Abun<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">In the other sources: Abbin.</i> in the name of Rebbi Eleazar, the reason of Rebbi Simeon ben Eleazar: <sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 29:28" href="/II_Chronicles.29.28"><i>2Chr</i>. 29:28</a>. Since this is not a pentateuchal verse it only can prove what people did or, as explained there in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 29:25" href="/II_Chronicles.29.25">v. 25</a>, what was prophetic instruction.</i><i>The entire congregation were bowing down</i>, these are Israel, <i>and the song was sung</i>, these are the Levites, <i>and the trumpets were trumpeting</i>, these are the Cohanim, <i>everything up to the end of the elevation offering</i>, all are indispensable for the sacrifice. Rebbi Tanḥuma in the name of Rebbi Eleazar understood it from here<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">Num. 8:19.</i>: <i>And I gave the Levites to Aaron and his sons from the midst of the Children of Israel</i>, these are the Levites, <i>to work the service of the Children of Israel in the Tent of Meeting,</i> these are the Cohanim, <i>and to atone for the Children of Israel</i>, that is the song<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 8:19" href="/Numbers.8.19"><i>Num</i>. 8:19</a>.</i>, <i>so there shall be no plague when the Children of Israel approach the Sanctuary</i>, these are Israel.
From where that the song is called atonement? Ḥinena the father of Bar Nata in the name of Rebbi Banaia: <i>and to atone for the Children of Israel</i>, that is the song. From where that the song invalidates? Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Simeon βουλευτής <sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">“The city councillor”.</i>, in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina, <i>and to atone for the Children of Israel</i>, that is the song.
Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Moses instituted eight watches, four from Eleazar and four from Ithamar<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 27a" href="/Taanit.27a">Babli 27a</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 3:2" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).3.2">Tosephta 3:2</a>.</i>, until David and Samuel the Seer added another eight, four from Eleazar and four from Ithamar. They wanted to add another eight to bring them to 24, and found from Eleazar but did not find from Ithamar. This is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 24:4" href="/I_Chronicles.24.4"><i>1Chr</i>. 24:4</a>.</i>: <i>it was found that the descendants of Eleazar were more heads than the descendants of Ithamar</i>, etc. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, the Elder Rebbi Ḥuna from Sepphoris in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: <i>One clan, one clan selected from Eleazar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 24:6" href="/I_Chronicles.24.6"><i>1Chr</i>. 24:6</a>. The repetition is not in the MT.</i>, other clans were added for him; <i>and selected, selected for Ithamar</i>, what he had, he had. Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rav Ḥuna: <i>For Ḥezir, seventeen</i><sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 24:15" href="/I_Chronicles.24.15"><i>1Chr</i>. 24:15</a>. It is claimed that ranks 1–8, 17–24 in the cycle of watches are from Eleazar.</i>. The cycle came back to Eleazar.
<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">This text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:8:2-8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.8.2-8"><i>Sukkah</i> 5:8</a>, explaining the discrimination against the Bilgah watch.</i> One could not make them 23, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 9:22" href="/I_Chronicles.9.22"><i>1Chr</i>. 9:22</a>.</i>, <i>these are the institutions of David and Samuel the Seer in their professionalism</i>. It was a great feat of professionalism that no watch was taking and repeating in inheritance fields before the other could take<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">It is prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:21" href="/Leviticus.27.21"><i>Lev</i>. 27:21</a> that real estate dedicated to the Temple by a person whose ancestor received this land in the original distribution under Joshua and which is not redeemed by the next Jubilee becomes property of the Cohanim. This is read to mean that it becomes property of the watch which regularly is on duty on the day of Atonement in the Jubilee year (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 25:9" href="/Leviticus.25.9"><i>Lev</i>. 25:9</a>). (Property bought, not inherited, <i>must</i> be redeemed, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:23-24" href="/Leviticus.27.23-24"><i>Lev</i>. 27:23–24</a>.)
