It now is asserted that no watch repeats serving on the Day of Atonement in a Jubilee year after less than 24 Jubilee periods (or 1200 years.) Since we have no details about the calendar rules of the First Temple period, at the end of which the rules of original distribution became moot, the statement can be neither verified nor falsified.</i>. Rebbi Abbahu said, I computed it that no watch was taking and repeating in inheritance fields before the other could take.
Four watches returned from the Diaspora: Yedaya, Ḥarim, Pashḥur, and Immer<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:36-39" href="/Ezra.2.36-39"><i>Ezra</i> 2:36–39</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:39-42" href="/Nehemiah.7.39-42"><i>Neh.</i> 7:39–42</a>.</i>. The prophets among them stipulated that even if Yehoyariv would return from the Diaspora that it would not displace the watch taking its place but would be made an appendix to it<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence should be deleted; its place is at later in the text.</i>. The prophets among them took the initiative and made 24 lots which they put in an urn. Yedaya came and took five; with his own this makes six<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">The 24 watches which served in the Second Temple were really subdivisions of the four which returned from Babylonia.</i>. Ḥarim came and took five; with his own this makes six. [Pashḥur came and took five; with his own this makes six. Immer came and took five; with his own this makes six.] The prophets among them stipulated that even if Yehoyariv<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">The leading watch in <i>Chr</i>.</i> would return from the Diaspora that it would not displace the watch taking its place but would be made an appendix to it. The heads of the watches took the initiative and made themselves heads of clans. There were watches containing five, six, seven, eight, or nine. For a watch containing five, three were sacrificing during three days and two were sacrificing during four days<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 2:11:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.2.11.1">Mishnah 2:12</a>, each clan served one day during the week allotted to its watch. That Mishnah seemed to presume that each watch is composed of exactly 7 clans. But numbers from 5 to 9 can be accommodated.</i>. For a watch containing six, five were sacrificing during five days and one was sacrificing during two days. For a watch containing seven, each single one was sacrificing on its day. For a watch containing eight, six were sacrificing during six days, and two were sacrificing on one day. For a watch containing nine, five were sacrificing during five days and four were sacrificing during two days. There were those who fixed themselves permanently. A watch<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">One has to read “clan” instead of “watch”.</i> who served on the Sabbath always served on the Sabbath, after the end of the Sabbath always served after the Sabbath. They were those of them which were sacrificing with every watch<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence is slightly garbled. It seems to mean: There were those which were serving at different days each time their watch was called to Jerusalem.</i>; and those who drew lots for every week<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">There were watches which organized a drawing of lots among their clans. Because of the different meanings of “week” this either means every time their watch was going to officiate, or once in a Sabbatical period.</i>.
Rebbi used to ordain double ordinations<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">This ordination was not simply the granting of an ecclesiastical degree but carried with it the appointment as <i>Ḥakham</i> to a rabbinic post which it was the Patriarch’s duty to see to it that it was filled.</i>. If they were worthy of it they were continuing; if not they were disappearing<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">If those appointed by Rebbi were found worthy of the posts given to them in the eyes of heaven, they lived a long life; otherwise they would die an early death.</i>. When he was to die, he commanded his son; he said, do not act thus but ordain all of them together, and ordain Rebbi Ḥama bar Ḥanina<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">One has to read either simply Ḥanina (as in the parallel <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kohelet Rabbah 7:16" href="/Kohelet_Rabbah.7.16"><i>Eccl. rabba</i> 7(16</a>)) or Ḥanina bar Ḥama (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Ketubot 103b" href="/Ketubot.103b">Babli <i>Ketubot</i>103b</a>). As the name Ḥama shows and the story confirms, he was a Babylonian (Babylonian Aramaic from the Accadic ח֗מי “to protect, guard, trust”.)</i> first. Why did he not ordain him himself? Rebbi Derosa said, because the Sepphoreans complained about him<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">That he was too strict in his rabbinic rulings, being a recognized scholar but not appointed by the Patriarch.</i>. And because of complaints one acts? Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Yose said, because he corrected him in public. Rebbi was sitting, stating: <i>Their refugees will remember Me</i><sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 7:9" href="/Ezekiel.7.9"><i>Ez</i>. 7:9</a>.</i><i>, on the mountains like valley doves, all of them cooing</i><sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 7:16" href="/Ezekiel.7.16"><i>Ez</i>. 7:16</a>. For “cooing”, Rebbi used rabbinic Hebrew <i>hōmiōt</i>.</i>. He said to him, <i>all of them cooing</i><sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">In correct biblical Hebrew (almost MT) <i>hōmōt</i>.</i>. He asked him, where did you study this text? He said, before the Babylonian Rav Hamnuna. He said to him, if you will descend there, tell him that he should ordain you as <i>Ḥakham</i>. He understood that he<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">R. Ḥanina understood that he would not become <i>Ḥakham</i> in Rebbi’s lifetime.</i> never would be ordained in his lifetime. After he died, his son wanted to ordain him, but he did not accept to be ordained unless Rebbi Ephes the Southerner was ordained before him. There was there an old man who said, if Ḥanina precedes me, I have to be the second; if Rebbi Ephes the Southerner precedes me, I have to be the second. Rebbi Ḥanina accepted to be ordained as third<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">According to both parallel sources he agreed to be the third in rank in the Academy of Rebbi’s successor.</i>.
Rebbi Ḥanina said, I merited to live a long life. Whether because of this matter I do not know, or whether when I was climbing from Tiberias to Sepphoris I made a detour to ask about the well-being of Rebbi Simeon ben Ḥalfuta I do not know.
Samuel and those of the family Shilo asked about the Patriarch’s well-being every day; those of the family Shilo entered first and sat down first. They honored Samuel and brought him in first. Rav immigrated from there and Samuel honored him [and brought him in first.] Those of the House of Shilo said, we are the second ones. Samuel accepted to sit as third<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">According to both parallel sources he agreed to be the third in rank in the Academy of Rebbi’s successor.</i>.
Three scrolls were found in the Temple courtyard<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">It is asserted that even before the work of the Masoretes, the received text of the Pentateuch was a scholarly edition.</i>, the <i>Meone</i> scroll, the <i>Zaatute</i> scroll, the <i>hee</i> scroll. In one they found written <i>me`ôn is the preexisting God</i>, but in two was written <i>me`ônāh is the preexisting God</i><sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 33:26" href="/Deuteronomy.33.26"><i>Deut</i>. 33:26</a>.</i>. They confirmed the two and annulled the one. In one they found written <i>he sent the za`</i><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i>tûtē of the Children of Israel</i> but in two was written <i>he sent the na`</i><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i>rē of the Children of Israel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 24:5" href="/Exodus.24.5"><i>Ex</i>. 24:5</a>. The LXX translate <i>za`</i><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i>tûtē</i>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 9a" href="/Megillah.9a">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 9a</a>, bottom) as “young men” but <i>na`ar</i> (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 33:11" href="/Exodus.33.11"><i>Ex</i>. 33:11</a>) as “boy”.</i>. They confirmed the two and annulled the one. In one they found written nine היא, but in two they found eleven <sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">This is the accepted <i>mesorah</i>. The irregular spelling is found in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 14:3" href="/Genesis.14.3"><i>Gen</i>. 14:3</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 20:5" href="/Genesis.20.5">20:5</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 38:5" href="/Genesis.38.5">38:5</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 11:39" href="/Leviticus.11.39"><i>Lev</i>. 11:39</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 13:10" href="/Leviticus.13.10">13:10</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 13:21" href="/Leviticus.13.21">13:21</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 16:31" href="/Leviticus.16.31">16:31</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 20:17" href="/Leviticus.20.17">20:17</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:9" href="/Leviticus.21.9">21:9</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 5:13" href="/Numbers.5.13"><i>Num</i>. 5:13</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 5:14" href="/Numbers.5.14">5:14</a>.</i> היא. They confirmed the two and annulled the one.
<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">A parallel text is in <i>Gen</i>. <i>rabba</i> 58(13); M. Sokoloff, <i>The Genizah fragmentss of Genesis rabba</i> (Jerusalem 1982) #110, lines 27–30.</i> Rebbi Levi said, they found a genealogical scroll in Jerusalem and in it was written: Hillel from David, Ben Yaṣaf<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Gen. rabba:</i> the family Yaṣah; in the Genizah: the House Ṣiṣit.</i> from Asaph, Ben Ṣiṣit Hakkeset from Abner, Ben Qubisin<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">In the Genizah: <i>Kobyses</i>.</i> from Ahab, Ben Kalba Savua` from Kaleb<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">These three families are mentioned as the richest of Jerusalem before the first revolt.</i>, Rebbi Yannai from Eli, Men Yehudah<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Gen. rabba:</i> The family Yehu.</i> from Sepphoris, the Elder Rebbi Ḥiyya from the sons of Shephatya ben Abutal<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">A son of David, <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 3:4" href="/II_Samuel.3.4"><i>2S</i>. 3:4</a>.</i>, <sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">The last two late Tannaim are not mentioned in <i>Gen</i>. <i>rabba</i>.</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Ḥalaphta from the sons of Yonadav ben Rekhav, Rebbi Neḥemiah from Nehemiah the governor.
[It was stated:]<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition; essential only in Babylonian style. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Berakhot (Lieberman) 5:5" href="/Tosefta_Berakhot_(Lieberman).5.5">Tosephta <i>Berakhot</i> 5:5</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 46b" href="/Berakhot.46b">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 46b</a>.</i> “The order of lying on couches. If there are two couches, the most important personality [goes and] lies down at the head of the upper one, and the next one next to him<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">In the dining hall (triclinium) two couches were arranged parallel to one another; three couches were arranged in the form of Π. Each couch had room for three occupants.</i>. If they are three couches the most important personality goes and lies down at the head of the middle one; the second one before him and the third one below him. In this way one continues to organize.” Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac said, the Patriarchs are buried in the way of lying on couches<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">Abraham and Sarah in the middle, flanked on one side by Isaac and Rebekka and on the other by Jacob and Leah.</i>.
Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Yasa: The world only continues to exist by the sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">In the absence of a Temple, this means that the daily recitation of the rules of daily sacrifices are necessary for the continued existence of the world. In Amoraic times this implied that the institution of the rules for bystanders to be explained in the following Halakhot was still followed, continuing the cycle of priestly watches uninterrupted theoretically from the time of Ezra (or practically from Hasmonean times.)</i>. There, we stated<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pirkei Avot 1:2" href="/Pirkei_Avot.1.2">Mishnah <i>Avot</i> 1:2</a>.</i>: “Simeon the Just was of the remainders of the Great Assembly. He used to say, the world continues to exist by three things, by the Torah, by worship, and by labors of love<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">Labors for which no thanks can be given, such as burying the dead or giving charity anonymously.</i>” All three are in one verse<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 51:16" href="/Isaiah.51.16"><i>Is</i>. 51:16</a>.</i>: <i>I shall put My word in your mouth</i>, that is Torah. <i>By the shadow of My hands I shall cover you</i>, these are labors of love; to teach you that he who is occupied with Torah and labors of love merits to dwell in the shadow of the Holy One, praise to Him. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 36:8" href="/Psalms.36.8"><i>Ps</i>. 36:8</a>.</i>, <i>how precious is Your grace, o God, and humans take shelter in Your wings’ shadow. To plant the Heavens and give foundation to the earth</i><sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 51:16" href="/Isaiah.51.16"><i>Is</i>. 51:16</a>.</i>, these are the sacrifices, <i>and to say to Zion, you are My people</i>, these are Israel. Rebbi Ḥinena bar Pappa said, we went over all of Scripture and only found this one that Israel was called Zion, <i>and to say to Zion, you are My people</i>. There, we stated<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pirkei Avot 1:18" href="/Pirkei_Avot.1.18">Mishnah <i>Avot</i> 1:18</a>. The following text shows that the verse quoted at the end was not part of the Yerushalmi Mishnah (and is not part of Maimonides’s autograph Mishnah.)</i>: “Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, the world is existing on three things, on justice, on truth, and on peace. All three are one: If justice is done, truth is accomplished. If truth is accomplished, peace is established. Rebbi Mana said, and all are in one verse<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 8:16" href="/Zechariah.8.16"><i>Zach</i>. 8:16</a>.</i>, <i>judge truth and law of peace in your gates</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On Sunday one reads, <i>In the Beginning</i>, <i>there shall be a spread</i>. On Monday, <i>there shall be a spread</i>, <i>the waters shall come together</i>. On Tuesday, <i>the waters shall come together</i>, <i>there shall be lights</i>. On Wednesday, <i>there shall be lights</i>, <i>the water shall swarm</i>. On Thursday, <i>the water shall swarm</i>, <i>the earth shall produce</i>. On Friday, <i>the earth shall produce</i>, <i>the heavens and earth and all their hosts were finished</i><sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">These are the details of the Torah readings by the bystanders mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.2.1">Mishnah 2</a>. The problem is that the Mishnah in <i>Megillah</i> states that three people have to be called to read the Torah, each one a minimum of three verses, and if one starts a new paragraph one must read at least two verses from it, and at the end of a paragraph one must read at least three verses. Every day one reads two paragraphs in the story of Creation (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 1:1-2:3" href="/Genesis.1.1-2.3"><i>Gen.</i>1:1–2:3</a>), but paragraph 1 only has five verses and paragraph 2 three. According to the rules, paragraph 1 should not be split. Similarly, on day 2 paragraph 2 has three verses but paragraph 3 has five, which raise the question how to accommodate second and third readers. The other days are no problem since paragraph 4 has six verses, paragraph 5 four, paragraph 6 eight, and paragraph 9 (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 2:1-3" href="/Genesis.2.1-3"><i>Gen</i>. 2:1–3</a>) three.</i>.<br>A large paragraph is read by two persons, and a small one by an individual<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">A paragraph of 5 sentences may be split into 2 readings as explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.3.2">Halakhah 3</a>.</i> in the morning and for <i>musaf</i>; for afternoon prayers<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">Since there are bystanders 365 days a year, they also hold their special services on days which require a <i>musaf</i> prayer; in contrast to all other Torah readings one reads both after morning and after <i>musaf</i> prayers; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 3:4" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).3.4">Tosephta 3:4</a>.</i> they were assembling and read by heart as one reads the <i>shema`</i>. Friday afternoon they were not assembling<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">For extended services.</i> because of the honor of Sabbath.<br>On any day of <i>hallel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">The first day of Passover, Pentecost, the eight days of Tabernacles and the eight days of Ḥanukkah.</i> there is no bystanding for morning prayers<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">Since these are festive days and the prayers of the bystanders are penitential prayers.</i>, on a <i>musaf</i> sacrifice there is no <i>ne`ilah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">For the same reason as before; most <i>musaf</i> sacrifices were on festive days and <i>ne`ilah</i> is characteristic of fastdays.</i>; on an offering of wood<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">Offerings of firewood to the Temple as described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.4.2">Halakhah 6</a>.</i> there is none for the afternoon prayers, the words of Rebbi Aqiba. Ben Azzai said to him, so was Rebbi Joshua stating: on a <i>musaf</i> sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">When except for the Day of Atonement there can be no <i>ne`ilah</i>.</i> there is none for the afternoon prayers; on an offering of wood no <i>ne`ilah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">Since the day is a festive day.</i>. Rebbi Aqiba changed to state following Ben Azzai’s words.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">This Halakhah is repeated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 4:2:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.4.2.2"><i>Megillah</i> 4:2</a>.</i> Rav Ḥuna said, three people reading in the Torah shall not do less than ten verses<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">Each one may not read less than three verses but one has to read at least 4. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 21b" href="/Megillah.21b">Babli <i>Megillah</i>21b</a>.</i>. Ḥizqiah said, corresponding to the Ten Commandments<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 21b" href="/Megillah.21b">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 21b</a>, as one of two explanations.</i>. But did we not state, “on Sunday, <i>In the Beginning</i> and <i>there shall be a spread</i>”? And these are only eight! Rebbi Idi said, Cahana and Assi disagreed<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 22a" href="/Megillah.22a">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 22a</a>, disagreement of Rav and Samuel.</i>. One said, he repeats. But the other said, he splits. He who says that he repeats, he repeats two verses. He who says he splits, he splits <i>it was evening, it was morning,</i> as a separate verse<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">He splits it off from v. 5 and reads it as separate sentence. In contrast to the Babli which prescribes only one sentence to be repeated, the Yerushalmi has the three readers reading a total of 10 verses as required by Rav Ḥuna.</i>. But did we not state, “on Monday, <i>there shall be a spread</i> and <i>the waters shall come together</i>”? One said, he repeats. But the other said, he splits. He who says that he repeats, he repeats two verses. He who says he splits, he could not split<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">Since “<i>it was evening, it was morning, the third day</i>” already is a separate verse.</i>. Rebbi Philippos ben Perita objected before Rebbi Ze`ira, is there not the paragraph about Amalek? He said to him, there is a difference since this is the topic of the day<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The reading for Purim, for which three readers are called on a weekday, is <i>Ex</i>.17:8–16. The reading is not connected to the text before or after, it cannot be augmented. Since there are 9 verses and the Mishnaic requirement can be satisfied without problems, there is no need to change anything to satisfy the additional Amoraic rule. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Megillah 21b:8:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Megillah.21b.8.1">Tosaphot <i>Megillah</i> 21b <i>s.v</i>. אין</a>.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar from Merom asked before Rebbi Jonah; was it not stated, the one who reads the conclusion from Prophets should not do less than 21 verses<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 23a" href="/Megillah.23a">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 23a</a>. The question would be that since we require that one reader at least read 4 verses, should there not be at least 22 verses? The question needs no answer since there is no reading from Prophets on weekdays; the number 21 refers to the seven people called to read on a Sabbath; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 4:2:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.4.2.2"><i>Megillah</i> 4:2 Note 74</a>.</i>?
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 27b" href="/Taanit.27b">Babli 27b</a>.</i>: The people of the watch<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning the bystanders who do not work in this week.</i> are fasting every day. On Monday they were fasting for travellers at sea; <i>God commanded, there shall be a spread in midst of the water</i><sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 1:6" href="/Genesis.1.6"><i>Gen</i>. 1:6</a>.</i>. On Tuesday they are fasting for road travellers; <i>God commanded, the waters under the sky shall congregate</i><sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 1:9" href="/Genesis.1.9"><i>Gen</i>. 1:9</a>.</i>. On Wednesday they are fasting for children that diphteria should not develop in their mouths; <i>God commanded, there shall be lights</i><sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 1:14" href="/Genesis.1.14"><i>Gen</i>. 1:14</a>.</i>. “Curses” is written<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">Reading מְאֹרוֹת as מְאֵרוֹת.</i>. On Thursday they are fasting that pregnant women should not miscarry and that the children of nursing women should not die; <i>God commanded, let the waters teem with living creepers</i><sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 1:20" href="/Genesis.1.20"><i>Gen</i>. 1:20</a>.</i>. They fasted neither on Friday nor on Sunday in order to honor the Sabbath. It was stated: The Great Synhedrion was fasting with them. Can the Synhedrion fast every day? They split themselves into clans. “One does not fast for two reasons simultaneously<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 8b" href="/Taanit.8b">Babli 8b</a>.</i>, from the following: <i>we rose and asked of our God for this</i><sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 8:23" href="/Ezra.8.23"><i>Ezra</i> 8:23</a>, misquoted. The same misquote is in the Munich ms. of the Babli (<i>Diqduqe Soferim Ta`anit</i> p. 38, Note ס). Therefore the misquote is a Midrash, not a scribal error. Editors of the printed Babli corrected the quote.</i>.” Rebbi Tanḥuma said, not because of this but because of the following, <i>to ask for mercy from the God of Heaven for this secret</i><sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Daniel 2:18" href="/Daniel.2.18"><i>Dan</i>. 2:18</a>.</i>. For if there were two reasons, such as a drought and locusts, one blows the <i>shofar</i> about them. When Rebbi Ḥaggai went for a fast, he said before them: Our brothers, even though in our hearts are many worries, this is for what we came.
The Mishnah is Rebbi Meïr’s, as Rebbi Meïr said, one prays and reads, one prays and reads. But following the Rabbis, one prays and reads, one prays and leaves<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">On a festive day, the service of the bystanders ends after the Torah reading from <i>Gen</i>. The <i>musaf</i> service is the regular one, disregarding the bystanders.</i>. Therefore on it<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">A festive day with <i>musaf</i> prayer which falls into the week in which the community observes the rules of bystanders, such as New Year’s Day of Nisan (Mishnah 6).</i> is a <i>musaf</i>. Is the Mishnah Rebbi Meïr’s since Rebbi Meïr said, one prays and reads? There are Tannaim who state it inversely. Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Yasa following our Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">Irrespective of the attribution of names one follows the rule of the Mishnah (since, as noted earlier, the rotation of the obligation of bystanders was continued after the destruction of the Temple.)</i>. Rebbi Simon said, is the load of firewood such an exertion<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote">Since the bystanders did not work the entire day, even in Temple times there was no reason not to follow the rules both of the New Moon and the bystanders.</i>? Rebbi Mana said, because of the meal of the New Moon. Rebbi Eleazar said, because of “what is more frequent than something else has precedence over the other.<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">Since the New Moon happens 12 times a year but Temple service of the clan only about twice a year.</i>”
The verse supports Rebbi Joḥanan: <i>It was in the morning of the second</i> New Month<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 20:27" href="/I_Samuel.20.27"><i>1S</i>. 20:27</a>.</i>. If you would say, there were two months, is it not written: <i>why did Jesse’s son come neither yesterday not today to the meal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">Which shows that even in the early monarchy, New Month was celebrated for two days at places (such as Saul’s Gibea) far from the religious center (at Nob).</i><i>?</i> Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, Rebbi Joḥanan commanded those of the Kufra synagogue<sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote">A synagogue in Tiberias.</i>, make sure that you come home when it is still daytime and you should mention its time and its addition<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">If the New Moon was not seen on day 30 of the previous month, in the evening prayers one uses the text for New Moons and mentions that the day is New Moon’s Day, and continues the same for a second day the next evening and the following day. (in a different context <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 4:4:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.4.4.4"><i>Roš Haššanah</i> 4, Notes 42–43</a>.)</i>.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The times of wood offerings<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">Even though fire wood for the altar as a necessity of sacrifices could be bought with money from the Temple tax, the families mentioned in the Mishnah had the privilege of offering fire wood to the Temple as explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:4:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.4.2">Halakhah 6</a>, and their wood had to be used before any bought by tax money could be used.</i> of the priests and the people are nine. On the first of Nisan, the family Araḥ<sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:10" href="/Nehemiah.7.10"><i>Neh</i>. 7:10</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:9" href="/Ezra.2.9"><i>Ezr</i>. 2:9</a>.</i> from the tribe of Judah. On the twentieth of Tammuz, the family of David from the tribe of Judah. On the fifth of Av, the family of Par`osh<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:8" href="/Nehemiah.7.8"><i>Neh</i>. 7:8</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:3" href="/Ezra.2.3"><i>Ezr</i>. 2:3</a>.</i> from the tribe of Judah. On the seventh, the family of Yonadav ben Rekhav<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 35:16" href="/Jeremiah.35.16"><i>Jer</i>. 35:16</a>.</i>. On the tenth, the family of Senaah<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:38" href="/Nehemiah.7.38"><i>Neh</i>. 7:38</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:35" href="/Ezra.2.35"><i>Ezr.</i>2:35</a>.</i> from the tribe of Benjamin. On the fifteenth the family of Zatuel<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:13" href="/Nehemiah.7.13"><i>Neh</i>. 7:13</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:8" href="/Ezra.2.8"><i>Ezr</i>. 2:8</a>.</i> from the tribe of Judah, and with them priests and Levites and everybody who is unsure of his tribe. The families of the pestle stealers and the fig hackers<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">These names are explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:4:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.4.3">Halakhah 7</a>.</i> on the twentieth. The family of Paḥat Moab<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:11" href="/Nehemiah.7.11"><i>Neh</i>. 7:11</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:6" href="/Ezra.2.6"><i>Ezr</i>. 2:6</a>.</i> from the tribe of Judah on the twentieth of Elul. The family of Adin<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:20" href="/Nehemiah.7.20"><i>Neh</i>. 7:20</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:15" href="/Ezra.2.15"><i>Ezr</i>. 2:15</a>.</i> from the tribe of Judah on the first of Tevet. The family of Parosh came a second time. On the first of Tevet was no bystanding since there was <i>hallel</i>, <i>musaf</i>, and wood offering<sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">Since the New Moon of Tevet always is a day of Ḥanukkah, there can be no morning bystanding because of the Hallel to be recited, and none afterwards because of <i>musaf</i> and the additional festivities of the wood offering.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph was copied from here in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Shekalim 4:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Shekalim.4.1.2"><i>Šeqalim</i> 4:1 (Notes 10–18</a>). It also is copied in <i>Megillah</i> 1:1. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 28a" href="/Taanit.28a">Babli 28a</a>).</i> For what reason were the times of wood by the priests and the people to be counted? Only that at the time when Israel returned from the Diaspora and did not find wood in the chamber, those came forward and volunteered wood from their own and donated it to the public. It was used to offer public sacrifices. The prophets among them stipulated that even if the chamber was full of wood [they would bring of their own]<sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">Unnecessary corrector’s addition, missing in all parallels.</i>. If those came and offered and volunteered wood from their own, that the sacrifice should only be brought first from theirs. Rebbi Aḥa said, this is Rebbi Yose’s, since Rebbi Yose said, also he may volunteer as unpaid trustee. Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">This is R. Yose the late Amora, in contrast to R. Yose the Tanna quoted in the preceding sentence.</i> in the name of Rebbi Ila, it is the opinion of everybody. Where do they disagree? About the body of the offering. But for enablers of the offering everybody agrees that a private offering can be turned into public offering. It was stated, a woman<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote">A priestly woman who makes a garment for her son serving in the Temple. All priestly garments for serving in the Temple must be public property.</i> who made a coat for her son has to surrender it to the public. Rebbi Aḥa said, this is Rebbi Yose’s, since Rebbi Yose said, also he may volunteer as unpaid trustee. Rebbi Yasa<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">This must be R. Yose (the Amora) as noted in the parallels; R. Yasa was a teacher, not a student of R. Ila.</i> in the name of Rebbi Ila, it is the opinion of everybody. Where do they disagree? About the body of the offering. But for enablers of the offering everybody agrees that a private offering can be turned into public offering. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Yose: <sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta <i>Ta`aniot</i> 3:6.</i>“Those days are observed at the time of sacrifices and not at the time of sacrifices; Rebbi Yose says, they are observed only at the time of sacrifices.” Also from the following: “Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">With the parallels and the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 12a" href="/Taanit.12a">Babli 12a</a> read : R. Ṣadoq. Since R. Yose denies that these festival days had meaning after the destruction of the Temple, his son cannot report that his family celebrated the holiday on the national day of mourning.</i> said, we were of the descendants of Senaah ben Benjamin. When the Ninth of Av fell on a Sabbath, we postponed it to the end of the Sabbath and they were fasting but not completing.<sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">This disproves the second statement reported due to R. Yose, that the festive days were not celebrated after the destruction of the Temple, but supports R. Aḥa’s statement that the Mishnah must follow R. Yose since the offering of firewood must have the status of a sacrifice if it is important enough to push aside the fast of the Ninth of Av.</i>”
What are “the families of the pestle stealers and the fig hackers”? <sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 28a" href="/Taanit.28a">Babli 28a</a>, the story is told of the Roman government “acting in the manner of Jeroboam”. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 3:7" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).3.7">Tosephta 3:7</a> it is “Greek government acting in the manner of Jeroboam.” In both Babylonian sources the occurrences are dated to the Second commonwealth, which is a more reasonable scenario.</i> But when Jeroboam ben Nabat installed border guards on the roads which did not permit Israel to make a pilgrimage to Jerusalem, everybody who was qualified and sin-fearing in that generation brought his first fruits, put them in a basket, covered them with dried figs and took the pestle. He takes the basket on his shoulder and the pestle in his hand. When he reaches that guard-post they were asking him, where are you going? He answered him, I am only going to make these few dried figs into a single fig cake with this pestle in my hand. After he had passed this guard, he adorned them and brought them to Jerusalem. <sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 28a" href="/Taanit.28a">Babli 28a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 3:8" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).3.8">Tosephta 3:8</a>, as before.</i> Why does one say, the family of Salmai<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">In both Babylonian texts, <i>Salmay from Netofa</i>. The reference probably is to “the family of Salma from Bethlehem and Netofa” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 2:54" href="/I_Chronicles.2.54"><i>1Chr</i>. 2:54</a>), Calebites. This makes sense for the Babylonian texts which date the story to the Second Commonwealth, but not for the Yerushalmi version.</i> the puller-down? But anybody who was volunteering logs and firewood for the altar brought wood and makes them into a kind of steps, assembles them into a kind of ladder, and puts them on his shoulder. When he reaches that guard he asks him, where are you going? He answers him, I am only going to bring two pigeon chicks from this dovecote over there using the ladder on my shoulder. After he had passed this guard, he disassembled {his package} and brought it to Jerusalem. Since they put themselves in danger for the meritorious deed that merited a good reputation in the world, and about them he says<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 10:7" href="/Proverbs.10.7"><i>Prov</i>. 10:7</a>.</i>, <i>the remembrance of the just is a blessing</i>.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Five things happened to our forefathers on the Seventeenth of Tammuz and five on the Ninth of Av<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">Or at least these two days commemorate these events even if the dates may not be correct, as explained in the Halakhah.</i>. On the Seventeenth of Tammuz were the tablets broken, the daily sacrifice ceased<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">During a siege of Jerusalem.</i>, the city was breached<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">Jerusalem surrendered to Nebukadnezar, and its walls were breached by Titus.</i>, Apostomos<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">This personality cannot be identified since he cannot be dated.</i> burned the Torah, and put up an idol in the Temple. On the Ninth of Av was decided that our forefathers would not enter the Land<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">After the return of the scouts, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 14:23" href="/Numbers.14.23"><i>Num</i>. 14:23</a>.</i>, the Temple was destroyed the first and second times, Betar was taken, and the city ploughed over<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">By Hadrian, imitating the mythical foundation of Rome in the founding of pagan Aelia Capitolina. Described in a coin of Hadrian minted 130 C.E.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 24:16" href="/Exodus.24.16"><i>Ex</i>. 24:16</a>.</i>: <i>The glory of the Eternal dwelt on Mount Sinai; the cloud covered it for six days; He called to Moses on the Seventh Day. Moses ascended</i><sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 24:13" href="/Exodus.24.13"><i>Ex</i>. 24:13</a>.</i>. The Seventh after the Ten Commandments, the start of the Forty. Moses said to them, I shall be occupied on the Mountain for 40 days<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">This is the argument which shows that the tablets were broken on the 17th of Tammus (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 28b" href="/Taanit.28b">Babli 28b</a>). In rabbinic tradition, Pentecost (Siwan 6) is the anniversary of the epiphany of Mount Sinai. If one assumes that at the Exodus this month had 30 days and counts 40 days from the following day one has 13 days in Siwan and 17 in Tammuz for a sum of 40. Therefore the date of 17 Tammuz presupposes not only the rabbinic date for the giving of the Ten Commandments but also that Moses did not eat during the six days of waiting for permission to ascend the Mountain.<br>The remainder of the paragraph consists of sermon concepts; presupposing like many sermons that the persons acting in biblical history had foreknowledge of what was going to happen, such as Moses knowing that he would spend 40 days on the Mountain. Similarly, the crass anthropomorphism of the sermon about the tablets would be inadmissible in a discussion with possible consequences for rules of behavior.</i>. When the fortieth day came and he did not come, immediately <i>the people saw that Moses tarried in descending from the Mountain</i><sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:1" href="/Exodus.32.1"><i>Ex</i>. 32:1</a>.</i>. When noontime came and he did not come, immediately <i>the people congregated on Aaron and said to him, rise and make us gods which shall go before us</i>, etc. <i>The Eternal said to Moses, descend, for your people corrupted</i><sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:7" href="/Exodus.32.7"><i>Ex</i>. 32:7</a>.</i>, etc. <i>And Joshua heard the sound of the people in its dealings; he said to Moses, there is sound of war in the camp</i><sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:17" href="/Exodus.32.17"><i>Ex</i>. 32:17</a>.</i>. Moses said, a man who in the future will rule over 600’000 does not know to distinguish between sound and sound? <i>He said, there is no sound of shouts of strength nor sound of sounds of weakness, a sound of shouts I am hearing</i><sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:18" href="/Exodus.32.18"><i>Ex</i>. 32:18</a>.</i>. Rebbi Yasa said, a sound of acclaim of foreign worship I am hearing. Rebbi Yudan in the name of Rebbi Yasa: There is no generation in which there is not an ounce<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>uncia</i>.</i> of the sin of the Calf<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">Any trouble for the Jewish people contains some punishment for the sin of the Golden Calf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 102a" href="/Sanhedrin.102a">Babli <i>Sanhedrin</i> 102a</a>.</i>. <i>It was when he approached the camp that he saw the Calf and fifes</i><sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:19" href="/Exodus.32.19"><i>Ex</i>. 32:19</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥilkiah in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: From here<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">Even though Moses correctly analyzed the sound, he did not act until he had visual confirmation that his analysis was correct.</i> that a person should not argue from guesses. Moses made an argument <i>de minore ad majus</i>. Since for the <i>pesaḥ</i> sacrifice, which is an isolated obligation, it is said <i>no uncircumcised may eat from it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:48" href="/Exodus.12.48"><i>Ex</i>. 12:48</a>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 87a" href="/Shabbat.87a">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 87a</a>.</i>, the Torah in which all commandments are contained not so much more? <i>Moses got angry and he threw the tablets from his hand and broke them below the Mountain</i><sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 32:19" href="/Exodus.32.19"><i>Ex</i>. 32:19</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ismael stated, the Holy One, praise to Him, told him to break them, [as it is said,] <i>I shall write on the tablets the words which were on the first tablets luckily you broke</i><sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 10:2" href="/Deuteronomy.10.2"><i>Deut</i>. 10:2</a>, taking אשר not as relative pronoun but as derived from the root אשר “riches, happiness”.</i>. He said to him, you did well that you broke. Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: The tablets were six hand-breadths long and three wide. Moses held two hand-breadth, the Holy One, praise to Him two hand-breadth, and two hand-breadths of space were between them. When Israel sinned in that way, the Holy One wanted to seize them from Moses’s hand, but Moses’s hand had the better of it and seized them from Him. That is what the verse praises him at the end and says, <i>and all the strong hand</i><sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 34:12" href="/Deuteronomy.34.12"><i>Deut</i>. 34:12</a>.</i>, <sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Here starts an Ashkenazic text edited by J. Sussman (A), differing from the Leiden ms. mostly in the names of the tradents. The readings of the Leiden ms. are more reliable; they are confirmed by excerpts from this Chapter published by L. Ginzberg.</i> peace shall be on the hand which had the better on mine. Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Abbai: the tablets wanted to fly off but Moses held them, [as is written,] <i>I grabbed the two tablets</i><sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 9:17" href="/Deuteronomy.9.17"><i>Deut</i>. 9:17</a>.</i>. It was stated in the name of Rebbi Nehemiah, the writing itself flew off<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 87b" href="/Pesachim.87b">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 87b</a>, last line.</i>. Rebbi Ezra in the name of Rebbi Jehudah ben Rebbi Simon: The tablets were a load of forty <i>seah</i> but the writing was carrying them. When the writing flew off they were too heavy for Moses’s hands, they fell, and broke<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 87b" href="/Pesachim.87b">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 87b</a>, last line.</i>.
“The daily sacrifice ceased.” <sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 4:1:12-13" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.4.1.12-13"><i>Berakhot</i> 4:1 (Notes 22–28</a>, ב). <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rosh Hashanah 18b" href="/Rosh_Hashanah.18b">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 18b</a>.</i> Rebbi Simon said in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: In the time of the hellenistic government<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 64b" href="/Menachot.64b">Babli (<i>Menaḥot</i> 64b</a>) telescopes this story and the next into one and dates it at the civil war of the two Hasmonean brothers Hyrkanos and Aristobulos.</i> they<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">The officials of the Temple lowered the boxes from the wall of besieged Jerusalem; in each box was payment for the lamb to be placed in it for the daily sacrifice.</i> lowered them two boxes with gold and they gave them two lambs to pull up. Once they lowered them two boxes with gold and they gave them two kid goats<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">Which cannot be used for the perpetual sacrifice.</i> to pull up. At that moment the Holy One, praise to Him, enlightened their eyes and they found two lambs in the hall of lambs<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">Since the verse (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 28:3" href="/Numbers.28.3"><i>Num</i>. 28:3</a>) requires that the perpetual sacrifice be “a yearling sheep without blemish” the sheep were usually held in a separate “hall of lambs” and were inspected three times before being used as sacrifice.</i>. About that time did Rebbi Yehudah bar Abba testify that the perpetual morning sacrifice was brought at four hours. Rebbi Levi said: Also in the days of the present evil government<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">In both Talmudim, the “evil government” or simply “government” is the Roman government.</i> they lowered them two boxes with gold and they gave them two kid goats<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">This obviously is a copyist’s error (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 4:5:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.4.5.3">Note 225</a>); with the text of <i>Berakhot</i> one has to read “lambs”.</i> to pull up. Once they lowered them two boxes with gold and they gave them two swine to pull up<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 64b" href="/Menachot.64b">Babli (<i>Menaḥot</i> 64b</a>), there was only one swine and not only the wall but the entire Land of Israel trembled. (The civil war was at the time when Pompey conquered the East for Rome but the story here clearly speaks of the war of Titus. However, it seems that the Babli tradition in this case is more correct.)</i>. They did not manage to get to half the height of the wall when the swine (damaged) [clawed]<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">The change by the corrector follows the text ב. However, there one reads “the swine clawed the wall and the wall trembled”, which is well described by the term used by the Leiden scribe.</i> the wall and jumped 40 parasangs from the Land of Israel. At that time the sins caused that the perpetual sacrifice was stopped and the Temple destroyed.
<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is repeated again in this Halakhah. Since the later text shows that the text here is incomplete, its correct place is there.</i> Rebbi Simeon ben Yohai stated: So was my teacher Aqiba explaining. <i>So says the Eternal of Hosts, the fast of the fourth, the fast of the fifth, the fast of the seventh, and the fast of the tenth will be for the House of Israel enjoyment and joy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 8:19" href="/Zechariah.8.19"><i>Sach</i>. 8:19</a>.</i>. The fast of the fourth is the Seventeenth of Tammuz, the day when the tablets were broken, the daily sacrifice ceased, the city was breached, Apostomos burned the Torah, and put an idol in the Temple. The fast of the fifth is the Ninth of Av, when the Temple was destroyed the first and the second times. The fast of the seventh is the third of Tishre, when Gedalya ben Aḥiqam was murdered<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 41:2-3" href="/Jeremiah.41.2-3"><i>Jer</i>. 41:2–3</a>.</i>. The fast of the tenth is the Tenth of Tevet, the day when the King of Babylonia closed in on Jerusalem<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 24:2" href="/Ezekiel.24.2"><i>Ez</i>. 24:2</a>.</i>.
“And the city was breached.” It is written, <i>on the Ninth of the month the city was breached</i><sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 39:2" href="/Jeremiah.39.2"><i>Jer</i>. 39:2</a>. The date is confirmed <i>2K</i>. 25:3.</i>, and you are saying so? Rebbi Tanḥum bar Ḥanilai said, here is an erroneous computation<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 28b" href="/Taanit.28b">Babli 28b</a> disagrees and states that the city surrendered on Tammuz 9 to the Babylonians and was breached Tammuz 17 by the Romans.</i>. That is what is written, <i>it was in the eleventh year, on the first of the month, was the Eternal’s word to me, saying: Son of man, since Tyre said about Jerusalem hurrah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 26:1-2" href="/Ezekiel.26.1-2"><i>Ez</i>. 26:1–2</a>. The verse makes it clear that the joy was about the destruction of Jerusalem, for which the prophecy gives a date post <i>quem</i>.</i>. What “hurrah”? If you are saying on the first of Av, it still was not burned. If you are saying on the first of Ellul, cannot in one day and night the messenger leave Jerusalem and arrive at Tyre? But here is an erroneous computation<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">But Ezechiel implicitly states that Jerusalem was destroyed on Av 1.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish. Rebbi Joḥanan said, {a parable} of a king who was sitting and computing computations. They came and told him, your son was kidnapped; his computations became erroneous. He said, let this be the beginning of computations<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">What actually was Av 9 is now called Av 1.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, {a parable} of a king who was sitting and computing computations. They came and told him, your son was kidnapped and incapacitated; his computations became erroneous. He said, let this be the beginning of computations. Rebbi Mana asked, one understands this that they were erroneous for the past; maybe for the future<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">Maybe the participants in the destruction, Jeremiah and the author of Kings, erred in the date. But Ezechiel sitting safely in Babylonia and being divinely instructed cannot be assumed to err in his date.</i>? Whether one follows him who said on the ninth of the month, or the one who said on the seventeenth, [in what do they differ?]<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from a source similar to A. There it is clear that one has to read: In what do they differ? Are there not (according to everybody) twenty-one days from the day the city was breached to the day the Temple was destroyed?</i> there are twenty-one days from the day the city was breached to the day the Temple was destroyed. Rebbi Abuna said, an indication<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">Greek σημεῑον.</i>, <i>I am seeing an almond stick</i><sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 1:11" href="/Jeremiah.1.11"><i>Jer</i>. 1:11</a>.</i>. Since this almond tree from sprouting its flower to finishing its fruit needs twenty-one days, so from the day the city was breached to the day the Temple was destroyed twenty-one days. He who says on the Ninth of the month, the Temple was destroyed on the first of Av<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">The dating in <i>Ez</i>. is consistent with that of <i>Jer</i>. and <i>2K</i>.; there is no error in the computations.</i>. He who says on the Seventeenth, the Temple was destroyed on the Ninth of Av.
Rebbi Simeon ben Yoḥai stated: So was my teacher Aqiba explaining. <i>So says the Eternal of Hosts, the fast of the fourth, the fast of the fifth, the fast of the seventh, and the fast of the tenth will be for the House of Israel enjoyment and joy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 8:19" href="/Zechariah.8.19"><i>Sach</i>. 8:19</a>.</i>. The fast of the fourth is the Seventeenth of Tammuz, the day when the tablets were broken, the daily sacrifice ceased, the city was breached, Apostomos burned the Torah, and put an idol in the Temple. The fast of the fifth is the Ninth of Av, when the Temple was destroyed the first and the second times. The fast of the seventh is the third of Tishre, when Gedalya ben Aḥiqam was murdered<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 41:2-3" href="/Jeremiah.41.2-3"><i>Jer</i>. 41:2–3</a>.</i>. The fast of the tenth is the Tenth of Tevet, the day when the King of Babylonia closed in on Jerusalem<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 24:2" href="/Ezekiel.24.2"><i>Ez</i>. 24:2</a>.</i>. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 24:2" href="/Ezekiel.24.2"><i>Ez</i>. 24:2</a>.</i>, <i>the Eternal’s word came to me in the ninth year, in the tenth month, on the tenth of the month, saying: Son of man, write down the name of this day. On this very day the king of Babylonia closed in on Jerusalem</i>. But I am saying that the fast of the tenth is the Fifth of Tevet, the day when the news came to the diaspora. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 33:21" href="/Ezekiel.33.21"><i>Ez</i>. 33:21</a>.</i>, <i>it was in the eleventh year of our exile, in the fifth, on the fifth of the month, the fugitive came to me from Jerusalem, saying, the city was breached</i>. Only that in Judea one fasts on the act, and in the exile on the news. Rebbi Aqiba explains the first last and the last first; but I am explaining the first first and the last last<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">I am following the order of verses in <i>Ez</i>.</i>; and I hold my words more intelligible than Rebbi Aqiba’s words.
“Apostomos<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">This personality cannot be identified since he cannot be dated.</i> burned the Torah.” Where did he burn it? Rebbi Aḥa said, at the ford of Lydda. But the rabbis are saying, at the ford of Tarlosa<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">Place not identified. In A one reads “exercise field” instead of “ford”.</i>. “And put up an idol in the Temple.” There are Tannaim who state, “was put up.” He who says, “was put up,” Manasse’s idol. He who said, “put up”, Apostomos’s idol<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">A here has an insert from <i>Seder Olam</i> which identifies Apostomos with the Emperor Caligula.</i>. Why was it not fixed as a fast day<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">The question here is why the Seventeenth of Tammuz is not a full 24 hr. fast day like the Ninth of Av. The question in A, why was the day when the scouts were sent not made a fast day (since they caused the people to stay in the wilderness for 40 years and fixed the day for the double destruction of the Temple) is incompatible with the statement of R. Joshua ben Levi and has to be classified as gloss.</i>? Ḥinnena the father of Bar Yanta in the name of Rebbi Banaia: Because most of the community did not accept it as obligation<sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">And a rabbinic institution which is not accepted by a majority of the people is invalid.</i>. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, all that happened on this was repeated, all that happened on that was not repeated<sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote">The happenings on Tammuz 17 do not have the severity of those on Av 9.</i>. Rebbi Levi said, it is written, <i>which a person shall do and live by them</i><sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 18:5" href="/Leviticus.18.5"><i>Lev</i>. 18:5</a>. The verse shows that danger to life or limb supersedes religious obligations.</i>, and the light in a person’s eyes only returns after 40 days<sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore full 24 hr. fast-days must be spaced at least 40 days apart. This forbids making Tammuz 17 a full fast-day.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote">Here the heading is missing: “On the Ninth of Av was decided that our forefathers would not enter the Land.” The date of the return of the scouts is not directly spelled out in <i>Num</i>.</i> That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">256</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:11" href="/Numbers.10.11"><i>Num</i>. 10:11</a>.</i>, <i>it was in the second year in the second month on the twentieth of the month</i>, etc. And it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">257</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:33" href="/Numbers.10.33"><i>Num</i>. 10:33</a>.</i>, <i>they travelled from the Eternal’s mountain a distance of three days</i>. Rebbi Zacharia, the son-in-law of Rebbi Levi: {a parable} like children who are freed from &lt;school&gt; (books)<sup class="footnote-marker">258</sup><i class="footnote">The text in &lt; &gt; is from A (and also in a clearly wrong text in a Genizah excerpt, <i>Yerushalmi Fragments</i>, p. 184.)</i> and leave to run<sup class="footnote-marker">259</sup><i class="footnote">The letters [בכ] added by the corrector indicate a text like A: “leave to villages.” The word is missing in the Genizah excerpt. These changes misunderstand the text. R. Zacharia notes that they did not travel for three days, but the distance of three days, implying that the actual travel time was one day.</i>. On that very day they desired a desire<sup class="footnote-marker">260</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 11:20" href="/Numbers.11.20"><i>Num</i>. 11:20</a>. No new date is indicated; an unqualified added month is 30 days.</i>; <i>up to a month, until it will come out of your noses</i>. And the seven days of Miriam; <i>Miriam was secluded outside the camp</i><sup class="footnote-marker">261</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 12:15" href="/Numbers.12.15"><i>Num</i>. 12:15</a>.</i>. And the 40 days of the scouts, <i>they returned from scouting the Land at the end of 40 days. They walked and came to Moses and Aaron</i><sup class="footnote-marker">262</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 13:25" href="/Numbers.13.25"><i>Num</i>. 13:25</a>.</i> etc. They came and found them occupied with the rules for <i>ḥallah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">263</sup><i class="footnote">The heave to be taken from bread dough “when you come into the Land” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:18" href="/Numbers.15.18"><i>Num</i>. 15:18</a>).</i> and <i>orlah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote">The fruits to be stripped from a tree during its first three years “when you come to the Land” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 19:23" href="/Leviticus.19.23"><i>Lev</i>. 19:23</a>).</i>. They said to them, you are not going to enter the Land and you are studying the rules for <i>ḥallah</i> and <i>orlah</i>? Immediately, <i>the entire congregation raised their voices; the people cried in that night</i><sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 14:1" href="/Numbers.14.1"><i>Num</i>. 14:1</a>.</i>. He said to them, you cried before Me a pointless crying. By My life, in the future you shall cry a substantial crying. <i>Crying she will cry in the night</i><sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 1:2" href="/Lamentations.1.2"><i>Thr</i>. 1:2</a>, referring to the Ninth of Av. The computation goes as follows. Starting from the 20<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> of the second month one counts this day for travel, 7 days for Miryam’s seclusion, 30 days for the quail, and 40 days for the scouts, for a total of 97 days after the first of the 2<sup class="footnote-marker">nd</sup> month. The year is supposed to start with a full 30 day first month. Therefore the 2<sup class="footnote-marker">nd</sup> and 4<sup>th</sup> months have 29 days, the 3<sup>rd</sup> month 30 days, for a total of 88 days. The count ends on the 9<sup>th</sup> of the 5th month, Q. E. D. Differently in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29a" href="/Taanit.29a">Babli 29a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Yoḥai stated: It is written<sup>267</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 11:10" href="/Numbers.11.10"><i>Num</i>. 11:10</a>. This is the second unnecessary crying mentioned in the verse.</i>, <i>Moses heard the people crying for its families</i>, etc. About the six incest prohibitions which Moses forbade them<sup class="footnote-marker">268</sup><i class="footnote">They cried about the paternal and maternal half-sisters, the maternal and paternal aunts, the sister-in-law, and the menstruating woman, which are permitted to Gentiles but forbidden to Israelites. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 75a" href="/Yoma.75a">Babli <i>Yoma</i> 75a</a>.</i>.
He said to them<sup class="footnote-marker">269</sup><i class="footnote">Moses to the scouts. One explains why the sin of the scouts, which kept the people 38 years in the desert, is the equivalent of the destruction of the Temple and merits inclusion in the fast of the Ninth of Av. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 35a" href="/Sotah.35a">Babli <i>Sotah</i> 35a</a>.</i>, even so, what did you see? They told him, <i>it is a Land devouring its inhabitants</i><sup class="footnote-marker">270</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 13:32" href="/Numbers.13.32"><i>Num</i>. 13:32</a>.</i>; in any town we entered there people had died. The Holy One, praise to Him, said to them: Because of the benefit which I gave you, you are saying <i>it is a Land devouring its inhabitants</i>? In any town which they entered, a head of the town died. While they were occupied with him, they passed through the town and left before anybody noticed them. Not only this, but you said, <i>we were in our eyes like locusts, and so we were in their eyes</i><sup class="footnote-marker">271</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 13:33" href="/Numbers.13.33"><i>Num</i>. 13:33</a>.</i>. You knew what I made you in their eyes. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, they said things against Heaven: <i>for he is stronger than Him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">272</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 13:31" href="/Numbers.13.31"><i>Num</i>. 13:31</a>.</i>; even He can do nothing against them. Rebbi Levi in the name of Rebbi Ḥama bar Ḥanina: <i>with a big uproar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">273</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 11:16" href="/Jeremiah.11.16"><i>Jer</i>. 11:16</a>.</i>, by the noise of the big (word) [uproar]<sup class="footnote-marker">274</sup><i class="footnote">The text of the scribe (in parentheses) is preferable to that of the [corrector] since it refers to the blasphemous character of the statement in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 13:31" href="/Numbers.13.31"><i>Num</i>. 13:31</a>. The public blasphemy started the fire.</i> which you pronounced, <i>He started a fire which broke its branches.</i>
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">275</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29a" href="/Taanit.29a">Babli 29a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Arakhin 11b" href="/Arakhin.11b"><i>Arakhin</i> 11b</a>.</i>: Rebbi Yose says, the day of the destruction of the Temple was after the end of the Sabbath, at the end of a Sabbatical year<sup class="footnote-marker">276</sup><i class="footnote">69 C.E.</i>, during the watch of Yehoyariv, on the Ninth of Av. And so it happened the second time. Both times the Levites were standing on the platform and singing, <i>He turned on them their wrongs, in their malice he eradicates them, eradicates them the Eternal, our God</i><sup class="footnote-marker">277</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 94:23" href="/Psalms.94.23"><i>Ps</i>. 94:23</a>.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish asked before Rebbi Joḥanan; may one sing without libations<sup class="footnote-marker">278</sup><i class="footnote">If there are sacrifices, the Levites have to sing the daily song at the time the libations accompanying the daily sacrifice are poured. Since daily (and all other animal) sacrifices stopped on Tammuz 17, the question is whether the Levites may sing at all.</i>? He said to him, let us hear from what was stated: “both times the Levites were standing on the platform and singing, <i>He turned on them their wrongs</i>, etc.” Rebbi Abbahu said, Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish disagreed. Rebbi Joḥanan said, one may sing without libations. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, one may not sing without libations. Rebbi Joḥanan objected to Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: Was it not stated, “both times the Levites were standing on the platform and singing, <i>He turned on them their wrongs</i>”? Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said to him, what do you conclude from this? He said to him, since if there were libations it would have been time for the song. Rebbi Joḥanan said, the daily song. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, yesterday’s song<sup class="footnote-marker">279</sup><i class="footnote">In this version, R. Joḥanan disputes either whether the song was <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 94" href="/Psalms.94"><i>Ps</i>. 94</a> or that the destruction was on a Sunday, since the song is the one for Wednesday. He holds that if there are no sacrifices, one performs the services which are possible under the circumstances. R. Simeon ben Laqish holds that no service can be performed if not all rules can be observed; for him the song here was not a service but a dirge.</i>.
Rebbi Levi said, Yehoyariv, a person. Meron, a town. Mesarbei. He delivered His House to the enemies<sup class="footnote-marker">280</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that the clans of Yehoyariv serving on that day were Meron and Mesarbei.</i>. Rebbi Berekhia said, [Yehoyariv], Yah quarrelled with His children since they rebelled and rejected Him. Yeda`ya Amoq Sipporim<sup class="footnote-marker">281</sup><i class="footnote">Also name of a watch and two of its clans.</i>. Yah knew the deep counsel in their hearts and exiled them to Sepphoris<sup class="footnote-marker">283</sup><i class="footnote">A parallel text is <i>Thr. rabba</i> 3(38); cf. also <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 57a-58a" href="/Gittin.57a-58a">Babli <i>Gittin</i> 57a–58a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 93b" href="/Sanhedrin.93b"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 93b</a>.</i>.
“Bettar was taken.” <sup class="footnote-marker">283</sup><i class="footnote">A parallel text is <i>Thr. rabba</i> 3(38); cf. also <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 57a-58a" href="/Gittin.57a-58a">Babli <i>Gittin</i> 57a–58a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 93b" href="/Sanhedrin.93b"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 93b</a>.</i> Rebbi used to preach 24 facts about the <i>Eternal swallowed and showed no mercy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">284</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 2:2" href="/Lamentations.2.2"><i>Thr</i>. 2:2</a>.</i>, but Rebbi Joḥanan 60. So Rebbi Joḥanan more than Rebbi? Only since Rebbi was closer to the destruction of the Temple, there were there old men remembering, and those would cry and continuously silence him. It was stated: Rebbi Jehudah ben Rebbi Illai said, Baruch my teacher used to preach, <i>the voice is Jacob’s voice but the hands are Esau’s hands</i><sup class="footnote-marker">285</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 27:22" href="/Genesis.27.22"><i>Gen</i>. 27:22</a>.</i>. Jacob’s voice cries about what Esau’s hands did at Bettar.
Rebbi Simeon ben Yohai stated: Aqiba my teacher used to preach, <i>there appeared a star out of Jacob</i><sup class="footnote-marker">286</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 24:17" href="/Numbers.24.17"><i>Num</i>. 24:17</a>.</i> there appeared Koziba out of Jacob. When Rebbi Aqiba saw Bar Koziba he said, this is King Messias. Rebbi Joḥanan ben Torta said to him, Aqiba! Grass will grow from your jaws and still David’s son (still has to) [will not have]<sup class="footnote-marker">287</sup><i class="footnote">The corrector’s [text] is from the Midrash. The scribe’s text asserts that the Messiah always will be coming.</i> come. Rebbi Joḥanan said, the voice of Emperor Hadrian killing eighty thousand myriads at Bettar<sup class="footnote-marker">288</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Cant. rabba</i> 2(36) the number is 90’000’000. <i>Thr. rabba</i> shows that the statement here is copied in the wrong place; it belongs to the previous paragraph, explaining the sound of Esau.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, eighty [thousand] couples of horn-blowers<sup class="footnote-marker">289</sup><i class="footnote">Roman army commanders.</i> were encircling Bettar, each of which was commanding several army units. There was Ben Koziba who had 200’000 with him missing a finger. The Sages sent, how long will you turn Israel into defective persons? He told them, how would it be possible to test them? They said to him, anyone who riding on his horse cannot uproot a cedar of Lebanon should not be enrolled in your army<sup class="footnote-marker">290</sup><i class="footnote">Greek στρατιά.</i>. He had 200’000 of either kind. When he went into battle he said, Master of the World: Do not support and do not hinder, <i>did not you, God, neglect us, and do not go out with our armies</i><sup class="footnote-marker">291</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 60:12" href="/Psalms.60.12"><i>Ps</i>. 60:12</a>.</i>. Three and a half years did Hadrian encircle Bettar. Rebbi Eleazar from Modiin was sitting in sackcloth and ashes, praying every day and saying, Master of the World, do not sit in judgment today, do not sit in judgment today. Hadrian wanted to go away. A Samaritan said to him, do not go away, for I am seeing what to do that the city will submit to you. He went to the city gate, entered, and found Rebbi Eleazar from Modiin standing in prayer. He showed himself as if he would whisper into his ear. The people of the city saw him and brought him to Ben Koziba. They said to him, we saw this old man turning to your uncle. He asked him, what did you say to him and what did he say to you? He answered, if I shall tell you, the king will kill me; but if I do not tell you, you will kill me. It is better that the king should kill me but not you. He told him, he said to me, I will make the town submit to the king. He came to Rebbi Eleazar from Modiin. He asked him, what did this Samaritan say to you. He answered, nothing. What did you say to him? He answered, nothing. He kicked him and killed him. Immediately there came an unembodied voice and said, <i>woe, criminal shepherds, who abandon the flock, a sword on his arm and on his right eye. His arm shall dry up and his right eye darken</i><sup class="footnote-marker">292</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 11:17" href="/Zechariah.11.17"><i>Zach</i>. 11:17</a>.</i>. You killed Rebbi Eleazar from Modiin, the arm of Israel, and their right eye. Therefore this man’s arm shall dry up and his right eye darken. Immediately Bettar was taken and Ben Koziba killed. They came carrying his head to Hadrain. He asked them, who killed him? A Samaritan said to him, I killed him. He said to him, show me his body. He showed him his body; he found a poisonous snake wrapped around him. He said, if God had not killed him, who could kill him? He recited over him, <i>if not that their Rock had sold them, and the Eternal handed them over</i><sup class="footnote-marker">293</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 32:30" href="/Deuteronomy.32.30"><i>Deut</i>. 32:30</a>.</i>. They killed them continuously until the horse was immersed in blood up to his nose. The blood was moving rocks of 40 seah loads, until the blood colored the sea for four <i>mil</i>. If you would say that it was close to the sea, in fact it is 40 <i>mil</i> distant from the sea. They said, 300 children’s brains were found on one stone, and they found three boxes of <i>tefillin</i> capsules of nine <i>seah</i> each, but some say nine of three each. It was stated, Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, 500 schools were in Bettar, the smallest one for not less than 500 children. They were saying, if the haters come against us we shall go out against them with these stylos and blind them. When the sins caused, they were binding each single one into his book and burning him; and of them only I remained. He recited referring to himself, <i>my eye hurts my soul more than all daughters of my city</i><sup class="footnote-marker">294</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 3:51" href="/Lamentations.3.51"><i>Thr</i>. 3:51</a>.</i>. The evil Hadrian had a large vineyard, eighteen <i>mil</i> by eighteen <i>mil</i>, as from Tiberias to Sepphoris. He fenced it in with the slain of Bettar standing up with outstretched arms, and did not decide that they should be buried, until another king arose<sup class="footnote-marker">295</sup><i class="footnote">An expression used for a new dynasty, in this case Septimius Severus.</i> who decided that they should be buried.
<sup class="footnote-marker">296</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph has no parallel in <i>Thr. rabba</i>.</i> Rav Ḥuna said, when the slain of Bettar were permitted to be buried, “the good and the benefactor” was fixed. “The good” that they did not decompose, “the benefactor” that they were permitted for burial<sup class="footnote-marker">297</sup><i class="footnote">The fourth benediction of Grace. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 31a" href="/Taanit.31a">Babli 31a</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 1:5:21" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.1.5.21"><i>Berakhot</i> 1:8 (Note 278</a>), 7:1 (Notes 35,36), Babli 48b.</i>. It was stated, Rebbi Yose said, 52 years Bettar existed after the destruction of the Temple. And why was it destroyed? For they lit lights after the destruction of the Temple. Why did they light lights? Because the council members<sup class="footnote-marker">298</sup><i class="footnote">Greek βουλευτής.</i> of Jerusalem were dominating the center of the city. When they were seeing a person moving to Jerusalem they said to him, since we heard about you that you are aspiring to be made judge<sup class="footnote-marker">299</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ʼάρχων, - οντος.</i> or councillor; he would say to them, that is not my intention<sup class="footnote-marker">300</sup><i class="footnote">To become elected and to pay bribes for the purpose.</i>.
