Because we heard about you that you intend to sell your property<sup class="footnote-marker">301</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ου ʼσία.</i>; he would say to them, that is not my intention. His colleague would say to him, what are you arguing with this one, write and I shall sign<sup class="footnote-marker">302</sup><i class="footnote">Since a sale document is valid if it is testified to by two witnesses; it needs no signature of any of the parties to the sale.</i>. He would write and his colleague would sign. They would send the sale document<sup class="footnote-marker">303</sup><i class="footnote">A Semitic form of Greek ʼωνή.</i> to his house companion and told him, if X comes to enter his property, do not let him, because it is sold to us. When he heard this from them he said, if only this man’s leg had been broken before he came to Jerusalem. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">304</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 3:18" href="/Lamentations.3.18"><i>Thr</i>. 3:18</a>.</i>, <i>they caught our steps, not to walk in our streets. They caught our steps</i>, destroy the way to that House, <i>our end is near</i>, the end of this House is near, <i>our days are fulfilled</i>, the days of this House are fulfilled. They also did not come out well, <i>he who enjoys disaster will not be acquitted</i><sup class="footnote-marker">305</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 17:5" href="/Proverbs.17.5"><i>Prov</i>. 17:5</a>.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">306</sup><i class="footnote">This again is found in <i>Thr. rabba</i>, but the corrector’s insert is copied from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 32:1-52" href="/Deuteronomy.32.1-52"><i>Yalqut Haazinu</i> (§946</a>), to which tradition also belongs the text of A (which ends here). In the traditional text of <i>Thr. rabba</i> it is very clear that the story belongs to the legend of Bar Kochba since there the crown is to be offered to Simon (bar Koziba).</i>[Two brothers were in Kefar Ḥariba; the Romans went out against them and they would kill them. They said, the medicine for this is for us to bring a crown to their heads. They said, let us try a last time. When they went out, an old man met them and said, your Maker may support you. They said, may He neither help nor [support] &lt;obstruct&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">307</sup><i class="footnote">The word &lt;added&gt; is from A; it might be Arabic סבפ “to put a step on an entrance”,as sign of an obstacle, or בספ “affairs go badly”.</i>, <i>did not you, God, neglect us</i><sup class="footnote-marker">291</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 60:12" href="/Psalms.60.12"><i>Ps</i>. 60:12</a>.</i>.]
<sup class="footnote-marker">308</sup><i class="footnote">From here to the last paragraph of the Halakhah most of the text is found in <i>Thr. rabba</i> 3(38).</i> There grew two cedars on the Mount of Olives. Under one of them there were four shops selling in purity<sup class="footnote-marker">309</sup><i class="footnote">They only sold food of guaranteed purity for pilgrims to the Temple (and Pharisees eating all food in purity).</i>; from the other they were bringing 40 <i>seah</i> of pigeon chicks every single month and from there were providing all of Israel with nests<sup class="footnote-marker">310</sup><i class="footnote">A “nest” is a couple of birds required for purification by many people whose impurity was caused by their own body. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 44a" href="/Berakhot.44a">Babli <i>Berakhot</i>44a</a>.</i>. Mount Simon<sup class="footnote-marker">311</sup><i class="footnote">Unidentified.</i> was producing 200 barrels of fig pieces every Friday. Why was it destroyed? Some say, because of whoring; but some say it was because they were playing ball<sup class="footnote-marker">312</sup><i class="footnote">Possibly the sin was not the ball playing but the accessory wagering.</i>. 10’000 towns were on King’s Mountain<sup class="footnote-marker">313</sup><i class="footnote">The hill region N of Jerusalem and W of Antipatris.</i>; Rebbi Eleazar ben Ḥarsom owned 1’000 of them, and correspondingly 1’000 ships on the Sea. And all of them were destroyed<sup class="footnote-marker">314</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 35b" href="/Yoma.35b">Babli <i>Yoma</i> 35b</a>.</i>. Of three villages was the <i>qtmos</i><sup class="footnote-marker">315</sup><i class="footnote">A word for which no reasonable source or meaning is found in the literature.</i> brought to Jerusalem in carts, Kabul, Shiḥin, and Magdala of the dyers<sup class="footnote-marker">316</sup><i class="footnote">All places in Galilee.</i> All three were destroyed. Kabul because of quarrel, Sḥihin because of sorcery, and Magdala of the dyers because of whoring. Three villages of which each one was populated by twice the number of those leaving Egypt<sup class="footnote-marker">317</sup><i class="footnote">1’200’000.</i>, the evil village, the cress village, and the boys’ village. Why was it called evil village? Because they did not receive travellers. Why was it called cress village? Because they were growing children like cress. Why was it called boys’ village? Because all their women gave birth to boys. If one of them never left from there she would not give birth to a girl. Rebbi Joḥanan said, 80 pairs of priestly brothers married 80 pairs of priestly sisters at Gufna<sup class="footnote-marker">318</sup><i class="footnote">N of Jerusalem.</i> in one night, not counting brothers but not sisters, sisters but not brothers, not counting Levites, not counting Israel. Rebbi Joḥanan said, in Magdala of the dyers there were 80 establishments of fustian. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, 80 stores selling in purity were in Kefar Imra. Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba, 80 metal <i>shidda</i><sup class="footnote-marker">319</sup><i class="footnote">A person or things transported by שִׁידָּה תֵיבָה ומִגְדָּל made of wood do not become impure if transported through impure territory (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Kelim 18:3" href="/Mishnah_Kelim.18.3">Mishnah <i>Kelim</i> 18:3</a>); according to Maimonides a box containing at least 40 <i>seah</i>, about half a cubic meter. R. Yannai denies knowledge of the exact dimensions required.</i> were in Shiḥin. Rebbi Yannai said, in our time was no <i>shidda</i>. Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Rav Ḥuna: Immer was the smallest of the watches, and it was producing 85’000 young priests.
<sup class="footnote-marker">320</sup><i class="footnote">A slightly shortened version of <i>Thr. rabba</i>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 57b" href="/Gittin.57b">Babli <i>Gittin</i> 57b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 94b" href="/Sanhedrin.94b"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 94b</a>.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, 80’000 young priests were slaughtered for the blood of Zachariah<sup class="footnote-marker">321</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 24:20-22" href="/II_Chronicles.24.20-22"><i>2Chr</i>. 24:20–22</a>. In dying he invoked God’s vengeance.</i>. Rebbi Yudan asked Rebbi Aḥa, where did they kill Zachariah? In the women’s courtyard or in Israel’s courtyard<sup class="footnote-marker">322</sup><i class="footnote">Herod’s Temple had an outer courtyard accessible to women, a middle one accessible to Israel males, and an inner one reserved uniquely for the sacrificial service by Cohanim.</i>? He said to him, neither in Israel’s courtyard nor in the women’s courtyard but in the priests’ courtyard. They treated his blood neither as ram’s blood nor as gazelle’s blood<sup class="footnote-marker">323</sup><i class="footnote">Ram’s blood has to be poured on the base of the altar; deer’s blood has to be covered as indicated in the verse.</i>. There is written, <i>he shall pour out its blood and cover it with dust</i><sup class="footnote-marker">324</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 17:13" href="/Leviticus.17.13"><i>Lev</i>. 17:13</a>.</i>. But here<sup class="footnote-marker">325</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 24:7" href="/Ezekiel.24.7"><i>Ez</i>. 24:7</a>.</i>, <i>for its blood was in its midst, on a bare rock he put it</i>. Why all this? <i>To arise rage, to avenge vengeance, I put its blood on a bare rock, without being covered</i><sup class="footnote-marker">326</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 24:8" href="/Ezekiel.24.8"><i>Ez</i>. 24:8</a>. In the verse: “impossible to cover.”</i>. Seven sins did Israel commit on that day. They killed a priest, prophet, and judge, spilled innocent blood, defiled the Temple courtyard, and it was a Sabbath and Day of Atonement. When Nebuzaraddan<sup class="footnote-marker">327</sup><i class="footnote">Sent to burn down Jerusalem after its surrender and the exile of its inhabitants.</i> came here and saw the blood bubbling, he asked them, what is the matter with this? They told him, it is the blood of bulls, sheep, and rams, which we were sacrificing on the altar. Immediately he brought bulls, rams, and sheep and slaughtered them on it, but the blood still was bubbling. Since they did not confess, he hung them on gallows. They said, since the Holy One, praise to Him, wants to ask for his blood from us, they told him, it is the blood of a priest, prophet, and judge who was prophesying for us [all that you are doing to us.] We conspired against him and killed him. Immediately he brought 80’000 young priests and slaughtered them on it, but the blood was still bubbling. At this moment he got angry with him<sup class="footnote-marker">328</sup><i class="footnote">Zachariah.</i>, and said to him, do you want to destroy your entire people because of you? Immediately the Holy One, praise to Him, was filled with mercy and said, if this one who is flesh and blood, and cruel, is filled with mercy for My children, I, where it is written about Me<sup class="footnote-marker">329</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 4:31" href="/Deuteronomy.4.31"><i>Deut</i>. 4:31</a>.</i>, <i>for a compassionate power is the Eternal, your God, He will not destroy you nor forget the covenant of your forefathers</i>, not so much more? Immediately he indicated to the blood and it was absorbed on its place.
<sup class="footnote-marker">330</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is not in <i>Thr. rabba</i>.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, 80’000 young priests fled into the hollows<sup class="footnote-marker">331</sup><i class="footnote">The word usually is used for a hollow into which a portable stove is brought for cooking.</i> of the Temple, and all of them were burned. Of all of them only Joshua ben Yehoṣadaq the High Priest was left, as it is said, <i>is he not a wooden poker saved from fire</i><sup class="footnote-marker">332</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zechariah 3:2" href="/Zechariah.3.2"><i>Zach</i>. 3:2</a>.</i>?
<sup class="footnote-marker">333</sup><i class="footnote">Similarly <i>Thr. rabba</i> 3(38), <i>Yalqut Prophets</i> 421; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 18:1-20:23" href="/Exodus.18.1-20.23"><i>Tanhuma Yitro</i> 5</a>.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, 80’000 young priests (broke through) [fled to] Nebuchadnezzar’s armies and went to the Ismaelites. They said to them, give us to drink for we are thirsty. They brought before them salted fish and inflated waterskins. They said to them, eat and then you can drink. When one of them opened the waterskin and put it into his mouth, the wind came out and suffocated him. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">334</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 21:13-15" href="/Isaiah.21.13-15"><i>Is</i>. 21:13–15</a>.</i>, <i>load in Arabia</i>, a large load on Arabia. <i>In a forest in Arabia they will stay</i>, those that should have been in the forest of Lebanon, in <i>Arabia they will stay</i>. But <i>the ways of Dedanians</i><sup class="footnote-marker">335</sup><i class="footnote">A grandson of Abraham by Qetura.</i>, that is the way the Dedanians act. When Ismael was thirsty, did they not <i>bring water towards the thirsty? God opened her eyes and she saw a water cistern</i><sup class="footnote-marker">336</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 21:19" href="/Genesis.21.19"><i>Gen</i>. 21:19</a>.</i>. Not voluntarily they came to you, <i>for they fled from swords. From the unfettered sword</i>, because they did not want to keep their Sabbaticals, as you are saying, <i>and the seventh unfetter and abandon</i><sup class="footnote-marker">337</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 23:11" href="/Exodus.23.11"><i>Ex</i>. 23:11</a>.</i>. <i>And because of</i><i>cocked bows</i>, because they did not want to keep their Sabbaths, as you are saying, <i>in these days I saw in Jehudah people pressing wine-presses on the Sabbath</i><sup class="footnote-marker">338</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 13:15" href="/Nehemiah.13.15"><i>Neh</i>. 13:15</a>.</i>. <i>And because of the difficulty of war</i>, they did not want to engage in the Torah’s war, [as you are saying], <i>therefore it was said in the book of the wars of the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">339</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 21:14" href="/Numbers.21.14"><i>Num</i>. 21:14</a>.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">340</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Thr. rabba</i> 3(38), <i>Megillah</i> 1:1 (מ).</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, from Gibbethon<sup class="footnote-marker">341</sup><i class="footnote">The full biblical name is spelled out in <i>Thr. rabba</i>.</i> to Antipatris there were 60’000 villages. The smallest among them was Bet Shemesh, about which is written<sup class="footnote-marker">342</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 6:19" href="/I_Samuel.6.19"><i>1S</i>. 6:19</a>.</i>, <i>He smote of the men of Bet Shemesh, for they looked at the Ark of the Eterna</i>, etc. These were in one direction. If you execute this with reeds it will not carry it. Rebbi Ḥanina said, the Land of Israel folded its fist.
<sup class="footnote-marker">343</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph in <i>Thr. rabba, Petiḥta</i>34.</i> Rebbi Ze`ira said, come and see how insolent is the Land of Israel, that it yields fruit<sup class="footnote-marker">344</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 29:22" href="/Deuteronomy.29.22"><i>Deut</i>. 29:22</a>) <i>sulfur and salt, burns all over its land</i>, describing the land after the destruction of the Temple, how can it have regained agricultural productivity?</i>. Why does it yield fruit? Two Amoraim. One said, because one fertilizes it. The other one said, because one turns its earth over. It happened that a person was sowing in the valley of Arbel when he dug down with his hand and brought up burning dust which burned the seeds.
<sup class="footnote-marker">345</sup><i class="footnote">From here on there exists another Genizah fragment edited by Ginzberg (G). Cf. also <i>Seder Olam</i> Chap. 27 (in the author’s edition p. 234), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 145b" href="/Shabbat.145b">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 145b</a>.</i> It was stated: Rebbi Yose says, for 52 years no bird was flying in the Land of Israel. What is the reason? <i>From the bird &lt;of the sky&gt; to the domesticated animal, they moved, they went away</i><sup class="footnote-marker">346</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 9:9" href="/Jeremiah.9.9"><i>Jer</i>. 9:9</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanina said, 40 years before Israel was exiled to Babylonia they planted date palms in Babylonia, so they should be ardent after sweets since this accustoms the tongue to Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">347</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 87b-88a" href="/Pesachim.87b-88a">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 87b/88a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanina the son of Rebbi Abbahu said, 700 kinds of pure fish and 800 kinds of pure locusts and innumerable birds all were exiled with Israel to Babylonia; and when they returned, all of them returned, except the fish called turbot. How did fish migrate? Rebbi Ḥuna (bar Joseph) &lt;in the name of rav joseph&gt;<sup class="footnote-marker">348</sup><i class="footnote">Since no R. Huna bar Joseph is otherwise known, prefer the reading of <b>&lt;g&gt;</b>.</i> said, they went into exile through the abyss end returned through the abyss.
<sup class="footnote-marker">340</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Thr. rabba</i> 3(38), <i>Megillah</i> 1:1 (מ).</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, hail to him who sees the downfall of Palmyra, for it was partner in the destruction of the first Temple and the destruction of the second Temple. In the first destruction it put up 80’000<sup class="footnote-marker">349</sup><i class="footnote">In G: 80. In <i>Thr. rabba</i> different numbers are given by different Amoraim of later generations.</i> archers and in the second destruction 8’000 archers.
“And the city was ploughed over.” Rufus<sup class="footnote-marker">350</sup><i class="footnote">Tineius Rufus, prefect of Judea at the start of Bar Kokhba’s uprising. This sentence is missing in G (and in the Midrashim.) <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29a" href="/Taanit.29a">Babli 29a</a>.</i>, may his bones be ground, ploughed over the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">By Hadrian, imitating the mythical foundation of Rome in the founding of pagan Aelia Capitolina. Described in a coin of Hadrian minted 130 C.E.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> From the start of Av one restricts happy occasions. The week in which the Ninth of Av falls one is forbidden to barber and to launder, but on Thursday one is permitted for the honor of the Sabbath.<br>In the day before the Ninth of Av a person may not eat two dishes, he may not eat meat nor drink wine<sup class="footnote-marker">378</sup><i class="footnote">He has to behave as if a close relative had died. R. Jehudah requires this in all respects, the anonymous majority only in matters of the meal preceding the fast.</i>. Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, he shall alterate. Rebbi Jehudah obligates him to turn up his couch<sup class="footnote-marker">378</sup><i class="footnote">He has to behave as if a close relative had died. R. Jehudah requires this in all respects, the anonymous majority only in matters of the meal preceding the fast.</i> but the Sages did not agree with him.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, that is a building of enjoyment. But if his wall was inclined, he tears it down and rebuilds it. Samuel said, the wall where he sleeps<sup class="footnote-marker">351</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 1:8:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.1.8.2">Chapter 1, Notes 247–248</a>.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">352</sup><i class="footnote">The following is in <i>Yom Tov</i> 5:2 (Notes 65–70), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.1.7"><i>Ketubot</i> 1:1 (Notes 34–42</a>).</i> Rebbi Abba bar Cohen said before Rebbi Yose: Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Jacob bar Idi: A man may not preliminarily marry on a Friday. That means, to make an engagement feast<sup class="footnote-marker">353</sup><i class="footnote">Since this would impinge on the Sabbath meal. It is in order to make the preliminary marriage on Friday and arrange the festive meal as Sabbath meal.</i>. This implies that the preliminary marriage itself is permitted. Samuel says, even on the Ninth of Av a preliminary marriage is permitted, lest another forestall him. The argument of Samuel seems inverted. There<sup class="footnote-marker">354</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:7" href="/Psalms.68.7"><i>Ps</i>. 68:7</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 62:10" href="/Psalms.62.10">62:10</a>. This means that marriages are pre-ordained in Heaven. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Vayikra Rabbah 29:5" href="/Vayikra_Rabbah.29.5"><i>Lev</i>. <i>rabba</i> 29(5</a>), Babli <i>Mo`ed qaṭan</i> 18b.)</i>, he says, <i>God puts singles in a house</i>; <i>To rise on scales; they all are of vapor!</i> And here, he says so<sup class="footnote-marker">355</sup><i class="footnote">If marriages are pre-ordained, why should anybody be afraid that another man could snatch the bride preselected for him? Another man might by his prayer cause the Heavenly decree to be changed, but this would lead to the early death of one of the partners of the marriage. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 2a" href="/Sotah.2a">Babli <i>Soṭa</i> 2a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 22a" href="/Sanhedrin.22a"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 22a</a>.</i>? That means, that he should not forestall him in prayer. Even so, it would not be permanent.
Rebbi Jonah said, what you are saying refers to washing to wear; but washing to mend? So we are saying, this washerman is forbidden to work in his trade<sup class="footnote-marker">356</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Mishnah only forbids people to wash their garments but not washermen to exercise their trade, there must be washing activities which are permitted. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29b" href="/Taanit.29b">Babli 29b</a> decides otherwise.</i>? Our Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Jonah, “the week in which the Ninth of Av falls one is forbidden to barber and to launder, but on Thursday<sup class="footnote-marker">357</sup><i class="footnote">If the Ninth of Av falls during the week, the following Sabbath already is after the fast and it is permitted to wash during the week in order to wear after the fast.</i> one is permitted for the honor of the Sabbath.” Rebbi Jonah in the name of Rav Hamnuna, it was repeated regarding (addition) [barbering.]<sup class="footnote-marker">358</sup><i class="footnote">The reading of the scribe is confirmed by G; the corrector’s change is indicated in <i>Or zarua</i>` §414. The corrector’s text means that barbering does not follow the rules of washing and is strictly forbidden before and during the fast. The scribe’s text seems to mean that there is no extension of the fast (following R. Simeon ben Laqish and R. Isaac ben Eleazar); immediately after the end of the fast all activities are permitted.</i> Rebbi Abba bar Cohen said before Rebbi Yose: Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Abbahu. If the Ninth of Av falls on a Sabbath, both weeks are permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">359</sup><i class="footnote">If the Ninth of Av falls on a Sabbath there is no week in which the Ninth of Av falls.</i>. What is afterwards? Rebbi Joḥanan said, afterwards is forbidden; Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, afterwards is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">360</sup><i class="footnote">A disagreement of Babylonian authorities in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29b" href="/Taanit.29b">Babli 29b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba preached it to the Sepphoreans but they did not accept it. Rebbi Immi said to Rebbi [Yasa]<sup class="footnote-marker">361</sup><i class="footnote">A necessary correction of the text of G: “R. Ammi asked R. Ammi”.</i>. Does not the nephew of the Great Rebbi Ḥiyya<sup class="footnote-marker">362</sup><i class="footnote">Rav.</i> disagree with him? He answered, they disagree explicitly: Rebbi Joḥanan said, afterwards is forbidden; Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, afterwards is permitted. How does Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish explain it<sup class="footnote-marker">363</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah which forbids the entire week if the fast was Sunday or Tuesday.</i>? He explains it if the Ninth of Av falls on a Sabbath, and one cannot infer anything. Rebbi Isaac ben Eleazar announced at the end of the Ninth of Av, the barbers shall open<sup class="footnote-marker">364</sup><i class="footnote">Their shops.</i>, any who has to eulogize may eulogize<sup class="footnote-marker">365</sup><i class="footnote">All commentators read יספר “barber” for יספר “eulogize” but this seems to be impossible in light of the evidence of G. While the rule not to eulogize on the Ninth of Av appears in the sources as Medieval Ashkenazic (<i>Šulḥan Arukh Oraḥ Ḥayyim</i> 559:10) this may be indicated here since the Ashkenazic (originally, South-Italian) order of prayers is based on the Yerushalmi.</i>. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">366</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Hosea 2:13" href="/Hosea.2.13"><i>Hos</i>. 2:13</a></i>, <i>I shall eliminate all her enjoyment, her holiday, her month, her Sabbath, and all her feast</i>. The Southerners have the custom of <i>ḥer holiday</i><sup class="footnote-marker">367</sup><i class="footnote">They start the mourning rites already on the New Moon of Av.</i>, the Sepphoreans have the custom of <i>her month</i><sup class="footnote-marker">368</sup><i class="footnote">They follow them the entire month and do not stop after the fast.</i>, the Tiberians have the custom of <i>her week</i><sup class="footnote-marker">369</sup><i class="footnote">The rule presented in the Mishnah.</i>. The Rabbis of Tiberias changed to follow the Rabbis of Sepphoris.
<sup class="footnote-marker">370</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph also appears in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Megillah 1:4:2-14" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Megillah.1.4.2-14"><i>Megillah</i>1:6</a> (מ).</i> Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ḥiyya, it should have been logical that one should fast on the Tenth, since on it our God’s Temple was burned. Why on the Ninth? Because the calamity started on it<sup class="footnote-marker">371</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 25:8" href="/II_Kings.25.8"><i>2K</i>. 25:8</a>.</i>. So it was stated, on the Seventh they entered, on the Eighth they were misbehaving in it, on the Ninth they started the fire, and on the Tenth it was burned<sup class="footnote-marker">372</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29a" href="/Taanit.29a">Babli 29a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Taanit (Lieberman) 3:10" href="/Tosefta_Taanit_(Lieberman).3.10">Tosephta 3:10</a>.</i>. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi fasted Ninth and Tenth. Rebbi Abun fasted Ninth and Tenth. Rebbi Levi fasted on the Ninth and the night of the Tenth. Rebbi Abba bar Zavda in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: Rebbi wanted to uproot the Ninth of Av but they did not let him<sup class="footnote-marker">373</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Megillah 5b" href="/Megillah.5b">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 5b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar said to him, I was with you but it was not said so, but Rebbi wanted to uproot the Ninth of Av which fell on a Sabbath but they did not let him. He said, because it was pushed aside, let it be pushed aside. They said to him, let it be pushed to the next day. In a similar case, that which we stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">374</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 6:6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.6.6.1">Mishnah <i>Yebamot</i> 6:6</a>.</i>: “Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa said, for both of them it says, <i>God blessed them and God said to them, be fruitful and multiply</i><sup class="footnote-marker">375</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 1:28" href="/Genesis.1.28"><i>Gen</i>. 1:28</a>.</i>, etc.” Rebbi Eleazar in the Name of Rebbi Ḥanina: Practice follows Rebbi Joḥanan ben Beroqa. Rebbi Abba bar Zavda said to him, I was with you and it was only said, if she asks to be married the law is on her side<sup class="footnote-marker">376</sup><i class="footnote">If a woman is married childless for ten years she may ask the court to force her husband to give her a divorce with full payment of her <i>ketubah</i>. In her application to the court she must state that her request is in order to be able to marry another man (who implicitly is supposed to be more fertile than the first.) In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 65b" href="/Yevamot.65b">Babli <i>Yebamot</i> 65b</a> she is required to state explicitly that she wants to marry another man in order to have children who will be able to care for her in her old age.</i>. He said about them, <i>two are better than one</i><sup class="footnote-marker">377</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 4:9" href="/Ecclesiastes.4.9"><i>Eccl</i>. 4:9</a>.</i>.
What means “he shall alterate”? He shall change. If he is used to eat a pound<sup class="footnote-marker">379</sup><i class="footnote">A Roman pound of 12 unciae, 345g.</i> of meat he shall eat half; if he is used to drink a sextarius<sup class="footnote-marker">380</sup><i class="footnote">Possibly Greek ξέστης; in both Talmudim the equivalent of a <i>log</i> (.53 l) but in the Galilean Targumim the equivalent of a hin, 12 <i>log</i> (6.5 l). <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30a" href="/Taanit.30a">Babli 30a</a>.</i> of wine he shall drink half. Rebbi Joḥanan said, but only for the main meal of the Ninth of Av. Rav<sup class="footnote-marker">381</sup><i class="footnote">In G: Rebbi. In the Babli, Rav Jehudah.</i> Hoshaia said, and only in the afternoon. Rebbi Yose says, both statements are for leniency. If he ate the main meal of the Ninth of Av before noon, even if he brings on his table like Salomon’s meal it is permitted. If he ate his meal<sup class="footnote-marker">382</sup><i class="footnote">Intending to eat another later in the afternoon.</i> in the afternoon, even if he brings on his table like Salomon’s meal in his time<sup class="footnote-marker">383</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 5:2-3" href="/I_Kings.5.2-3"><i>1K</i>. 5:2–3</a>.</i> it is permitted. It was stated: If the Ninth of Av fell on a Friday or the day before the Ninth of Av on a Sabbath, even if he brings on his table like Salomon’s meal in his time it is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">384</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 29b" href="/Taanit.29b">Babli 29b</a>.</i>. Rav after he had eaten his fill was coloring his piece of bread with ashes and said, this is the main meal of the Ninth of Av, to keep what is said<sup class="footnote-marker">385</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 3:16" href="/Lamentations.3.16"><i>Thr</i>. 3:16</a>. Mentioned in <i>Thr. rabba ad loc</i>.</i>, <i>He filled me with asperity, made me imbue poison</i>.
Rebbi Jehudah says it correctly; what is the Rabbis’ reason? They made him like one whose deceased is lying before him<sup class="footnote-marker">386</sup><i class="footnote">As long as a person is occupied with arranging a burial, the formal rules of mourning do not apply to him. Since the mourner is not supposed to leave his house but the person who fasts on a public fast day is supposed to leave his house, no public fast can imitate the rules of formal mourning.</i>; he neither overturns his couch nor sleeps on an overturned couch.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel said, Israel had no holidays like the Fifteenth of Av and the Day of Atonement, when the people of Jerusalem went out in borrowed white garments, not to embarrass those who had none. All garments need immersion<sup class="footnote-marker">387</sup><i class="footnote">So that all were pure. In this version, also the men who were looking for a bride had to appear in a plane white kaftan.</i>. The daughters of Jerusalem went out and played flutes<sup class="footnote-marker">388</sup><i class="footnote">Usually one translates “dance” but it is impossible to dance in a tightly planted vineyard. On the other hand one may not play musical instruments on the Day of Atonement. Therefore it seems that the correct wording is in Maimonides’s autograph Mishnah: חונות “stay”.</i> in the vineyards.<br>What were they saying? Young man, lift your eyes and see what you are choosing for yourself. Do not fix your eye on beauty, fix your eyes on the extraction<sup class="footnote-marker">389</sup><i class="footnote">The text in the Babli and the independent Mishnah mss. is much longer, confirmed by Maimonides’s autograph.</i>. And so it says<sup class="footnote-marker">390</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Song of Songs 3:11" href="/Song_of_Songs.3.11"><i>Cant</i>. 3:11</a>. In the allegorical interpretation of the Song of Songs, any “Solomon” refers to the King of Peace.</i>, <i>Daughters of Zion go out and see king Solomon</i><sup class="footnote-marker">391</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>.</i>, etc. <i>The day of His enjoyment</i><sup class="footnote-marker">391</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>.</i> is the giving of the Torah; <i>and the day of His heart’s joy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">391</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>.</i> is the building of His Temple which may be built soon in our days.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">391</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>.</i> One understands the Day of Atonement which is atonement for all of Israel. <sup class="footnote-marker">392</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 31a" href="/Taanit.31a">31a</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Batra 121a" href="/Bava_Batra.121a"><i>Bava batra</i> 121a</a>.</i> Why on the Fifteenth of Av? Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Yasa: For this is the good time to cut wood, because any wood cut on this day does not develop worms; as we have stated there, “any wood containing a worm is disqualified from the altar.<sup class="footnote-marker">393</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 2:5" href="/Mishnah_Middot.2.5"><i>Mishnah Middot</i> 2:5</a>. In the Babli the reason is given that this is the last day on which wood for the altar may be cut before the rainy season.</i>” Rav Ḥiyya bar Ashi in the name of Rav, because on it Hoshea ben Ela abolished the guards which Jeroboam ben Nabath posted on the roads<sup class="footnote-marker">394</sup><i class="footnote">To prohibit pilgrimages to Jerusalem.</i>. Cahana asked [Rav]. He did all this good deed and it is written about him<sup class="footnote-marker">395</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Kings 17:3" href="/II_Kings.17.3"><i>2K</i>. 17:3</a>.</i>, <i>against him came Salmanessar the king of Assyria</i>? He answered him, because he removed the collar from his neck and hung it on the community’s neck. He did not say, all the people should go on pilgrimage, but, any one who wants to go may go. Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac, but some say in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman: On it the tribes were permitted to intermarry. As it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">396</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 36:7" href="/Numbers.36.7"><i>Num</i>. 36:7</a>.</i>, <i>family heritage should not be transferred from tribe to tribe; but the Children of Israel shall stick everyone to the family heritage of his forefathers</i>, etc. And it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">397</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 36:8" href="/Numbers.36.8"><i>Num</i>. 36:8</a>.</i>, <i>any daughter inheriting family heritage in the tribes of the Children of Israel</i>, etc. How is it possible for a daughter to inherit from two tribes? Explain it if her father was from one tribe and her mother from another tribe<sup class="footnote-marker">398</sup><i class="footnote">According to the Babli, a later generation read <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 36" href="/Numbers.36"><i>Num</i>. 36</a> to apply only to the daughters of Salpaad and their contemporaries.</i>. But the Rabbis say, on it the tribe of Benjamin was permitted to intermarry, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">399</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Judges 21:18" href="/Judges.21.18"><i>Jud</i>. 21:18</a>.</i>, <i>cursed be he who gives a wife to Benjamin</i>. They read a verse and included him; they read a verse and excluded him. They read a verse and included him<sup class="footnote-marker">400</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 48:5" href="/Genesis.48.5"><i>Gen</i>. 48:5</a>.</i>, <i>Ephraim and Manasse shall be to me like Reuben and Simeon</i>. They read a verse and excluded him, <i>a people and community of peoples shall be from you and kings will come from your loins</i><sup class="footnote-marker">401</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 35:11" href="/Genesis.35.11"><i>Gen</i>. 35:11</a>.<br>In the explanations, the terms “included” and “excluded” have to be switched. The text follows the usual pattern, that if possibilities A and B are raised, B is explained before A. Since the number 12 of tribe cannot be changed, either Joseph is counted as one tribe and Benjamin is included (35:11), or Ephraim and Manasse are counted as full tribes, there seems to be no place for Benjamin. This logic is not followed by the Babli.</i>, and Benjamin was not yet born. <sup class="footnote-marker">402</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Thr. rabba, Introduction</i> (33).</i> Rebbi Abun said, digging stopped on it, as Rebbi Levi said, on every eve of the Ninth of Av, Moses had a declaration published in all the encampment and said, go out for digging, go out for digging. They went out, dug graves for themselves, and slept. In the morning they were getting up and found themselves missing 15’000 and detail<sup class="footnote-marker">403</sup><i class="footnote">If always the same number died on the Ninth of Av and nobody during the year, the number would be 600’000:38 = 15’789.47.</i>. In the last year they did that, got up, and found themselves whole. They said, maybe we erred in the computation. The same on the Tenth, the Eleventh, the Twelfth, the Thirteenth, and the Fifteenth. Since the moon was full they said, it seems that The Holy One, praise to Him, vacated this hard judgment against us. They got up and made a holiday.
“All garments need immersion. The daughters of Jerusalem went out and played flutes in the vineyards.” Rebbi Yannai ben Rebbi Ismael said, even if put in a box<sup class="footnote-marker">404</sup><i class="footnote">He required that all plain white garments had to be immersed in a <i>miqweh</i> even if it was obvious that they were pure and there was no intention to use them.</i>. Put in a box and you are saying so? Because you are doing that, he will lend them.
“What were they saying? Young man, lift your eyes and see what you are choosing for yourself. Do not fix your eye on beauty, fix you eyes on the extraction, etc.” If she was the king’s daughter she was borrowing from the High Priest’s daughter; the High Priest’s daughter was borrowing from the king’s daughter<sup class="footnote-marker">405</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 31a" href="/Taanit.31a">Babli 31a</a>.</i>. The ugly ones did say, “do not fix your eye on beauty<sup class="footnote-marker">406</sup><i class="footnote">The corrector’s spelling follows the (Babylonian) consensus, the spelling in both Yerushalmi texts is the etymologically correct one.</i>,” and the beautiful ones did say, “fix you eyes on the extraction.” “And so it says<sup class="footnote-marker">390</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Song of Songs 3:11" href="/Song_of_Songs.3.11"><i>Cant</i>. 3:11</a>. In the allegorical interpretation of the Song of Songs, any “Solomon” refers to the King of Peace.</i>, <i>Daughters of Zion go out and see king Solomon</i><sup class="footnote-marker">391</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 30b" href="/Taanit.30b">Babli 30b</a>.</i>, <i>with the crown with which his mother crowned him on the day of his marriage and the day of his heart’s joy. The day of His enjoyment</i> is the giving of the Torah; <i>and the day of His heart’s joy</i> is the building of His Temple which may be built soon in our days.”
